# Verifiable Wallet-State Snapshot — Design (roll-up)

**Branch:** `fix/verifiable-snapshot-v2` (was `feature/verifiable-snapshot`) · **Date:** 2026-07-22 · **Status:** v7 — revised after a sixth adversarial design-council review round (split-but-convergent verdict: Opus called v6 sound-with-minor-gaps, characterizing the local-store-restore beacon as a scoping overclaim; Fable 5 and GPT-5.6 Sol both independently found, via an identical concrete counterexample, that the beacon was not merely narrower than claimed but STRUCTURALLY BROKEN — a static, never-updated `storeInstanceId` cannot detect a restore that regresses `localCounter` while the untouched beacon still shows the same ID; GPT-5.6 Sol additionally found the round-6 manifest-authentication fix introduced two new bugs — a privacy-correlation leak and a key-rotation break — on top of not fixing the beacon) — this round redesigns the beacon around a genuinely evolving, mirrored counter with a full crash-safe write protocol and state machine, replaces the chain-facing `manifestHash` witness with a small re-encryption-invariant, low-entropy `formatMetadataCommit` folded into the existing hiding commitment (closing the privacy leak and the key-rotation break together), completes the KDF/bootstrap metadata spec with canonical length-delimited encoding, specifies a real historical-restore mechanism using the `history` tree's own inclusion-proof capability, finalizes the padding scheme byte-exactly, closes the remaining `dbSeq`-as-monotonicity-signal stragglers, and corrects the collision-probability figure to its exact value. Ready for a seventh review pass before implementation begins.
**Author role:** Design Lead, synthesizing research briefs 01–11 (`design/research/2026-07-21-snapshot-root-of-trust/`) plus the v2, v3, v4, v5, v6, and v7 fixes below.

This document is **decisive** — it recommends one v1 design and states what is deferred — but it flags, in §12, the genuinely open decisions the council must ratify before any implementation begins. Every load-bearing choice is grounded in a brief (cited `[NN]`) and, where the mechanism lives in Midnight, a `repo/path:line`.

---

## Revision history — v7

Round 6 of design-council review came back **split-but-convergent**: **Opus** judged v6 sound with only minor gaps, characterizing the local-store-restore beacon (§7.3.1) as narrower in scope than claimed, not broken; **Fable 5** and **GPT-5.6 Sol**, independently, constructed the *identical* concrete counterexample and both concluded the beacon is **structurally broken**, not merely narrow — it fails on this design's own primary motivating scenario (iOS app reinstall after data loss); **GPT-5.6 Sol** additionally found that round 6's own manifest-authentication fix (Priority 3 of that round) introduced two new defects on top of not fixing the beacon. This revision closes all of it with real mechanism redesign, traced through the same counterexamples the auditors used. Summary:

0. **(CRITICAL, 2/3 convergent via an identical concrete counterexample — the liveness beacon does not detect the counterexample it was built to catch.)** v6's beacon compared a `storeInstanceId` generated **once**, at store-creation time, and never rotated or updated afterward. Concrete counterexample (constructed independently by Fable 5 and GPT-5.6 Sol): primary store and beacon both hold ID `X` at T0 (`localCounter = 100`); the device continues saving, reaching `localCounter = 250`; the primary store is restored from the T0 backup (still ID `X`, `localCounter = 100`); the beacon — untouched by the restore, by construction — **also** still holds `X`, because v6's beacon never recorded anything about the device's subsequent progress, only its identity. The "IDs match → continuous state, proceed normally" branch fires; the very next save reserves `localCounter = 101`, a value already consumed by a genuine ciphertext chunk 150 saves earlier under the same `deviceId`/key — deterministic AES-GCM nonce reuse, exactly the failure this construction exists to prevent, and undetected by v6's check. This is not an edge case: it fires on the design's own headline example (Keychain data survives an iOS reinstall; the app's primary local-store file usually does not). **Fixed, structurally, not by re-tuning the same mechanism:** the beacon now mirrors the *evolving* `localCounter` value itself, updated on every reservation, and the startup/reservation check becomes "primary's `localCounter` must be ≥ beacon's mirrored counter" rather than "IDs match" — a mismatch (primary behind beacon) is the fresh-store-redraw signal. A full crash-safe dual-write protocol (write-primary-then-beacon, with an explicit, provably-safe reconciliation rule for the interrupted case), a MUST-abort rule extended to beacon-write failure, the five state-machine cases (including the two v6 left unspecified: primary-absent-beacon-present, and primary-at-counter-0 with a mismatched/absent beacon), and an explicit fail-closed rule for platforms with no reliable backup-excluded primitive at all are all specified below (§7.3.1). The desktop "marker file outside backup directories" gap (does not survive a full-disk-image restore) is closed where a TPM/Secure-Enclave/hardware-Keystore-backed sealing primitive is available, and named as an explicit, narrower residual (same-machine-same-TPM disk-image restore only) where it is not; AES-GCM-SIV is recommended as a named, not-built-for-v1 defense-in-depth fallback specifically for that residual. See §7.3.1's rewritten local-store-restore subsection and revised §12 D11.
1. **(HIGH, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — round 6's own manifest-authentication fix created a privacy-correlation leak.)** Making the extended `manifestHash` (covering ciphertext chunk hashes plus `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion`/`manifestSectionChunkCount`) a disclosed witness inside the public, on-chain-verifiable `attestLeaf` let a hosted DB — which already holds the ciphertext manifest — recompute the identical hash locally and correlate its own stored blob to the wallet's on-chain pseudonymous identity, since a chunk-hash-covering hash is an effectively unique fingerprint. This directly contradicted this same document's own §3 text (the `persistentCommit(snapshotRoot, salt)` hiding construction exists specifically so "a hosted DB cannot even *identify* whose snapshot it holds," brief 05 §7). **Fixed together with item 2 below** (they are the same mechanism): the ciphertext-covering `manifestHash` is removed from `attestLeaf`/`AttestRecord` entirely, restoring the original, pre-round-6 rule that it is never chain-facing; the two format-dispatch fields that genuinely need chain-facing tamper-evidence are folded *inside* the existing `persistentCommit` hiding construction instead, at negligible entropy cost. See §2.5.2/§2.5.3/§7.3.1/§8 and revised §12 D13.
2. **(HIGH, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — the same fix bound ciphertext-dependent metadata into the chain-facing leaf, breaking key rotation, contradicting this document's own earlier, still-present text.)** §2.5.2 has said since v2 that "a key rotation changes `manifestHash` but by construction cannot change `snapshotRoot`, so it never invalidates a prior attestation" (line still present, unchanged, in this same document) — and §2.5.1/§7.3 both state `manifestHash` "has no chain-facing meaning and must not be substituted for `snapshotRoot` in any restore-time equality check, attestation, or `AttestRecord`." Round 6's fix violated both: it put a chunk-hash-covering (hence re-encryption-*variant*) `manifestHash` directly into the chain-facing `attestLeaf`, so any future re-encryption of an already-attested checkpoint (which changes ciphertext, hence chunk hashes, hence `manifestHash`) would make the historically-attested `commitment`/`attestLeaf` unreconstructable — and the contract has no same-height replacement mechanism, only strictly-increasing `height`. **Fixed by re-deriving what actually needs chain-facing tamper-evidence from first principles (§7.3.1's new "self-detecting vs. needs-explicit-protection" analysis):** of the four round-6 fields, `encKdfVersion` and `manifestSectionChunkCount` are already self-detecting — tampering either one causes the wrong key or the wrong per-chunk AAD to be used, which AES-GCM's own authentication tag catches on the very next decrypt attempt, with no additional mechanism needed. Only `envelopeVersion` and `encodingVersion` are true decode-dispatch fields with no other authentication path, and both are genuinely re-encryption-invariant (same plaintext, same format tags, regardless of which key/device/epoch re-encrypts the ciphertext). These two, and only these two, are folded into a small, low-entropy `formatMetadataCommit` inside the existing hiding `persistentCommit(...)` construction — never the full, ciphertext-chunk-hash-covering `manifestHash`, which reverts to local-only (Domain S, never chain-facing), exactly as originally specified before round 6. This closes the key-rotation break (the folded fields never change under re-encryption, so `commitment` is invariant under it, matching the pre-round-6 invariant) and item 1's privacy leak (the folded value has only a handful of possible values across an entire user base, so it carries negligible fingerprinting power, unlike a chunk-hash-covering hash) **simultaneously, by the same fix** — traced through concretely below. See §2.5.2/§2.5.3/§7.3.1/§8 and revised §12 D13.
3. **(HIGH — KDF/bootstrap metadata incomplete for real interoperability, named but not previously closed.)** `deviceId` and the random HKDF salt are both required inputs to decrypt any checkpoint but neither previously appeared in `ManifestMetadata` or any authenticated header equation. **Fixed:** both are added explicitly to `ManifestMetadata` (§7.3.1 point 1); the salt's lifetime is pinned unambiguously — **one salt per `(walletId, networkId)` pair**, generated once and carried in every manifest (not per-checkpoint, not local-store-only, so any device holding the wallet seed can re-derive `key_device` for any `deviceId` it observes without needing that device's own local state); and the `walletId‖networkId‖scope‖deviceId` HKDF `info` concatenation, the header-hash equation, and the AAD tuple are all respecified with explicit fixed-width, length-delimited, big-endian-byte-order encoding so two independent implementations produce byte-identical results. See §7.3.1 point 1/4.
4. **(HIGH — the advertised point-in-time historical restore did not actually exist, named but not previously closed.)** §3's text has said since v2 that the `history` Merkle tree "turns *intentional* point-in-time restore into a verifiable first-class op" — but no restore code path ever fetched anything but the *latest* `attestations[id]` record, and the `history` tree, despite being hashed into `history.insertHash(...)` on every attestation, was never actually consumed as a restore proof anywhere. **Fixed by option (a) — the real mechanism is specified, not deferred:** a new indexer capability indexes every `history` insertion by position and by wallet `id`; a new `fetchHistoricalAttestation(id, targetHeight)` retrieval returns the historical `AttestRecord` plus a genuine Merkle inclusion proof against the `history` tree's root (read via the same GRANDPA-justified `state_getReadProof` discipline §4 already uses, not a new primitive — inclusion proofs are ordinary Merkle-tree functionality, unlike the harder non-membership gap already named for nullifiers/absent attestations); a new `restoreAtHistoricalCheckpoint()` reuses the existing L0/L1/L3 machinery against the retrieved, chain-verified historical record. See new §3.6.2 and new §12 D15.
5. **(MEDIUM — padding scheme not byte-exact, named but not previously closed.)** The "round to next power of two" rule and the "1–2, 3–4, 5–8" bucket examples were only reconcilable by inference; `trueLength`'s relationship to its own encoding, the padding byte value, canonical-padding validation, empty/maximum-section handling, and a chunk-count sanity bound were all unspecified. **Fixed:** an explicit minimum bucket size of 2 chunks (resolving the apparent conflict — 1 rounds up to 2, not down to itself), `trueLength` excludes its own field's bytes, zero-byte (`0x00`) padding with mandatory canonical-padding validation on decode, an explicit empty-section rule (still padded to the 2-chunk minimum, never zero chunks), a `2³² byte` per-section maximum, and an explicit `chunkCount < 2³²` bound. See §2.5.4/§7.3.1 point 6.
6. **(MEDIUM — five remaining stale `dbSeq`/`seq`-as-monotonicity instances, named but not previously fully closed.)** A further grep sweep (this round's own, on top of v4/v5/v6's equivalent passes) found: the architecture-diagram L2 box still read "local monotonic seq" for anti-rollback; the §2 L2 "Anti-rollback / freshness" bullet still described "a strictly-increasing `seq` + `anchorHeight`" as the mechanism protecting a running wallet; §10 residual item 12 still allowed "`height` (or, redundantly, the contract-internal `attestOrdinal`)" as an alternate freshness signal despite this document elsewhere stating height is *sole*; §11.1's L2 anti-rollback property test still asserted rejection keyed on "`seq`/height," which — per the traced §12 D14 Device A/B race — would wrongly reject Device A's legitimate, freshest attestation; and §3.6.1's own heading and opening paragraph still used bare, un-disambiguated `seq` language predating the `dbSeq`/`attestOrdinal` split it documents. All five fixed in place; see the corresponding sections below.
7. **(MINOR — the birthday-bound approximation was stated without its exact value, a third instance of this document's own previously-flagged false-precision pattern.)** §7.3.1's `D²/(2·2¹²⁸)` figure (`≈5.8775×10⁻³⁷`) is the simpler, conservative approximation; the exact birthday-bound value, `1 − ∏ᵢ₌₀¹⁹(1 − i/2¹²⁸) ≈ D(D−1)/(2·2¹²⁸) ≈ 5.5836×10⁻³⁷`, is now stated alongside it — the discrepancy (~5.26%) is exactly the `D²` vs. `D(D−1)` numerator difference. The simpler formula is kept for readability, explicitly labeled as a conservative upper bound, not a false-precision restatement.

Section numbers below mostly match v1–v6 to keep prior review comments addressable; v7 material is inserted in place within existing subsections (flagged inline), with §7.3.1's local-store-restore subsection substantially rewritten, §2.5.2/§2.5.3/§8's canonical equation revised again, and new §3.6.2 added (flagged at their headers).

---

## Revision history — v6

Round 5 of design-council review came back **split**: **Opus** judged v5 sound with only minor gaps, not blocking; **Fable 5** and **GPT-5.6 Sol** both said **NEEDS ROUND 6**, with GPT-5.6 Sol — the reviewer whose findings have been independently re-verified against source the most often across this whole process — finding the most severe and broadest remaining issues, and all three of its own internal review personas returning **BLOCK**. This revision closes all of it with structural changes, verified where checkable, not with corrected numbers alone. Summary:

0. **(CRITICAL, Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, independently computed and converging — the nonce probability claim in v5 was not merely imprecise, it was backwards.)** v5's §7.3.1 computed `P(deviceId collision) ≈ 4.66×10⁻⁸` for a realistic 20-device wallet lifetime and asserted this "comfortably clears NIST's ≤2⁻³² collision-probability guidance." **Recomputed and confirmed this session:** `4.66×10⁻⁸ ÷ 2⁻³² (≈2.33×10⁻¹⁰) ≈ 200` — the v5 construction's own collision probability is **~200× above (worse than)** the bound it claimed to clear, not under it. The v5 text's *arithmetic* (the 4.66×10⁻⁸ figure itself) was correct; its *conclusion* was the opposite of what that number means. Separately, v5's claim that requiring matching `localCounter` values "narrows the probability further" was also wrong: two devices sharing a `deviceId` both start `localCounter` at the same value and increment in lockstep from their first save, so a `deviceId` collision does not merely raise the *chance* of an eventual nonce collision — it produces one on the very first save both devices make under that shared `deviceId`, deterministically. **Fixed, structurally, not by re-tuning the same construction (Priority 1 below):** nonce material is restructured so `deviceId` is bound into **key derivation** (HKDF `info` context) rather than relied on purely as nonce-space partitioning, so that even the (now separately closed) residual `deviceId`-collision case cannot silently degrade into catastrophic nonce reuse under a *shared* key the way v5's construction could. `deviceId` is also widened from 32 to 128 bits. The corrected math is derived in full in §7.3.1 and restated in §12 D11 (v6).
1. **(CRITICAL, Opus + Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, 3/3 convergence — local-store restore-from-backup causes deterministic nonce reuse.)** A routine OS/cloud backup restore of a device's trusted local store preserves `deviceId` but can regress `localCounter` to an earlier, already-used value — every prior chunk encrypted since that earlier point gets its nonce reissued deterministically on the very next save. v5 named this gap without specifying a defense. **Fixed:** a concrete backup-restore detection mechanism (a backup-excluded "liveness beacon," §7.3.1) redraws a fresh `deviceId` (and resets `localCounter`) whenever the primary trusted store's own consistency marker doesn't match the beacon's — the only state a genuine OS/cloud backup restore cannot silently carry forward together with the primary store. Also fixed, as part of the same restructure: fsync failure is now specified as a hard, MUST-abort condition on the encrypt/save path; a concrete atomic counter-reservation protocol (advisory exclusive lock around durable increment-and-fsync) is specified for concurrent same-device saves; and counter exhaustion gets an explicit, mandatory fail-closed/rekey rule (not merely an informal "13.6 years" estimate). New negative tests cover both the restore/rollback scenario and concurrent-save contention (§11).
2. **(HIGH, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — v5's own tail-verification fix introduced a mixed-time wallet state.)** v5's restore sketch built the returned wallet from `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }` — checkpoint-N-scoped everywhere except a tip-advanced frontier — inconsistent with the design's normal `[N, tip]` live-resume path, which assumes the wallet starts *fully* at N and catches up from there. **Fixed by discarding `advancedFrontier`** (option (a) of the two offered — see §7.1(b) for the full justification): `verifyTailComplete` becomes purely a validation check (it confirms the tail is complete, then its working copy is thrown away); the wallet `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` returns is fully N-scoped, built from `sections` directly, and proceeds through the *same* `[N, tip]` catch-up every restore already uses, rather than a special-cased tip-advanced substitution. Also fixed: `treeFrontierAtN`'s "never mutated" claim is now structurally enforced (a defensive-copy-on-read accessor, not a bare `Uint8Array` passed by reference and a `Schema.Uint8Array` convention alone — JS/TS `Object.freeze()` does **not** prevent writes to a typed array's indexed elements, so the previous "never mutated" claim had no actual enforcement mechanism behind it). See §7.1(a)/(b) and new §12 D10 (revised).
3. **(HIGH, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — no real manifest authentication existed.)** Moving `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion` to unencrypted per-manifest metadata (v5) was the right structural move but left them genuinely unauthenticated — `manifestHash` never covered them. **Fixed:** `manifestHash` is extended to cover these fields (plus a new explicit `manifestSectionChunkCount` field, closing the separate "where does `manifestSectionPlain` end" gap) and is itself folded into `attestLeaf` as a new disclosed witness (§2.5.3, §8) — the same pattern used for `dbSeq` in v5 — making tampering any of these fields a chain-detectable L3 failure for anchored (v2) restores, not merely a local corruption signal. Also fixed: a concrete padding scheme (round each section up to the next power-of-two chunk-count bucket before chunking) is specified to close the section-boundary/size privacy leak, chosen over disclosing it as accepted residual because owned-note/nullifier counts are financially sensitive and the fix is cheap. See §7.3.1, §2.5.3, §8, and new §12 D13.
4. **(HIGH, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — `dbSeq` was never actually enforced as monotonic on-chain, and other logic silently assumed it was.)** The attestation contract enforces increasing `height` only; several places in the v5 text (the §3.6 pre-spend/periodic recheck, `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`'s local high-water-mark check) nonetheless compared `dbSeq` values as though `dbSeq` carried the same monotonicity guarantee `height` does. It does not: `dbSeq` reflects `CheckpointStore` save order, which can legitimately diverge from attestation-arrival order across devices with different attestation latency, letting a perfectly honest, height-increasing attestation land with a *lower* `dbSeq` than one it supersedes. **Fixed by option (b):** `dbSeq` is stripped of any monotonicity role everywhere it had one and used strictly as a storage locator (unchanged for that purpose); `height` (already contract-CAS-enforced) becomes the sole anti-rollback high-water-mark signal, both in `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`'s local check and in §3.6's divergence condition. Traced through the concrete Device A/B race in §7.1(b) and §12 D14 to confirm the fix actually resolves it, including what happens to a genuinely-CAS-rejected ("loser") attestation, which was already specified in §3.6.1 and needed no change.
5. **Five further stale/contradictory text instances found and fixed (GPT-5.6 Sol).** (i) §3's salt-derivation prose still read `(sk_attest, seq)`, predating the v5 `dbSeq`/`attestOrdinal` split — updated to `(sk_attest, attestOrdinal)`, matching §2.5.3/§8's actual construction. (ii) §7.1(a) twice reinstated the superseded shared/lockstep `seq` invariant and separately claimed no `CheckpointStore`/`PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()` interface change was needed — directly contradicting §3.6.1/§10 item 11's own (correct) finding, in the same document, that a load()-signature change is a required, blocking companion fix. Both corrected; the superseded lockstep-invariant paragraph is removed and replaced with a forward reference to §2.5.3/§3.6.1's actual mechanism. (iii) §7.3's `CheckpointStore` paragraph still referenced "§2.5.3's `seq` field" — updated to `dbSeq`. (iv) §11.1's L0-scope test claimed owned-notes-base tampering is "caught only once L1 + local trial-decryption run" — this contradicts the design's own established residual (§2.5.5/§10 item 4: the *base* owned-note set at N is attest-time-honesty-only; only notes added *after* N are independently re-derived by live trial-decryption). Corrected to state the tampering is caught by the L3 commitment-equality check when an attestation exists to compare against, and is *not* caught by L1 or trial-decryption at all otherwise — matching the residual as already scoped. (v) §11.2's AES-GCM AAD-tampering test still listed "wrong `encKdfVersion`" as an AAD-tampering case, even though `encKdfVersion` was moved *out* of per-chunk AAD in this same v5 revision line — corrected to test `encKdfVersion` tampering via the new manifest-header authentication (Priority 3), not AAD. A full grep sweep for other stale `seq`-only references across §§2–12 found no further instances beyond the ones already itemized in v4/v5's own equivalent sweeps.

Section numbers below mostly match v1–v5 to keep prior review comments addressable; v6 material is inserted in place within existing subsections (flagged inline), with §7.1(b) (wallet-construction data flow), §7.3.1 (nonce construction, manifest authentication), and §2.5.3/§8 (attestLeaf equation, again) substantially rewritten (flagged at their headers).

---

## Revision history — v5

Round 4 of design-council review came back **2-of-3**: **Fable 5** re-confirmed the core owned-notes defect genuinely closed but flagged the v4 nonce fix as vulnerable to a hostile DB replaying `nextval()`; **Opus** judged v4 fully closed, no round-5 needed; **GPT-5.6 Sol** (the most consistently rigorous reviewer across this whole process) said **NEEDS ROUND 5** and found the situation strictly worse than Fable 5's framing: a real, honest-Postgres crash-recovery counterexample requiring no hostile behavior at all, plus a genuinely new defect neither other reviewer caught — `verifyTailComplete` mutating `sections.treeFrontier` in place *before* `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` ran, silently breaking the "unmodified sections flow" both other reviewers had verified for any restore with a non-empty tail. This revision closes all four findings with structural mechanism changes, not caveats:

1. **(CRITICAL, GPT-5.6 Sol, new — the sections-mutation defect.) `verifyTailComplete` mutated the exact object `computeSnapshotRoot` reads, before that read happened, silently breaking every legitimate non-empty-tail restore.** v4's §7.1(b) called `verifyTailComplete(sections.treeFrontier, ...)` — described in v4's own text as mutating `sections.treeFrontier` "to reflect the tip" — *before* `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` ran a few lines later. But the on-chain `commitment` authenticates `snapshotRoot` as of **checkpoint N**, not the tip; for any restore where `[N, tip]` is non-empty, the root computed after L1 ran would hash the **tip**-advanced frontier, which cannot equal the checkpoint-N commitment for a perfectly honest restore. This was a correctness bug that v4's own trace-through (§12's "fifth-order risk" paragraph) should have caught and didn't — nobody actually traced a non-empty-tail restore end to end. **Fixed:** §7.1(a)'s schema field is renamed `treeFrontier` → `treeFrontierAtN` and is now **never mutated, by anything, at any point** in `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`. `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` always reads `sections.treeFrontierAtN` exactly as decoded from the envelope. `verifyTailComplete` no longer takes or mutates `sections` at all — it takes `sections.treeFrontierAtN` **by value**, applies the collapsed update to a **locally-derived copy**, checks that copy rehashes to the tip root, and **returns** the advanced copy as a new value (`advancedFrontier`) rather than writing it back into `sections`. The wallet returned by `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` is built from a **new object** — `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }` — never from mutated `sections` itself. Traced through a concrete non-empty-tail restore below (§7.1(b)); see also new §12 D10.
2. **(CRITICAL, Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, converged from two angles — the v4 nonce fix still didn't establish "never reissued, forever.") The `ckpt_nonce_ctr` Postgres `SEQUENCE` fix (v4) does not survive either a hostile DB (Fable 5: the DB is this design's own named adversary; a malicious operator can simply replay a `nextval()` result or run `setval()`) or an honest one (GPT-5.6 Sol, with a citation: PostgreSQL's own documentation warns sequence state can be uncertain after a crash before the sequence advancement is durably flushed — an honest, non-malicious Postgres can re-issue a previously-allocated `nonceBase` after an ungraceful crash/restart, no adversary required).** **Fixed by removing the DB from the nonce-material trust path entirely — nonce material is now fully client-side, per Fable 5's suggested direction.** §7.3.1 is rewritten around a device-random-prefix + durable-local-monotonic-counter hybrid (option (b) extended with a standard per-device randomness component so concurrent multi-device writers never need to coordinate), stored and durably fsynced in the same trusted local store this design already assumes for the L2 anti-rollback high-water mark — never transmitted to, or trusted from, the DB in either direction. `ckpt_nonce_ctr` (the Postgres `SEQUENCE`) is removed from the design entirely. Concrete birthday-bound math for the chosen construction, and a trace through GPT-5.6 Sol's exact honest-crash-then-restart scenario, are both in §7.3.1. See new §12 D11.
3. **(GPT-5.6 Sol, new — AAD circular dependency.) The v4 AAD scheme required `envelopeVersion`, `encodingVersion`, and `sectionId` — fields that live *inside* the encrypted material — as authenticated associated data for decrypting that same material, a chicken-and-egg problem; and fixed-size chunks could straddle section boundaries, leaving `sectionId` ill-defined for a straddling chunk.** **Fixed:** `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` are promoted to small unencrypted per-manifest metadata columns (standard practice — a format/version tag is not sensitive, and this is no different from every other envelope-format version byte). Chunking is restructured to be **strictly section-aligned** (no chunk ever spans two Domain P sections), eliminating the straddling-chunk ambiguity outright. `manifestSectionPlain` — the section that itself carries the chunk-range→section mapping needed to decrypt everything else — is designated the structurally-first section and its own chunks always carry a **fixed, format-constant** `sectionId := 0`, never a value derived from decrypted content, breaking the circularity for the one section that would otherwise need to bootstrap itself. Every other section's `sectionId` becomes known only *after* `manifestSectionPlain` decrypts successfully, and is applied to that section's own (section-aligned, unambiguous) chunks in a second decryption pass. See §7.3.1 for the full scheme and the residual it (slightly) widens.
4. **(GPT-5.6 Sol, new — seq/record.seq non-atomicity.) The DB's checkpoint `seq` and the on-chain `record.seq` were assumed to stay in lockstep with no durable protocol for a save-succeeds/attest-fails partial failure or concurrent multi-device reordering — and `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()` was claimed by the audit to discard the checkpoint sequence, contradicting what this design assumed was preserved.** **Verified directly this session** against `origin/main:src/postgres/wallet-state-envelope.ts`: confirmed true — `load()` reads `record.sequence` off the `CheckpointRecord` it gets from `checkpointStore.load()` but returns only the decoded `envelope`, never surfacing the sequence to its caller. **Fixed:** the attestation contract's internal gapless counter is renamed `attestOrdinal` (pure CAS/anti-rollback ordering, no external meaning) and a new, explicit, client-disclosed `dbSeq` witness — the actual `CheckpointStore` sequence number of the specific checkpoint being attested — is added to `AttestRecord`/`attestLeaf`/the salt derivation, replacing the overloaded `seq` field that previously had to mean both things at once. A named, non-fatal "orphaned checkpoint" protocol is specified for the save-succeeds/attest-fails case, and the concurrent multi-device attest race is wired into §3.6's existing recovery path rather than left unspecified. `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`'s signature change (to surface `record.sequence`) is named as a required, blocking companion implementation fix — not silently assumed to already be true. See §7.1(a)/(b), §2.5.3, §3.6, §8, and new §12 D12.
5. **Stale test/wording instances found and fixed (GPT-5.6 Sol).** §11.2's legacy-envelope integration test still described "genuinely legacy (no `envelopeVersion`)" as the legacy-routing case — contradicts v4's own `envelopeVersion === 1` redefinition, under which a version-less envelope is malformed, not legacy. §11.2's present-vs-absent L3 lookup test still described the absent case as "a state-read-proof correctly proving non-membership" — contradicts v4's own honest rescoping (§7.1(b), Priority 4) to a Tier-0 k-of-n cross-check, no real non-membership primitive. §11.2's AES-GCM nonce test still asserted the superseded `uint64(seq)||uint32(chunkIndex)` layout — updated to the v5 client-side construction. §11.1's "L3 pinned vk" test conflated `attestCircuitVkHash` with `statementVersion` as though both are chain-checked, when only `statementVersion` is (§7.1(b), Priority 6) — split and corrected, `attestCircuitVkHash` explicitly named as config-only. §11.6's C8 line similarly overclaimed "the vk/contract pin is enforced" — narrowed to name exactly which sub-pins are enforced. All five fixed in place; see §11.
6. **The one remaining dust-labeling straggler (Opus + GPT-5.6 Sol, independently).** §12's D5 restatement still read "'verified'/'trustless' language is reserved for the consensus-reduced shielded/dust-root path," bundling dust back into "consensus-reduced" language that §2.6 and every other instance in this document correctly splits out. Fixed — see §12 D5.

Section numbers below mostly match v1–v4 to keep prior review comments addressable; v5 material is inserted in place within existing subsections (flagged inline), with §7.3.1's nonce/AAD construction and §7.1(b)'s tail-verification data flow substantially rewritten (flagged at their headers).

---

## Revision history — v4

Round 3 of design-council review came back **unanimous 3/3 NEEDS-ROUND-4**: **Fable 5**, **Opus**, and **GPT-5.6 Sol** (via Codex) all independently re-found the owned-notes-binding defect — the same defect found in round 1 (equation didn't include owned notes), round 2 (added to the equation, restore never checked it), and again in round 3 (restore *still* didn't check it, despite v3's own §2.5.5 prose claiming it did). GPT-5.6 Sol additionally found several new, more severe issues, including a real AES-GCM nonce-reuse vulnerability and a write path that was unimplementable as specified. This revision closes all of it with structural changes, not additional caveats. Summary:

0. **(The core defect, closed for real this time.) `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` never actually recomputed `snapshotRoot` — it trusted a transported field.** v3's §2.5.5 prose asserted the restore predicate recomputed and compared `snapshotRoot`; the actual pseudocode computed `expectedCommitment = persistentCommit(envelope.snapshotRoot, salt)` — reading `envelope.snapshotRoot` directly from the (hostile-DB-controlled) transported envelope — and separately built the returned `Wallet` from `envelope.deserialized`, with nothing binding the two. **Concrete exploit (GPT-5.6 Sol):** a hostile DB serves the genuine, honestly-attested `snapshotRoot` string alongside a tampered `envelope.deserialized` — every check passes, the tampered wallet loads at `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"`. **Fixed, structurally:** §7.1(a)'s envelope schema no longer carries a trusted `snapshotRoot` field at all — only an optional, explicitly-non-authoritative `snapshotRootHint`, plus the canonical Domain P `sections` themselves. §7.1(b)'s `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` now performs **one** canonical decode (`decodeSections`, per §2.5.4's CDDL) producing a single `sections` object; `snapshotRoot` is **always recomputed** from `sections`; the L3 commitment check compares the on-chain `commitment` against a value derived exclusively from that recomputation; and the returned `Wallet` is constructed from that **same** `sections` object — not a second, independently-populated field. The exploit above is now blocked at the mechanism level: there is no longer a separate field to lie about, because the root is always whatever `sections` actually decodes to, and `sections` is also what becomes the wallet. §2.5.5's "practical consequence" paragraph and §12 gain a new decision (D7) naming this fix explicitly, separately from D6 (which fixed the *equation*, not the *predicate* — the round-3 audit's core finding was exactly that this distinction had never been enforced).
1. **A genuine AES-GCM nonce-reuse vulnerability in the v3 encryption construction (GPT-5.6 Sol, CRITICAL).** v3 derived the per-chunk nonce as `uint64(seq) || uint32(chunkIndex)`, with `seq` allocated inside the same Postgres transaction that inserts the (to-be-encrypted) chunk rows. If a later statement in that transaction aborts after a hostile DB/operator has already observed the inserted ciphertext, Postgres rolls back `seq` along with everything else — and the next `save()` attempt can reallocate the identical `seq`, reusing the identical nonce under the identical key for different plaintext: a catastrophic AES-GCM failure, not a theoretical one. **Fixed:** nonce material is decoupled entirely from `seq`. A new, dedicated, native PostgreSQL `SEQUENCE` (`ckpt_nonce_ctr`) supplies `nonceBase` — by ordinary, well-documented Postgres semantics, `nextval()` on a native sequence is never rolled back, even when its enclosing transaction aborts, so `nonceBase` can never repeat regardless of how many times a `save()` is retried. `seq` keeps its existing gapless, transaction-scoped semantics (needed for the v3-item-4/item-10 attested-sequence unification) untouched. AAD is additionally widened to bind the chunk's logical section (`sectionId`, from `manifestSectionPlain`'s own chunk-range mapping) and `nonceBase` itself, closing a second finding — the v3 revision-history text claimed the AAD bound "section" when the actual tuple never did. See §7.3.1 for the full construction and a traced walkthrough confirming the abort/retry/hostile-observation scenario is blocked.
2. **`seq` could not actually be embedded in the envelope before serialization, as v3's schema required (GPT-5.6 Sol, HIGH) — resolved together with item 1, not independently.** `PgCheckpointStore.saveImpl` only allocates `seq` internally, inside its transaction, strictly after receiving already-chunked `data` — verified directly against `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts:139-173` this session. A caller cannot know `seq` before serializing the envelope that is supposed to contain it. **Fixed by removing `seq` from the serialized envelope entirely** (§7.1(a)) rather than adding a two-phase reserve-then-write API to `CheckpointStore`: `seq` was never an input to the `snapshotRoot` equation (§2.5.2), so nothing requires it to be committed plaintext. It survives only as an attest-time witness (the `attest()` circuit computes its own `prev.seq+1` internally) and a restore-time value read from `CheckpointStore`'s own storage-native sequence metadata (already returned by `load()`/`save()` today, no interface change), cross-checked against the chain-authenticated `record.seq`. A two-phase reservation API was considered and rejected: it would decouple `seq` allocation from `seq` consumption, reintroducing sequence gaps the current gapless-upsert design deliberately avoids and threatening the v3 record.seq/envelope.seq unification invariant. Deciding items 1 and 2 together (nonce decoupled from `seq`, `seq` removed from the payload) meant neither fix had to compromise the other.
3. **`fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s "genuine absence, not just no answer" claim had no specified mechanism (GPT-5.6 Sol, HIGH).** v3's comment claimed a "cryptographically backed 'genuinely absent'" without ever specifying the second, deeper state-read traversal from a contract's own state root into its `Map` ledger field that a real non-membership proof would require — and this document's own §5.1 item 2 already names the identical primitive gap for nullifiers ("no exposed proof/non-membership API"). **Fixed, honestly:** the present case (state-read-proof-backed inclusion) is real and unchanged; the absent case is named as unclosable with a real cryptographic primitive in v1 and falls back to a Tier-0-style k-of-n cross-indexer agreement — federated/bounded trust, not consensus-reduced, carried in `AnchoredRestoreResult.residuals` and as new §10 item 9. Also fixed: "fresh finalized tip" language is tightened everywhere to mean "a block this restore independently verified as finalized," never "provably the chain's current latest finalized block" — an eclipsing endpoint serving a genuinely-finalized-but-stale head (with, where it exists, a valid absence proof for that older state) is now named explicitly in §10 item 2, not glossed over.
4. **L1 tail-check gaps (GPT-5.6 Sol, HIGH).** (a) Nothing checked `checkpointHorizon.endIndex === anchor.zswapEndIndex` (or block height) before trusting the envelope's claimed lower bound for the L1 tail scan — a hostile envelope could inflate this value to shrink or empty the range being scanned. **Fixed:** both are now checked against the chain-derived `checkpointHorizon` immediately after the existing root check, same pattern. (b) `verifyTailComplete` never actually received a concrete candidate frontier to apply the collapsed update to. **Fixed:** it now takes `sections.treeFrontier` — the same object L0a just rehashed and the same object the returned wallet is built from — directly.
5. **vk-hash comparison was presented as conditionally real when it isn't, in practice, today (GPT-5.6 Sol + prior rounds).** `assertContractVkPinned`'s "if the API exists, check it" framing let `conn.attestCircuitVkHash` look load-bearing. **Fixed:** since no such chain API has been confirmed to exist (still open on §12's Secondary list, now resolved for v1 scope specifically), v1 ships the structural-only check unconditionally; `attestCircuitVkHash` is a typed, forward-compatible placeholder, not consulted by any v1 check — stated plainly, not hedged, and named as §10 item 4's sharpened residual.
6. **Three remaining dust-labeling stragglers (Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol).** The L1 "Shielded / dust" bullet (§ "L1 — Bounded-scan completeness") and the C5 claim-to-test-matrix line both still bundled dust under "consensus-reduced" language despite §2.6's Tier-F-lite classification, contradicting v2/v3's own item-8 fix. **Fixed:** both now explicitly split shielded (consensus-reduced) from dust (Tier-F-lite, same ADS mechanism, different root trust), grepped and checked exhaustively against every remaining "consensus-reduced" mention in the document (two real stragglers found and fixed; the third approximate location the audit flagged, near old §D5, was already correctly scoped).
7. **Legacy envelope version mismatch against real current code — a concrete integration bug (GPT-5.6 Sol).** v3 defined "legacy" as "an envelope with no `envelopeVersion` field." **Verified directly this session** (`git grep -n "envelopeVersion" origin/main -- src/`, `src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts`): the real, currently-shipping envelope always carries a mandatory `envelopeVersion: 1` (`ENVELOPE_VERSION = 1 as const`, enforced by both the shape schema and a separate value guard) — no envelope with no version field has ever existed in this codebase. Under v3's own guard, every real existing wallet's envelope would have hit `SnapshotEnvelopeUnverifiableError` on first restore attempt post-upgrade, rather than routing to the legacy path as intended. **Fixed:** "legacy" is redefined as `envelopeVersion === 1` (the real shape); the new anchor-bearing shape is `envelopeVersion === 2`; anything that is neither is now correctly treated as genuinely malformed input (a *stricter*, more correct fail-closed posture than v3's), not silently accepted onto the legacy path. `decode()`'s real hardcoded single-version guard is noted as needing to become a small recognized-version dispatch as part of implementation.
8. **Minor hardening and honesty items (GPT-5.6 Sol).** `record.height === anchor.blockHeight` and `record.encodingVersion === envelope.encodingVersion` are now explicit, individually-diagnosable checks in the restore predicate (§7.1(b)), on top of (not instead of) the full `attestLeaf` reconstruction that already covered them transitively. The "no-key legacy probe" residual (§7.1(d)) is corrected from "vacuous outside a genuinely keyless wallet" to "opt-in and not enforced for any caller that omits `identity`, keyed or not" — v3 overclaimed here. The "trial-decryption over every commitment" sentence (§2.5.5) is corrected to "every *delivered* ciphertext," matching §6's own architecture rather than blurring the ciphertext-delivery residual it's supposed to respect. The AES-GCM dedup-loss cost is now disclosed as a one-sentence, explicit storage-efficiency tradeoff in §7.3.1, not left implicit in the corrected residual description.

Section numbers below mostly match v1/v2/v3 to keep prior review comments addressable; v4 material is inserted in place within existing subsections (flagged inline) rather than renumbering the document, with two exceptions: §7.1(b)'s function body is substantially rewritten (flagged at its header), and §7.3.1's nonce/AAD construction is substantially rewritten (flagged at its header).

---

## Revision history — v3

Round 2 of design-council review sent v2 back **2-of-3 NEEDS-ROUND-3**: **Claude Fable 5** and **GPT-5.6 Sol** (via Codex) independently found the same core remaining defect; **Claude Opus** judged no-round-3-needed but flagged one related gap (folded in as item 6 below). This revision fixes all of it. Summary:

0. **(The core defect.) The `snapshotRoot` commitment equation never actually bound the wallet's owned notes.** §2.5.2's v2 equation covered cursor, the *global* tree root `R_N^tree`, nullifiers, history, dust, and manifest description — but no canonical owned-notes/ownership-set section. Two snapshots with completely different owned-note sets but identical cursor/nullifiers/tree-root/dust/manifest therefore produced the **same** attested `snapshotRoot` — directly contradicting §3's own prose (the V1b+V2 description at "cursor/notes/nullifiers/history/dust/manifest," line ~189) claiming the root covers "notes." v2's §5.0 had correctly diagnosed that root equality on the *global* tree doesn't bind wallet identity, but the fix that diagnosis called for — an owned-notes section in the governing equation — was never actually added; only the surrounding prose was corrected. **Fixed:** §2.5.2 gains a required `ownedNotesPlain` section (Domain P) folded into the `snapshotRoot` equation; §2.5.4's CDDL requirement is extended to cover it; new §2.5.5 resolves the follow-on question both reviewers raised — how the section's own correctness is established at restore time without a full historical re-scan — by adopting **option (b)** (live-tail re-derivation bounds the risk to the base-at-N) **combined with an explicit, named (a)-residual for the base itself** (attest-time honesty, already §10 item 4, now extended to name owned-notes explicitly). §5.0 is updated to state precisely what this closes (*binding*) versus what it doesn't (*completeness* — still the unchanged §5/§5.1 ciphertext-delivery residual).
1. **Restore API was fail-open on L3 record authentication.** `fetchLatestAttestation` was an unauthenticated query, uncoupled from any freshness proof, and a present-but-mismatched record silently downgraded to `"L0+L1"` exactly like a genuinely-absent one. **Fixed:** §7.1(b) is rewritten around a second, independently-fetched *fresh* `verifyFinalizedTuple` horizon (the current finalized tip, not the checkpoint's own old block) that the attestation lookup is now read-proof-authenticated against (`fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`), and a present-but-mismatched record now throws a dedicated `RollbackDetectedError` instead of silently downgrading — only a *genuinely absent* record (proven absent via the same read-proof) still downgrades quietly.
2. **`attestLeaf` was never reconstructed at restore time.** Only `commitment` and `height` were checked. **Fixed:** §7.1(b)'s L3 step now reconstructs the full `attestLeaf` hash per §2.5.3's equation (genesis/network id, wallet kind, block hash, tree root, end index, encoding version, statement version, sequence, previous commitment) and requires it to equal `record.attestLeaf`.
3. **vk/contract/statement pins were prose-only.** **Fixed:** the restore `conn` config gains typed `attestCircuitVkHash` and `attestStatementVersion` fields (§7.1(b)); a per-restore check hard-fails on `record.statementVersion` mismatch (`PinnedStatementVersionMismatchError`), and a one-time, session-level `assertContractVkPinned` check is specified for the vk-hash pin (§7.1(b), §3.5 cross-ref).
4. **`record.seq` vs `envelope.seq` were allowed to silently diverge.** **Fixed:** §7.1(a)'s envelope schema and §7.1(b)'s restore logic now treat these as one shared sequence space (the wallet's attest-driving `seq` *is* the envelope's persisted `seq`); a hard equality check is added, and the local high-water mark is now updated from the chain-authenticated `record.seq`, never the DB-supplied `envelope.seq`.
5. **`horizon`'s type was missing `R_N`/`endIndex`** despite downstream code reading both. **Fixed:** §7.1(b)'s `HorizonTuple` type now carries the full tuple §4 already returns.
6. **The L1 tail-completeness check was a no-op in the normal case** (Opus's item, folded in here) — `horizon` was derived from the checkpoint's own block, making `anchor.zswapEndIndex == horizon.endIndex` trivially true. **Fixed:** §7.1(b) now derives L1's upper bound from the *same* fresh tip-horizon added for item 1, making the tail span `[checkpoint's endIndex, current finalized tip's endIndex)` genuinely non-trivial — one fix serves both gaps.
7. **AES-GCM was internally contradictory** (encrypt-then-chunk prose vs. per-chunk-nonce spec) and `CheckpointStore.save()`'s actual sequence-allocation order was never checked against source. **Verified directly against `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts:139-173` (v3 session):** confirmed — chunking and chunk-hash computation happen in `saveImpl` *before* `withTransaction` opens; `seq` is allocated *inside* the transaction, after chunks are already split, via the atomic `ckpt_sequence_counters` upsert-increment (`next_seq - 1 AS claimed_seq`). An external wrapper genuinely cannot pre-compute a `(seq, chunkIndex)` nonce before that point. **Fixed:** §7.3.1 picks **chunk-then-encrypt** as the sole construction, specifies an injective `uint64(seq) || uint32(chunkIndex)` (96-bit) nonce layout, moves encryption *inside* `PgCheckpointStore.saveImpl`'s transaction (after `seq` allocation, before each chunk's hash/insert) rather than pre-reserving a sequence, widens the AAD to bind chunk index/count/section plus key/encoding version, specifies `encKdfVersion` as a per-manifest rotation-epoch identifier, and corrects the dedup-leak residual: under a monotonic per-`(seq,chunkIndex)` nonce, cross-checkpoint plaintext equality is **no longer observable** as ciphertext equality (every `save()` gets a fresh `seq`); the real residual left is the much weaker chunk-count/byte-length shape leak inherent to any chunked store.
8. **Dust trust-tier labeling was inconsistent** — "consensus-reduced" in §1, the architecture diagram, and the phasing table, versus correctly "Tier-F-lite" in §2.6. **Fixed:** §1, the diagram, and §9's phasing table now split shielded (consensus-reduced) from dust (Tier-F-lite) everywhere they were previously bundled.
9. **§3's "closes threats A1–A4" overclaimed**, contradicting §2.6/§5's own adversarial matrix (ciphertext-downgrade sits under A1 and is explicitly *not* caught by L0/L1). **Fixed:** narrowed to name exactly what the contract supplies — latest-pointer rollback resistance, identity separation, attestation authorization — with commitment-omission correctly attributed to L1 and ciphertext-omission to the §5 residual.
10. **Rollback-recovery retrieval (§3.6 step 3) wasn't concrete** — `AttestRecord` has no storage locator, and a hiding commitment isn't one. **Fixed:** given item 4's `record.seq == envelope.seq` fix, step 3 now retrieves the checkpoint concretely via `CheckpointStore.load(walletId, networkId, record.seq)` — no new `AttestRecord` field needed, since the checkpoint-store's own monotonic sequence *is* the authenticated locator once the two sequence spaces are unified.
11. **Legacy-restore downgrade risk** — a hostile DB could serve an anchor-less envelope to a wallet that has a real on-chain attestation, forcing it through the unverified legacy path. **Fixed:** §7.1(d)'s `restoreLegacyUnverified()` now performs an independent pre-restore L3 pointer probe (when `identity.skAttest` is available) and refuses to proceed on the legacy path if a genuine on-chain record for this wallet's `id` is found.

Section numbers below mostly match v1/v2 to keep prior review comments addressable; new v3 material is inserted as further decimal subsections (§2.5.5, §7.1(e)) or in place within existing v2 subsections, flagged inline.

---

## Revision history — v2

The v1 draft (`8468657`) went to design-council review cold, before any adversarial pass. Three independent reviewers — **Claude Fable 5**, **Claude Opus**, and **GPT-5.6 Sol** (via Codex) — each read it without seeing the others' notes and converged strongly; GPT-5.6 Sol issued an explicit **NEEDS-REWORK / BLOCK** verdict. This revision addresses all eleven convergent and independently-discovered findings. Summary of what changed and why:

1. **Canonical commitment relation was self-contradictory** (§7.3 said `manifestHash` "is exactly" `snapshotRoot`, while §3/§8 use V2's structured root; ciphertext-level and plaintext-level commitments were never formally separated, so a routine key rotation would silently break every prior attested checkpoint's equality check). **Fixed:** new normative §2.5 defines two disjoint commitment domains (plaintext "semantic" vs ciphertext "storage") and a single canonical attestation equation; canonical encoding (old §12 Q6) is promoted from secondary to blocking (new §12 D0).
2. **Envelope migration was fail-open** (`anchor` was `Schema.optional` yet described as "mandatory"; `restoreVerified()` only checked anchors `if (anchor)`, so an anchor-less envelope — legacy or freshly fabricated — sailed through unverified while returning from a function named "Verified"). **Fixed:** §7.1(a) versions the envelope schema; a v2 envelope's anchor is non-optional and any envelope failing that shape is fail-closed, routed to a separately-named, never-"verified" legacy path (§7.1(d)), with a forced-reanchor migration policy.
3. **Rollback recovery was detection-only** (no story for an already-active wallet, no periodic/pre-spend recheck, no quarantine/recovery transition). **Fixed:** new §3.6 defines an explicit restore/operation state machine (`unverified → verified-at-finalized-head → caught-up → active → quarantined`) with concrete recovery steps for in-flight transactions and multi-device CRDT deltas.
4. **vk/circuit succession was unauthenticated** (the Mithril-CVE-class gap, GHSA-724h-fpm5-4qvr: protocol-parameter succession must be bound inside what's cryptographically authenticated, not travel as unauthenticated sidecar metadata) and was filed as merely "secondary." **Fixed:** new §3.5 explicitly commits v1 to full immutability with hard-pinned contract address + vk hash + statement version in client config (option **a**), adds this as a named §10 residual-trust item, and documents a successor-certificate mechanism (option **b**) as the specified-but-deferred v1.1+ upgrade path.
5. **Vocabulary overclaimed** ("consensus-grade," "proves S is exactly correct," "the chain is trusted unconditionally," "kills threats A1–A4"). **Fixed:** replaced throughout with scoped statements consistent with the rigor §10 already used; see inline diffs in §1, §2, §3.
6. **`restoreVerified()` didn't implement its own flagship guarantee** (no L3 attestation check, no `sk_attest` parameter, no L2 sequence check — L0+L1 only). **Fixed:** renamed to `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` in §7.1(b), fully rewritten to include the L3 attestation check and L2 anti-rollback sequence check, returning a structured `{wallet, verificationLevel, horizon, residuals}` result instead of a bare `Wallet`.
7. **L0's "proves S is exactly correct" claim was false** — the zswap root is a *global*, wallet-agnostic commitment; root equality alone doesn't bind wallet identity. **Investigated (§5.0):** L0+L1 together prove the *global* tree is complete and untruncated; wallet-identity binding additionally depends on the wallet's own local trial-decryption over that verified-complete leaf set, which is sound **except** for exactly the §5 ciphertext-delivery residual — i.e., items 7 and 5 are the *same* gap seen from two angles, now stated as one unified, correctly-scoped residual rather than two separately-described ones. No new cryptographic primitive was needed; the claim was rewritten. The §5 "first spend re-validates completeness" claim is corrected to scope it to the single spent input, not the whole note set.
8. **Unshielded/dust didn't reduce to an on-chain commitment** despite being described alongside claims that do. **Fixed:** new §2.6 names this explicitly as a separate, weaker **federated-quorum trust tier** (Tier-F / Tier-F-lite), distinct from the consensus-reduced tier the rest of the document claims; "verified"/"trustless" language is no longer applied to these paths unqualified.
9. **Finality proof wasn't cryptographically bound to the values it authenticates** (independently-fetched root + independently-verified finality, not one coupled proof). **Fixed:** §4 and §7.1(b) now define `verifyFinalizedTuple`, a single call that derives `(blockHash, R_N, endIndex, finalizedHash)` from one state-read-proof against one header, with the GRANDPA justification checked against that exact `blockHash` — every downstream check consumes only this one `horizon` object.
10. **The "UmbraDB already implements encryption" claim was factually false.** **Verified against source** (`git show origin/main:src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts`): `PgCheckpointStore.save()` only SHA-256-hashes chunks and stores raw bytes verbatim — zero encryption. `getOrCreateSalt` (cited as evidence) belongs to the unrelated `PgPrivateStateProvider` subsystem (`design/design.md` §"Encryption keys are derived..."), confirming the earlier session finding that it has nothing to do with the checkpoint/snapshot path. **Fixed:** §2 and §7.3 corrected to state encryption is **not yet implemented**; new §7.3.1 specifies it as a blocking v1 requirement (nonce rule, KDF/domain separation, AAD, key rotation, dedup-leak residual).
11. **BFT-CRDT treatment overstated automatic detection.** A malicious DB can show two devices indefinitely divergent forks unless they actually exchange histories or share an independently-authenticated head. **Fixed:** §2's L2 multi-device bullet now states this as an explicit precondition, proposes the L3 attestation pointer itself as a connectivity-free shared head, and names device-key membership/revocation and non-commutative merge rules as explicitly deferred, not silently solved.

Section numbers below mostly match v1 to keep prior review comments addressable; new material is inserted as decimal subsections (§2.5, §2.6, §3.5, §3.6, §7.1(d), §7.3.1) rather than renumbering the whole document.

---

## 1. Problem and core principle

UmbraDB persists a Midnight wallet's replay-derived sync state; the Midnight SDK ships only in-memory storage (brief 01 §5: every serialized snapshot today is `{local-state hex, protocolVersion, networkId, offset}` with the cursor itself `Schema.optional` — no block hash, no root, no anchor). On memory loss the wallet must restore from UmbraDB — **LOCAL or REMOTE/UNTRUSTED** — and verify the snapshot is correct **without replaying the chain**.

**The owner-set principle (the whole design pivots on it):** we do not prove "S is correct as of the tip." We prove **"snapshot S is complete with respect to on-tree commitments and correct with respect to the finalized chain view, as of a FINALIZED checkpoint block N"** — a deliberately narrower claim than "the complete, correct wallet state" (v1 draft's phrasing overclaimed this; see §5.0/§10 for exactly what is and is not covered, notably the ciphertext-delivery and spend-hiding residuals). Because the chain is append-only and GRANDPA finality precludes reverting blocks ≤ N, that certificate is **valid for horizon N for as long as the residual trust items in §10 hold** — it does not expire on its own terms, but it is not "permanent" in an absolute sense; call it a floor whose *on-tree* completeness is durably certified, not an unconditional permanent guarantee (brief 07 §0; contrast the ledger's rolling 1-hour `global_ttl` spend-anchor window, which is a *spendability* window, not a *verifiability* one — brief 01 §2, `zswap/src/ledger.rs:73-79`). On restore the wallet verifies the certificate, then catches up `[N, tip]` **LIVE** via the normal ADS-authenticated incremental sync. Each proven finalized checkpoint is a **cryptographically-certified floor for on-tree completeness** the wallet never rescans below again — stronger than Zcash's *trusted* birthday only along that specific axis (brief 02 §5, brief 07 §0), not across every axis of correctness.

The reduction that governs every layer (brief 03 §0's theorem): **the DB is never a source of correctness — only of availability.** Every no-replay check must reduce S to a check against an **on-chain commitment the wallet independently trusts**, whose trust in turn reduces to **consensus/finality**. Content-addressing and AES-GCM prove "the bytes I read are the bytes written"; they never prove "the bytes are the correct chain-derived state" (brief 03 §0). That gap is what this design closes — **for the shielded path, by full reduction to consensus; for dust, only to the softer Tier-F-lite tier (single indexer, `@beta`, not node-cross-checked); for the unshielded path in v1, to a federated quorum of indexer operators (Tier-F) — dust and unshielded are both explicitly weaker than shielded and named as such in §2.6 (v3: this sentence previously bundled dust with shielded under "consensus," inconsistent with §2.6's own classification — corrected, item 8).** Every plaintext/semantic value this document calls a "commitment" is precisely defined in §2.5; a canonical, versioned byte-encoding of every committed section (old §12 Q6) is a **blocking v1 requirement**, not optional plumbing — without it, the equations in §2.5 aren't well-defined.

---

## 2. The layered architecture, made concrete

Four layers, each with a precise job, a precise mechanism, and a precise residual it hands to the next.

```
                     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   L3 Self-cert      │  On-chain Compact "Attested Manifest Root" (05)  ── v1        │
   (freshness +      │  Offline v-lightweight ZK certificate (07)       ── v1.1 opt  │
    permanence)      │  Recursive IVC checkpoint ratchet (08)           ── research  │
                     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   L2 Remote/        │  Client-side AES-256-GCM (seed-derived) — NOT YET BUILT,     │
   untrusted-DB      │    spec in §7.3.1, blocking v1 requirement                    │
   hardening         │  Anti-rollback: chain-attested height + chain-as-freshness   │
                     │  Multi-device: signed hash-chained CRDT deltas (BFT-CRDT),    │
                     │    conditional on history exchange (§2 bullet 3)             │
                     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   L1 Bounded-scan   │  Shielded: collapsed-tree range proof vs on-chain root       │
   completeness      │    (ADS already present — 06 §2.1) — consensus-reduced       │
   (ADS)             │  Dust: same mechanism, roots @beta, NOT node-cross-checked   │
                     │    — Tier-F-lite, NOT consensus-reduced (§2.6)               │
                     │  Unshielded: NEW authenticated by-address MB-tree index      │
                     │    — Tier-F, federated-quorum trust tier, NOT               │
                     │    consensus-reduced; see §2.6                                │
                     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
                     ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
   L0 Anchor         │  {finalized N, blockHash, tree endIndex/frontier, R_N}       │
                     │  finality verified via GRANDPA justification + state-read     │
                     │  — all four values from ONE coupled tuple (§4, §7.1(b))      │
                     └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

### L0 — The anchor

**What is persisted, alongside each wallet-kind's serialized local state:** the block-anchor tuple `{blockHeight N, blockHash, treeEndIndex, R_N}` for the relevant tree(s) at serialization time — `zswapMerkleTreeRoot` + `zswapEndIndex` for the shielded wallet; both dust roots + end-indices for the dust wallet; the by-address UTXO-set root for the unshielded wallet (brief 01 §6 "strongest anchor candidate", brief 03 §7).

**Why every tree already has a usable root (no node change).** Midnight's `Sp<T,D>` content-addressing (`storage-core/src/arena.rs:1505-1519`) makes the zswap tree, both dust trees, and the whole `LedgerState` DAG deterministically hashable (brief 01 §1). The zswap/dust roots are exposed per-block by the indexer's `Block` type — `zswapMerkleTreeRoot`/`zswapEndIndex` (stable), `dustCommitmentMerkleTreeRoot`/`dustGenerationMerkleTreeRoot` (`@beta`) (`schema-v4.graphql:64-88`). **The load-bearing fact:** collapsing "leaves the hash invariant" (`transient-crypto/src/merkle_tree.rs:921`), so a restored snapshot's `merkle_tree.rehash().root()` — computed **entirely offline from the snapshot alone** — is bit-identical to the full on-chain root at the same `endIndex` (brief 01 §6.2). And the indexer recomputes zswap/full-ledger roots itself and `bail!`s on any mismatch vs the node on every block (brief 04 §3, `chain-indexer/src/application.rs:~404-420`) — so trusting `zswapMerkleTreeRoot` is trusting a value two independent re-executions already agree on. (Dust roots are computed and served but **not** node-cross-checked — no node dust-root RPC exists — so dust anchors ship on softer ground, and per §2.6 are scoped to a federated-quorum trust tier, not the consensus-reduced tier shielded gets; brief 04 §3, brief 06 §2.5.)

**What L0 alone proves — precisely, not "S is exactly correct" (the v1 draft's claim, now retracted).** The zswap commitment tree is **global**: it is the same tree, with the same root, for every wallet observing block N — it is not partitioned per-wallet. Root equality between the wallet's offline recompute and the chain's committed `R_N` therefore proves only that **the snapshot's reconstructed tree frontier — the full leaf set through `endIndex` — is bit-identical to the chain's own frontier at N.** It does **not**, by itself, bind which subset of those leaves the wallet is entitled to call "mine": a snapshot could carry a perfectly correct global frontier while its separate "owned notes" bookkeeping is tampered, truncated, or simply wrong, and L0's root check would not catch it. What closes that gap, and exactly how far it closes it, is worked out precisely in **§5.0** — the short version is that L0+L1 together establish global-tree completeness, and the wallet's own local trial-decryption over that verified-complete leaf set is what actually determines "mine," subject to one residual (ciphertext delivery) that is tracked, not hidden.

**Restore-time L0 check** (zero network, then one query): (1) recompute the local root offline, compare to persisted `R_N` — catches corruption/tamper/bit-rot instantly; (2) query `block(offset:{height:N})` and compare its committed root/endIndex to the persisted anchor — proves the tree frontier is correct as of N with **zero transactions replayed** (brief 01 §6); (3) the finality of N and the authenticity of R_N are discharged by L0's finality sub-layer (§4) — and, per the §4/§7.1(b) v2 fix, steps (2) and (3) now consume **one** coupled `(blockHash, R_N, endIndex, finalizedHash)` tuple rather than two independently-fetched facts that merely happen to agree.

### L1 — Bounded-scan completeness (the ADS)

L0 proves the base tree-frontier at N. L1 makes the live tail `[N, tip]` **verifiably exhaustive** at the tree level, not merely "hopefully complete," closing the *commitment*-omission freedom the anchor alone leaves (brief 06 §0, §2.1). Note precisely, per §5.0: L1 closes tree-level omission for the *global* leaf set, same as L0 — it is still not, by itself, a wallet-identity-binding proof; see §5.0 for the full picture.

- **Shielded / dust — the ADS mechanism is already present and already exposed, but the two paths do NOT share a trust tier (v4 straggler fix, Priority 7 — this bullet previously implied both did).** The zswap tree is fixed-height-32, append-only over contiguous indices; `MerkleTreeCollapsedUpdate` (`transient-crypto/src/merkle_tree.rs:302-405`) authenticates any leaf range in O(log range) ≤ 32 hashes, served by `zswapMerkleTreeCollapsedUpdate(startIndex,endIndex)` (`schema-v4.graphql:1258`, stable) for shielded, and by the equivalent `@beta` dust collapsed-update query for dust. By the RFC 6962 "fix size + root ⇒ leaf multiset determined" argument, a wallet that applies the bridge for `[endIndex_N, endIndex_tip)` and rehashes to a root equal to the on-chain tip root has a **commitment-completeness proof**: the indexer could not have omitted, inserted, or reordered any commitment (brief 06 §2.1). Penumbra ships exactly this shape in production (chain-provided inline span-hashes + Anchor = global tree root; brief 09 §1.3, ②). **This is SDK-only wiring** — `applyCollapsedUpdate` already exists in the ledger crate but is **never called** by the wallet today (brief 04 §2, `shielded-wallet/src/v1/CoreWallet.ts:148-151`). **For shielded, this path is consensus-reduced**: the tip root it checks against is the zswap root, which the indexer's own ingestion re-derives and `bail!`s on mismatch against the node (§ "L0 — The anchor" above). **For dust, the identical collapsed-update mechanism checks against a dust root that is *not* node-cross-checked (`@beta`, single indexer) — per §2.6 this is Tier-F-lite, NOT consensus-reduced, even though the ADS wiring is byte-for-byte the same shape.** The mechanism being shared does not make the trust tier shared; §2.6 governs which label applies to which root.
- **Unshielded — a genuinely new authenticated by-address index is required, and it is NOT consensus-reduced in v1 — see §2.6.** Unshielded state is `UtxoState{utxos: HashMap<Utxo,UtxoMeta>}` (`ledger/src/structure.rs:2948-2968`), keyed by `ArenaHash(whole-Utxo)` — no address locality, no exposed proof API, and no point-in-time "UTXO set by address" query exists (brief 06 §4.1; the `unshieldedUtxos` query is *proposed*, not extant). Build a **Merkle-B-tree / authenticated-dictionary** keyed by owner address as an indexer-maintained materialized view; a query returns A's UTXO list + Merkle path to `R_utxo(N)`, and for an absent address the **two boundary leaves** `A⁻ < A < A⁺` proving no leaf hides between them (Naor–Nissim / MB-tree non-membership; brief 06 §4.2–4.3). The subtree-size annotation gives verifiable counts — and Midnight's own MPT already carries a `SizeAnn` size monoid (`storage/src/merkle_patricia_trie.rs:499-515`), merely unexposed. **v1 ships this as Tier-F (federated quorum): a signed STH + k≥2 independent indexers, not a reduction to a consensus commitment** — see §2.6 for exactly what that means and does not mean.

### L2 — Remote/untrusted-DB hardening

Three properties the local single-writer case never needed (brief 03 §4, brief 11 §5):

- **Confidentiality.** Client-side **AES-256-GCM** under a key deterministically derived from the wallet seed (Zcash ZIP-32 shape; brief 03 §5). **Corrected from the v1 draft, which claimed this was already implemented: it is not.** `git show origin/main:src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts` confirms `PgCheckpointStore.save()` splits data into chunks, SHA-256-hashes each chunk plus the ordered hash list (`manifestHash`), and stores the **raw, unencrypted** bytes — there is no encryption anywhere in the checkpoint-envelope path today. The `getOrCreateSalt` mechanism the v1 draft cited belongs to `PgPrivateStateProvider` (`design/design.md`, the "Encryption keys are derived from a per-`(accountId, scope)` salt" passage) — an entirely different subsystem, Midnight contract *private state* storage, unrelated to wallet snapshots. Full v1 requirement spec is in **§7.3.1**. Once built: the DB sees only ciphertext + opaque content hashes; the commitment the DB sees (`manifestHash`) is over *ciphertext* (pure blob integrity, Domain S — §2.5.2), the commitment the wallet checks against the chain (`snapshotRoot`) is over *plaintext* (Domain P), computed locally after decrypt and **never sent to the DB** and **never substituted for or equated with `manifestHash`** (brief 03 §5, §2.5). Layers compose without leaking, and — critically, fixing the v1 draft's contradiction — a key rotation changes `manifestHash` but by construction cannot change `snapshotRoot`, so it never invalidates a prior attestation.
- **Anti-rollback / freshness.** The GCM tag carries **no** freshness — a remote DB can serve a *previously authentic* old snapshot and it decrypts perfectly (the ROTE replay attack; brief 03 §4). Two complementary defenses: (i) a strictly-increasing, writer-signed `anchorHeight`, with the highest-ever-accepted value held in a small trusted local store — protects a *running* wallet (**v7 straggler fix, Priority 7**: this bullet previously read "a strictly-increasing `seq` + `anchorHeight`" — `seq`/`dbSeq` carries no monotonicity guarantee anywhere in this design, per §12 D14, so it is removed from this local high-water-mark description; `height` alone is the signal, matching every other instance of this check in the document); (ii) **the chain as the freshness oracle** — require `anchorHeight ≥` last-known-finalized and `anchorBlockHash` on the canonical header chain (brief 03 §4). **Crucial gap for our exact scenario:** on total memory loss the wallet has *no* local counter, so (i) and (ii) cannot detect a rollback served to a cold-booted wallet. That gap is precisely what L3's on-chain attestation closes at restore time (§3) — and, per the v2 fix in **§3.6**, what an already-*active* wallet must also keep rechecking, since detection-at-restore alone leaves a wallet that resumed on stale-but-genuine state with no story for discovering that fact later.
- **Multi-device (the NECESSARY complement, brief 11 §5) — with an explicit communication precondition, corrected from the v1 draft.** A DB shared across N devices of one wallet is a *horizontal* trust relation none of briefs 01–06 covers. Adopt Kleppmann's **BFT-CRDT**: each device signs its wallet-state deltas and hash-chains each to its causal predecessor; the untrusted DB is demoted to a relay that can delay/drop (detectable, recoverable) but cannot forge, splice out-of-causal-order, or silently rewrite history without the hash chain visibly breaking — **provided devices actually exchange histories, or independently check a shared authenticated head, on some cadence.** This is a precondition, not an automatic consequence of hash-chaining: a malicious DB can show two devices two separate, internally-valid-looking forks **indefinitely** if it simply never lets them compare notes — signatures prove authorship, not synchronization, and a chain that is never cross-checked between devices cannot detect a split it was never shown (brief 11 §5.2, Kleppmann PaPoC 2022, with this caveat added in v2). **v1 requirement:** specify a minimum exchange cadence — either periodic direct device-to-device sync, or (simpler, no device-to-device connectivity required) each device independently re-checks the **L3 attestation pointer** (§3), which is a shared authenticated head by construction, since every device validates it against the chain rather than against each other. **Explicitly deferred, not silently solved:** device-key membership/revocation (adding/removing a device from the trusted signer set) and a merge-rule specification for non-commutative wallet operations (e.g. two devices independently initiating conflicting spends) are out of scope for v1.

### 2.5 Canonical commitment relation (normative)

*(New in v2 — fixes item 1: the internally-contradictory commitment relation.)*

This section is binding. Every "verified" / "matches" / "equality check" claim elsewhere in this document must resolve to exactly the equations below; where prose elsewhere is loose, this section governs.

**2.5.1 The problem this section fixes.** The v1 draft used `manifestHash` and `snapshotRoot` interchangeably in places (old §7.3: "its `manifestHash` … is exactly the `snapshotRoot`") while §3/§8 describe a V2 structured root where `manifestHash` is at most one leaf among several. Worse, the encryption boundary was never disambiguated: `CheckpointStore`'s `manifestHash` commits over **ciphertext** bytes (chunked after encryption, once §7.3.1 ships), while every chain-facing check in §4/§5/§7 is stated over **plaintext** semantics (tree roots, cursor, nullifiers). Under the old text, a routine key rotation or re-encryption (same plaintext, new ciphertext) would change `manifestHash` — and if `manifestHash` were ever substituted for the chain-checked root, **every** prior attested checkpoint would appear to fail its restore-time equality check even though nothing about the wallet's actual state changed. Fixed by strictly separating two commitment domains that must never be equated or substituted for one another.

**2.5.2 Two domains, never conflated.**

*Domain P (plaintext / semantic).* Everything the chain-facing verification layers (L0/L1/L3) check is computed over decrypted, canonicalized plaintext:

- `R_N^tree` — the per-tree Merkle root (zswap / dust) at finalized height N, as exposed on-chain. `computeSnapshotRoot` derives this input by rehashing `sections.treeFrontierAtN` (§7.1(a)) offline — the **same** rehash L0a already performs, over the **same, never-mutated** field — never from a chain query and never from a tip-advanced frontier (v5 fix, Priority 1: see §7.1(b) for why this distinction is now load-bearing and how it's enforced).
- `cursorPlain` — the wallet's local sync cursor (endIndex, appliedIndex) in canonical encoding.
- `ownedNotesPlain` — **new in v3 (item 0, the core round-2 defect).** Canonical encoding of the wallet's own local owned-note set at N: for each note the wallet currently believes it owns, its commitment `cc_i` (the same value the zswap tree indexes, `ZswapLocalState`'s local note representation — `ledger-v8.d.ts`'s `QualifiedCoinInfo`/note-commitment shape, the wallet's actual local representation, not a re-derivation), its `mt_index`, and its value/type fields, sorted by `mt_index` for determinism. This is **exactly** the section whose absence from v2's equation was the round-2 defect: without it, the `snapshotRoot` equation bound the global tree frontier and the wallet's bookkeeping metadata (cursor, nullifiers) but never the wallet's *actual claim about which notes are its own* — the one thing that makes the snapshot *this wallet's* state rather than an interchangeable, equally-valid-looking one for the same cursor. See §2.5.5 for exactly what including this section does and does not prove, and how its own correctness is established at restore time.
- `nullifiersPlain` — canonical encoding of the wallet's known-spent set at N.
- `historyRef` — a reference into L3's on-chain `history` tree (§8), not a local blob.
- `dustPlain` — dust-tree state, if applicable.
