**Fixed:** the envelope schema is versioned. Any envelope claiming `envelopeVersion: 2` carries a **non-optional** `anchor`:

```ts
envelopeVersion: Schema.Literal(2),
anchor: Schema.Struct({                 // MANDATORY for any v2 envelope -- no longer Schema.optional
  zswapMerkleTreeRoot: Schema.String,   // from ledger.ZswapLocalState.merkleTreeRoot
  zswapEndIndex: Schema.BigInt,         // the range LOWER boundary for the L1 tail proof
  blockHash: Schema.String,
  blockHeight: Schema.Number,
  finalizedHash: Schema.String,         // superseded at verify-time by verifyFinalizedTuple's horizon (§4)
}),
sections: Schema.Struct({               // v4 (Priority 1): the canonical Domain P sections
  cursorPlain: CursorSectionSchema,     // §2.5.4 CDDL -- the ONLY source restoreAnchoredCheckpoint
  ownedNotesPlain: OwnedNotesSectionSchema, //   trusts for recomputing snapshotRoot AND for
  nullifiersPlain: NullifiersSectionSchema, //   constructing the returned Wallet -- see §7.1(b)
  dustPlain: DustSectionSchema,             //   for why these must be the SAME decode, not two.
  manifestSectionPlain: ManifestSectionSchema,
  historyRef: Schema.String,            // v5 fix (Priority 1, second finding): §2.5.2's snapshotRoot
                                         //   equation has ALWAYS required historyRef as an input --
                                         //   it was missing from this schema (GPT-5.6 Sol + Opus,
                                         //   independently, round 5), so computeSnapshotRoot could
                                         //   not actually implement the equation it's specified to.
                                         //   A reference into L3's own on-chain `history` tree (§8),
                                         //   not a local blob -- see §2.5.2's definition.
  treeFrontierAtN: FrozenFrontier,      // v5 RENAMED from v4's `treeFrontier` (Priority 1, first
                                         //   finding). This is the wallet's local Merkle-tree/frontier
                                         //   bytes AS OF CHECKPOINT N -- rehashed offline to produce
                                         //   R_N^tree (§ "L0" / L0a) and fed into computeSnapshotRoot.
                                         //   v6 (Priority 2): type is now `FrozenFrontier`, not a bare
                                         //   `Schema.Uint8Array` -- see the class below. "Never mutated"
                                         //   is now STRUCTURALLY enforced, not a documentation convention.
}),
snapshotRootHint: Schema.optional(Schema.String),  // v4 (Priority 1, renamed from v3's `snapshotRoot`):
                                         // an OPTIONAL, EXPLICITLY UNTRUSTED cache/fast-fail value.
                                         // NEVER an input to any security-relevant equality check --
                                         // restoreAnchoredCheckpoint always recomputes snapshotRoot
                                         // from `sections` above and ignores this field for anything
                                         // but an early, non-authoritative local-corruption signal.
                                         // See §7.1(b) for the full rationale (this is the direct fix
                                         // for the round-3/GPT-5.6-Sol owned-notes-substitution exploit).
```

**`FrozenFrontier` — new in v6, Priority 2: structural (not conventional) enforcement of "never mutated."** v5's schema typed `treeFrontierAtN` as a bare `Schema.Uint8Array` and asserted, in prose, that it is "never mutated by anything downstream." Round 6 found that claim had no actual enforcement mechanism: `Object.freeze()` on a JS/TS typed array does **not** prevent writes to its indexed elements — per the ECMAScript spec, a `TypedArray`'s integer-indexed properties are exempt from the ordinary freeze semantics that block writes to regular object properties, a well-known JS gotcha. A `const` binding or a `readonly Uint8Array` TypeScript annotation is exactly as weak: both only prevent *reassigning the variable*, never prevent `bytes[i] = x` against the same underlying buffer. **Fixed with an actual defensive-copy accessor, not a stronger-sounding type annotation:**

```ts
class FrozenFrontier {
  readonly #bytes: Uint8Array;                 // private field, never exposed directly
  constructor(bytes: Uint8Array) { this.#bytes = bytes.slice(); }   // defensive copy IN, once, at construction
  get bytes(): Uint8Array { return this.#bytes.slice(); }           // defensive copy OUT, every read
  get byteLength(): number { return this.#bytes.length; }           // cheap reads that don't need a copy
}
```

Every reader of `sections.treeFrontierAtN.bytes` — `rehashFrontier`, `computeSnapshotRoot`, `verifyTailComplete` (below) — receives a **fresh copy** on every access, by construction. No caller, including a buggy or malicious future change to `verifyTailComplete`, can mutate the canonical stored bytes even by writing directly into what it was handed — the write lands on a throwaway copy, never on `#bytes`. This is what "never mutated" now means structurally, replacing the v4/v5 convention that had no enforcement behind it. `decodeSections` (§7.1(b)) is responsible for wrapping the raw decoded bytes in a `FrozenFrontier` exactly once, at decode time, before `sections` is ever handed to anything else.

**`seq` is no longer part of the envelope's serialized payload at all — v4 fix (Priorities 2+3, resolved together).** v3's schema above listed `seq: Schema.Number` as a field the caller was expected to embed into the envelope *before* calling `CheckpointStore.save()`. §7.3.1 below documents why that is unimplementable against the real `PgCheckpointStore.saveImpl` (verified this session against `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts:139-173`): `seq` is allocated *inside* `save()`'s own transaction, strictly after the caller has already handed over `data` to be chunked — there is no point before serialization at which the caller could know what `seq` will be. **Fixed by removing `seq` from the committed/serialized plaintext entirely, not by adding a reservation step to `CheckpointStore`.** `seq` was never an input to the `snapshotRoot` equation (§2.5.2 — check the equation: it isn't there), so nothing about Domain P's hash requires it to be embedded. `seq` remains meaningful only as (a) an attest-time witness (the `attest()` circuit computes its own `prev.seq + 1` internally regardless of anything the client supplies, §2.5.3/§8) and (b) a restore-time comparison value sourced from `CheckpointStore`'s own storage-native sequence metadata (`CheckpointSummary.sequence`/`CheckpointRecord.sequence`) rather than from decoded envelope bytes. **Correction (v6, Priority 5ii): the parenthetical this sentence originally carried here — "which the interface already returns today, no interface change needed" — was itself wrong and is removed.** `CheckpointStore.load()` does return `.sequence` on its own `CheckpointRecord`, but the *wrapper* class actually sitting in front of it, `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`, discards that value before returning to its own caller (verified directly against source, §3.6.1/§10 item 11) — so this claim was never true for the real call site `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` needs. See §3.6.1 for the actual required companion fix. See §7.1(b) for exactly how this is threaded through the restore predicate, and §7.3.1 for why this also cleanly resolves the AES-GCM nonce-reuse-under-abort defect without the two fixes conflicting.

**"Legacy" redefined against real source — v4 fix (Priority 8, GPT-5.6 Sol's finding, verified this session).** v3's text above defined legacy as "an envelope with no `envelopeVersion` field at all." **This was checked directly against `git grep -n "envelopeVersion" origin/main -- src/` and `origin/main:src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts` this session and found to be wrong.** The real, currently-shipping `WalletStateEnvelope` (`src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts:53,80`) already stamps every envelope with a **mandatory** `envelopeVersion: typeof ENVELOPE_VERSION` field — `export const ENVELOPE_VERSION = 1 as const` (line 51) — enforced both by the Zod shape schema (`envelopeVersion: z.number().int().positive()`, line 80) and by `decode()`'s separate version-value guard, which throws `EnvelopeVersionUnsupportedError` for anything other than the exact literal `1` (lines 102-108, 178-201). **No envelope with no `envelopeVersion` field has ever existed in this codebase's shipped format** — v3's "legacy = no version field" definition described a shape that does not correspond to any real envelope, past or present, and would have mis-routed every currently-deployed wallet's checkpoint: under v3's own guard (`envelope.envelopeVersion !== 2 || !envelope.anchor`), a real `envelopeVersion: 1` envelope fails the `!== 2` test exactly like a v2-claiming-but-corrupt envelope does, throwing `SnapshotEnvelopeUnverifiableError` from a path that was supposed to be the *fail-open* fix, not a new way to hard-brick every existing wallet's restore on first upgrade.

**Fixed:** "legacy" is redefined as **`envelopeVersion === 1`** (the real, current shape — three opaque sub-wallet strings, no anchor, no `snapshotRoot`, no `seq`) — not "no version field." The new anchor-bearing shape introduced by this design is `envelopeVersion === 2`. The real `decode()` in `src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts` must be widened, as part of implementation, from a single hardcoded `=== ENVELOPE_VERSION` equality guard to a small recognized-version dispatch: `1` → decode via the existing v1 `WalletStateEnvelopeSchema` (unchanged), route to `restoreLegacyUnverified()` (§7.1(d)); `2` → decode via the new v2 schema below, route to `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` (§7.1(b)). **Any envelope tagged with a value that is not `1` and not `2` — including one with a missing/non-numeric `envelopeVersion` entirely — is now correctly classified as genuinely malformed/corrupt input** (`EnvelopeCorruptError`/`EnvelopeVersionUnsupportedError`, a hard decode-time failure), not silently treated as "legacy." This is actually a *stricter*, more correct fail-closed posture than v3's text: v3 would have quietly accepted a fabricated version-less blob onto the unverified legacy path; v4 rejects anything that isn't a recognized real version outright. A malformed v2 envelope (claims `envelopeVersion: 2` but is missing/corrupt `anchor`) remains a hard schema-validation failure, not a silent fallback — unchanged from v3.

**Migration path, made concrete against the real schema:** on first post-upgrade `save()` of a wallet currently on `envelopeVersion: 1`, the SDK decodes the existing v1 envelope (three opaque sub-wallet strings), re-derives a fresh anchor/cursor/`endIndex`/`ownedNotesPlain`/etc. at the current sync tip (unchanged from v3's forced-re-anchor policy below), and writes it back out tagged `envelopeVersion: 2`. Until that first re-save happens, the wallet continues round-tripping through the real, existing `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore`/`decode()`/`encode()` path exactly as it does today — this design adds a new recognized version value to that dispatch, it does not require rewriting the v1 path.

**`seq`/`dbSeq` reconciliation — superseded text removed in v6 (Priority 5ii).** This subsection previously (v3/v4 text, left in place through v5 by oversight) asserted that the client drives `CheckpointStore.save()`'s internal `seq` and the `attest()` call's sequence witness "from the *same* locally-tracked counter" as an **invariant of correct operation**, with `candidateSeq === record.seq` always expected to hold and any mismatch treated as tamper evidence. That "lockstep" framing is exactly what §3.6.1 (added in v5) establishes has no durable protocol behind it and is not, in fact, an invariant: a save-succeeds/attest-fails partial failure or a concurrent multi-device attest race can leave the most-recently-*attested* checkpoint's `dbSeq` genuinely unequal to some other checkpoint's `dbSeq`, entirely without tampering — the "orphaned checkpoint" case §3.6.1 names as expected and non-fatal. Repeating the old "lockstep invariant, mismatch is tamper evidence" framing here, in the same document that specifies §3.6.1's tolerant reconciliation protocol a few sections later, directly contradicts it. **This paragraph's claim is superseded, not merely restated with new names** — see §2.5.3 for the current `dbSeq`/`attestOrdinal` split and §3.6.1 for the actual (tolerant-of-gaps) reconciliation protocol; §7.1(b)'s `record.dbSeq !== candidateSeq` check (v5) is a substitution/locator check for *the specific checkpoint being restored*, not a claim that `dbSeq` values are ever expected to form a lockstep sequence with anything else.

`buildSnapshot` reads `w.state.merkleTreeRoot` (already on `ledger.ZswapLocalState`, `ledger-v8.d.ts:2996`; dust via `commitmentTreeRoot()`/`generatingTreeRoot()`, `:1596,1601`) plus the block anchor from the new indexer field (7.2), and computes `snapshotRoot` per §2.5.3.

**Legacy migration policy:** on the first successful post-upgrade `save()` of a legacy wallet, the SDK forces a fresh full anchor capture (re-derives `R_N`/cursor/`endIndex` at the current sync tip) and writes `envelopeVersion: 2` — a **forced re-anchor on first post-upgrade save**. `SnapshotStorage` exposes `requiresReanchor(summary): boolean` so callers can surface this to users/telemetry.

**(b) `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` — renamed from `restoreVerified()`, and rewritten to actually implement its own flagship guarantee.** *Rewritten in v2 to fix item 6 (a real functional gap: the old sketch ran L0+finality+L1 only, took no `sk_attest`, ran no L3 check and no L2 sequence check, yet returned a bare `Promise<Wallet>` as though it had) — and to fix item 9 (all checks now consume one coupled `horizon` tuple, §4). Rewritten again in v3 to fix round-2 items 1 (L3 fetch was unauthenticated, present-but-mismatched silently downgraded), 2 (only `commitment`/`height` were checked, not the full `attestLeaf`), 3 (vk/statement pins were prose-only), 4 (`record.seq`/`envelope.seq` could silently diverge), 5 (`horizon`'s type was missing `R_N`/`endIndex`), and 6/Opus (the L1 tail check was a no-op because its upper bound was derived from the checkpoint's own block).*

**Rewritten a third time in v4 to fix the twice-confirmed, thrice-found core defect (Priority 1) plus four further round-3 findings (Priorities 4/5/9).** v3's version of this function still computed `expectedCommitment = persistentCommit(envelope.snapshotRoot, salt)` — trusting `envelope.snapshotRoot`, a plain transported string field the hostile DB itself controls — and loaded the returned wallet from a *separate* field (`envelope.deserialized`) with nothing cryptographically binding the two together, **despite §2.5.5's own prose already claiming the recomputation happened.** It didn't. **Concrete exploit (walked through in full in the report, restated here as the regression this rewrite must block):** a hostile DB serves the genuine, honestly-attested `envelope.snapshotRoot` string alongside a `envelope.deserialized` blob whose owned notes have been tampered — every v3 check passes (L0/L1 don't touch owned notes at all; L3's commitment check used the honest `snapshotRoot` string, which was never compared against anything derived from `deserialized`) — and the tampered wallet loads with `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"`. **Fixed structurally, not by adding another caveat:** there is no longer a separate trusted `envelope.snapshotRoot`/`envelope.deserialized` pair at all. A single canonical decode step (`decodeSections`, §2.5.4) turns the envelope's plaintext into one `sections` object; `snapshotRoot` is **always** recomputed from that exact object, never read from a transported field; and the `Wallet` returned is constructed from that **same** `sections` object — so "the data that was hashed into the recomputed root" and "the data the wallet is built from" are, by construction, the same reference, not two independently-populated fields that merely happen to agree in the honest case. `envelope.snapshotRootHint` (§7.1(a)) survives only as an optional, never-authoritative fast-fail cache.

**Rewritten a fourth time in v5 to fix the sections-mutation defect (Priority 1, GPT-5.6 Sol, round 5) and the seq/record.seq reconciliation gap (Priority 4).** v4's fix above was real but incomplete: it made the root recomputation and the wallet construction read from the *same reference* — but it never checked whether anything *between* those two reads **mutated that reference**. It did: v4's L1 step called `verifyTailComplete(sections.treeFrontier, ...)`, described in v4's own prose as mutating `sections.treeFrontier` "to reflect the tip," and this ran **before** `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` a few lines later. Since the on-chain `commitment` authenticates `snapshotRoot` **as of checkpoint N**, not the tip, this meant `computeSnapshotRoot` was hashing the wrong frontier for **every restore with a non-empty live tail** — i.e. every normal restore, since a checkpoint is by construction never taken at the current instant of the tip. This would have made the L3 commitment check fail for legitimate, honestly-attested restores (or, worse, silently pass if `computeSnapshotRoot`'s domain-separated hash happened to be checked against a similarly-recomputed-at-tip value somewhere — the design never specified that, so the honest failure mode is the design as specified). **Fixed by never mutating the field the root is computed from, full stop:** §7.1(a)'s field is renamed `treeFrontier` → `treeFrontierAtN` and `verifyTailComplete` is changed from an in-place mutator to a pure function that takes `sections.treeFrontierAtN` **by value** and **returns** a new, separately-named `advancedFrontier` value — it never writes back into `sections`. `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` is also moved earlier in the function body, immediately after the L0 checks pass and strictly before the L1 tail-verification step runs at all, so the ordering itself makes the invariant obvious by inspection: nothing that happens after `recomputedSnapshotRoot` is computed can possibly affect its value, because nothing after that point ever touches `sections.treeFrontierAtN` again. The wallet returned at the end is built from a **new** object, `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }`, so the returned wallet still benefits from the tail-verification work already done (its frontier reflects the tip, not just N) without that advancement ever leaking back into the value that was hashed for the L3 check.

**Rewritten a fifth time in v6 to fix the mixed-time wallet state v5's own fix (immediately above) introduced (Priority 2, GPT-5.6 Sol, round 6), and to stop treating `dbSeq` as a monotonicity signal (Priority 4).** v5's fix correctly stopped `advancedFrontier` from corrupting the *hashed* value (`recomputedSnapshotRoot`) — but it still used `advancedFrontier` to build the *returned wallet*, via `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }`. That wallet combines checkpoint-N-scoped `cursorPlain`/`ownedNotesPlain`/`nullifiersPlain`/everything-else with a tip-*advanced* frontier — a mixed-time object inconsistent with this design's own normal `[N, tip]` live-resume path (§1), which assumes a restore hands back a wallet **fully** at N and catches up from there through the *same* mechanism every restore already uses. Returning a frontier that has already silently absorbed the tail risks the live-resume path double-applying `[N, tip]`'s commitments against a frontier that already includes them, or — since this document never specified a distinct "already-tip-advanced" resume mode — leaves the actual behavior unspecified either way. **Two options were on the table: (a) discard `advancedFrontier` after using it only to *verify* the tail is complete, returning a wallet built entirely from unmodified `sections`, so every restore — whether or not L3 ran — ends up in the exact same N-scoped state and proceeds through the exact same `[N, tip]` catch-up; or (b) keep returning a tip-advanced wallet, but specify a complete, new, atomic tail-application mode that advances every wallet component (not just the frontier) in lockstep and is structurally distinguished from the normal resume path.** **Decision: (a).** It costs nothing new (the live-tail catch-up is §1's existing baseline, unconditionally required regardless of what `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` returns), it does not require inventing and auditing a second, parallel "partial-advance" wallet-construction mode whose interaction with every other component (owned-notes tracking, nullifier tracking, cursor) would need the same rigor this document has had to apply to the frontier alone across three rounds, and it makes every restore path — L0-only, L0+L1, L0+L1+L3 — converge on the identical invariant ("the returned wallet is exactly checkpoint N; the caller resumes forward") rather than L3-reaching restores getting a subtly different contract than the others. `verifyTailComplete` is changed again: it still reads `sections.treeFrontierAtN` by value and performs the identical collapsed-update-and-rehash check, but it no longer returns the advanced copy at all — it returns nothing (or throws `TailIncompleteError` on failure), a pure boolean-shaped validation. The wallet returned by `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` is built directly from `sections`, unconditionally. Traced through a concrete example below. **Separately, this rewrite also stops using `dbSeq` as an anti-rollback high-water-mark signal (Priority 4, §12 D14):** `assertSeqNotBelowHighestAccepted`/`updateLocalHighWaterMark` are replaced with height-keyed equivalents, because `dbSeq` reflects `CheckpointStore` save order (which can legitimately diverge from attestation-arrival order across devices with different attestation latency) while `height` is the one field the attestation contract's own CAS actually enforces as monotonic (§8) — see the traced Device A/B race below.

```ts
type VerificationLevel = "L0" | "L0+L1" | "L0+L1+L3";

interface HorizonTuple {                       // v3 (item 5): now carries the full tuple §4 returns
  blockHeight: number; blockHash: string; finalizedHash: string;
  R_N: string; endIndex: bigint;
}

interface AnchoredRestoreResult {
  wallet: Wallet;
  verificationLevel: VerificationLevel;      // callers can no longer mistake a partial-tier
                                              // restore for the full L3 guarantee
  horizon: { checkpoint: HorizonTuple; tip: HorizonTuple };   // v3: TWO horizons -- see below
  residuals: readonly string[];              // e.g. ["ciphertext-delivery-completeness (§5.0)",
                                              // "spend-hiding (§5.1)", "attest-time-honesty (§10.4)",
                                              // "owned-notes-base-at-N is attest-time-honesty-only (§2.5.5/§10.4)",
                                              // "L3-absence-is-federated-not-cryptographic (§7.1(b)/§10.9, v4)",
                                              // "tip-freshness-is-a-finalized-view-not-provably-the-latest (§10.2, v4)"]
}

// v4 (Priority 3): the caller supplies the CheckpointStore-native sequence metadata alongside the
// bytes, instead of `seq` being embedded inside the decoded plaintext (§7.1(a) -- seq cannot be
// known before serialization, verified against `saveImpl`'s real allocation order, §7.3.1).
// v5 CORRECTION (Priority 4): v4's comment claimed this is "exactly what CheckpointStore.load()/
// PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load() already return today -- no interface change... required." That
// claim was checked directly against source this session and is FALSE for the real wrapper class:
// `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()` reads `record.sequence` off the `CheckpointRecord` it gets
// from `checkpointStore.load()` but returns only the decoded `WalletStateEnvelope` -- `record.sequence`
// is silently discarded, never surfaced to its own caller. `storeSequence` below is therefore NOT
// available from the real call site today; widening `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`'s return
// shape (e.g. to `{ envelope, storeSequence }`) is a required, blocking companion implementation
// fix, out of this design document's own scope but named here as a concrete dependency rather than
// silently assumed already true -- see §10 item 11 and §12 D12.
static async restoreAnchoredCheckpoint(
  loaded: { serialized: string; storeSequence: CheckpointSequence;
            manifestMetadata: ManifestMetadata },   // v6 (Priority 3), NEW: the unencrypted per-manifest
                                                       // fields (envelopeVersion, encodingVersion, deviceId,
                                                       // hkdfSalt [v7, Priority 4], encKdfVersion,
                                                       // manifestSectionChunkCount, the chunk-hash list)
                                                       // CheckpointStore.load() already reads and verifies
                                                       // (§7.3, "always fully rehashes+verifies every chunk
                                                       // on load()") -- surfaced here so `computeFormatMetadataCommit`
                                                       // below (v7, REPLACES v6's `computeManifestHash`) can
                                                       // recompute the small format commitment without a
                                                       // second I/O round-trip; envelopeVersion/encodingVersion
                                                       // are the only two fields it actually reads (§2.5.3/§7.3.1)
  conn: {
    indexerHttpUrl: string; grandpaEndpoints: string[]; contractAddress: string;
    attestCircuitVkHash: Bytes32;            // v3 (item 3) -- typed, but see prose below (v4, Priority 6):
                                              // NOT enforced against chain in v1, no confirmed API exists
    attestStatementVersion: number;          // v3 (item 3) -- IS enforced, per record, below
    genesisHash: Bytes32;
  },
  identity: { skAttest: Bytes32 },           // required to derive the L3 pseudonym id
): Promise<AnchoredRestoreResult> {
  const envelope = deserializeEnvelope(loaded.serialized);
  if (envelope.envelopeVersion !== 2 || !envelope.anchor) {
    throw new SnapshotEnvelopeUnverifiableError();     // fail-closed (§7.1(a)/item 2), never silently downgrades
  }
  const anchor = envelope.anchor;

  // v4 (Priority 1, the core fix): ONE canonical decode, per §2.5.4's CDDL, into the Domain P
  // sections. Everything downstream -- the recomputed root AND the returned wallet -- reads from
  // THIS object. There is no second, independently-populated "envelope.deserialized" any more.
  // v5: `sections.treeFrontierAtN` (renamed from v4's `treeFrontier`) is NEVER mutated anywhere
  // below -- see the fourth-rewrite note above and the trace after this listing.
  const sections = decodeSections(envelope.sections, envelope.encodingVersion);

  // v3 (item 3): the vk pin is a property of the deployed CONTRACT, not of any one record --
  // checked once per session, not re-derived per restore (see prose below for what this can
  // and can't check today -- v4, Priority 6: honestly, today it can only check the former).
  await assertContractVkPinned(conn);

  // horizon #1: the CHECKPOINT's own block N -- used for L0's on-chain-agreement check, unchanged
  // in shape from v2's single-horizon design.
  const checkpointHorizon = await verifyFinalizedTuple(conn, anchor.blockHash);
  if (checkpointHorizon.blockHash !== anchor.blockHash) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();

  // L0a: offline self-consistency -- v5: operates on `sections.treeFrontierAtN`, the SAME,
  // NEVER-MUTATED field used below for computing the root and (in tip-advanced derived form only)
  // for constructing the wallet.
  const localRoot = rehashFrontier(sections.treeFrontierAtN);        // §"L0", the load-bearing fact
  if (localRoot !== anchor.zswapMerkleTreeRoot) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();
  // L0b: on-chain agreement -- against checkpointHorizon.R_N, not a second independently-fetched value
  if (checkpointHorizon.R_N !== anchor.zswapMerkleTreeRoot) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();
  // v4 (Priority 5): the missing lower-bound authentication for L1's tail scan. Without this, a
  // hostile envelope's `anchor.zswapEndIndex`/`anchor.blockHeight` (plain transported fields, same
  // trust problem as v3's `snapshotRoot`) could be inflated to shrink or empty out the tail range
  // L1 is about to scan, rubber-stamping "complete" over a truncated range. Both are now checked
  // against the CHAIN-DERIVED checkpointHorizon before anything downstream trusts them.
  if (checkpointHorizon.endIndex !== anchor.zswapEndIndex) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();
  if (checkpointHorizon.blockHeight !== anchor.blockHeight) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();
  // L0c: finality already checked inside verifyFinalizedTuple
  let level: VerificationLevel = "L0";

  // v5 (Priority 1, THE core fix, MOVED earlier): recomputed from `sections` -- specifically from
  // `sections.treeFrontierAtN` plus the other Domain P fields, per §2.5.2's equation and §2.5.4's
  // canonical encoding -- the moment L0 has confirmed `sections` is self-consistent with the
  // checkpoint's own anchor, and STRICTLY BEFORE anything below (in particular L1's tail
  // verification) runs at all. This ordering is itself the fix: nothing after this line can affect
  // `recomputedSnapshotRoot`'s value, because nothing after this line ever reads or writes
  // `sections.treeFrontierAtN` again. This is what actually blocks the owned-notes-substitution
  // exploit AND the sections-mutation defect together: there is no transported field to lie about
  // (v4's fix), and there is no later mutation of the hashed object to silently invalidate the
  // computation either (v5's fix).
  const recomputedSnapshotRoot = computeSnapshotRoot(sections);      // §2.5.2's H_dom(...) equation
  if (envelope.snapshotRootHint !== undefined && envelope.snapshotRootHint !== recomputedSnapshotRoot) {
    // Non-authoritative: a mismatch here is a useful early local-corruption signal (cheaper than
    // the on-chain round-trip below) but is NEVER itself a pass/fail security decision -- the
    // commitment equality below is authoritative regardless of whether this hint was even present.
    logLocalCorruptionSignal("snapshotRootHint mismatch");
  }

  // horizon #2 -- NEW in v3 (items 1 and 6): the CURRENT finalized TIP, fetched fresh and
  // independent of anything the checkpoint envelope itself claims. One fetch fixes two
  // previously-separate bugs:
  //  (item 6) L1's tail check now spans [anchor.zswapEndIndex, tipHorizon.endIndex) -- genuinely
  //    non-trivial. The v2 code used checkpointHorizon here, which is BY DEFINITION derived from
  //    the checkpoint's own block, making the range always empty -- a no-op disguised as a check.
  //  (item 1) the L3 attestation lookup below is authenticated against a FRESH finalized view,
  //    not left as a bare, freshness-blind query -- see fetchAuthenticatedAttestation.
  //  v4 (Priority 4): "fresh" here means "a genuinely-finalized view GRANDPA-verified in the same
  //    way as checkpointHorizon" -- it does NOT mean, and this design must not claim, "provably the
  //    chain's current latest finalized block." See the prose below and §10 item 2 for exactly what
  //    residual that leaves (an eclipsing endpoint serving an older-but-genuinely-finalized head).
  const claimedFinalizedHead = await fetchClaimedFinalizedHead(conn);  // untrusted CLAIM; the GRANDPA
                                                                         // justification inside
                                                                         // verifyFinalizedTuple is what
                                                                         // actually certifies it -- this
                                                                         // is the same "claim, then
                                                                         // independently verify" pattern
                                                                         // §4 already uses for claimedBlockHash
  const tipHorizon = await verifyFinalizedTuple(conn, claimedFinalizedHead);
  if (tipHorizon.blockHeight < checkpointHorizon.blockHeight) throw new SnapshotAnchorMismatchError();

  // L1: bounded-scan completeness. v6 (Priority 2, the mixed-time-wallet fix): verifyTailComplete is
  // now PURELY a VALIDATION check -- it reads `sections.treeFrontierAtN` BY VALUE, applies the
  // collapsed update to a local working copy, checks the copy rehashes to `tipHorizon.R_N`, and then
  // DISCARDS that working copy. It returns nothing (throws `TailIncompleteError` on failure). v5's
  // `advancedFrontier` return value is REMOVED -- see the fifth-rewrite note above for why returning
  // it produced a mixed-time wallet, and why discarding it (option (a)) is the fix, not merely a
  // reversion: this also makes verifyTailComplete's ONLY job "confirm the tail is complete," matching
  // its name, rather than "confirm the tail is complete AND hand back a value used for something else."
  await verifyTailComplete(sections.treeFrontierAtN, conn.indexerHttpUrl, anchor.zswapEndIndex, tipHorizon);
  level = "L0+L1";

  // v4 (Priority 3): candidateSeq is sourced from CheckpointStore's own storage-native sequence
  // metadata -- the value the storage layer itself returned alongside these bytes -- never from
  // decoded plaintext (§7.1(a): `seq` is no longer part of the serialized envelope at all). This is
  // still fully untrusted (the DB supplies it) -- it is cross-checked against the chain-authenticated
  // `record.dbSeq` below (v5, Priority 4 -- renamed from v4's overloaded `record.seq`) for SUBSTITUTION
  // detection ONLY -- see the v6 note just below for why it is never used for freshness/ordering.
  const candidateSeq = loaded.storeSequence;

  // L2: local anti-rollback HEIGHT check -- v6 (Priority 4): REPLACES v2-v5's dbSeq-keyed check.
  // `dbSeq` reflects CheckpointStore SAVE order, which can legitimately diverge from ATTESTATION-
  // arrival order across devices with different attestation latency (§12 D14's traced Device A/B
  // race) -- an honest, height-increasing attestation can carry a LOWER dbSeq than one it supersedes,
  // so comparing dbSeq against a local high-water mark can reject a perfectly legitimate, freshest-
  // available restore. `anchor.blockHeight` is used here instead: by this point in the function it has
  // ALREADY been cross-checked against the chain-derived `checkpointHorizon.blockHeight` (the L0 check
  // above), so it is not a bare DB-supplied claim -- it is a chain-corroborated value, strictly
  // stronger evidence than v5's raw `candidateSeq` (uncorroborated CheckpointStore storage metadata)
  // ever was for this specific purpose.
  assertHeightNotBelowHighestAccepted(anchor.blockHeight, loadLocalHighWaterMarkHeight());

  // L3: on-chain attestation check -- rewritten in v3 (items 1, 2, 3, 4), extended in v4, and in v5
  // (Priority 4) to use the new, explicit `dbSeq` witness instead of the overloaded `seq` field.
  const id = derivePseudonymId(identity.skAttest);
  // v3 (item 1), honesty-corrected in v4 (Priority 4): reads `attestations[id]` via a
  // state_getReadProof against tipHorizon.blockHash's OWN state_root for the PRESENT case -- that
  // part is real and sound, the same coupling discipline §4 uses for R_N/endIndex. The ABSENT case
  // is weaker than v3's comment claimed -- see fetchAuthenticatedAttestation's own doc comment and
  // §10 item 9 for exactly what "probe.present === false" does and does not prove today.
  const probe = await fetchAuthenticatedAttestation(conn, id, tipHorizon);

  if (probe.present) {
    const record = probe.record;

    // v5 (Priority 4): `record.dbSeq` is the NEW, EXPLICIT, client-disclosed witness naming exactly
    // which CheckpointStore-sequenced checkpoint this attestation is for (§2.5.3/§8) -- it is NOT
    // the contract's own internal `attestOrdinal` counter (v4's/v3's `seq`, renamed in v5 to make
    // the two roles impossible to conflate again). Because `dbSeq` is a value the client explicitly
    // supplies at attest-time for the checkpoint it is choosing to attest, it can never silently
    // drift from `candidateSeq`'s domain the way an internal, always-incrementing ordinal could --
    // see §3.6/§10 item 11 for the full reconciliation protocol this replaces.
    if (record.dbSeq !== candidateSeq) {
      throw new RollbackDetectedError("record.dbSeq != candidateSeq: substituted or stale blob");
    }
    // v3 (item 3): pinned statement version, enforced at the actual check site, not just documented.
    if (record.statementVersion !== conn.attestStatementVersion) {
      throw new PinnedStatementVersionMismatchError();
    }
    // v4 (Priority 9): explicit cross-checks, redundant with the full attestLeaf reconstruction
    // below but kept as direct, individually-diagnosable equality checks per the round-3 audit's
    // hardening request.
    if (record.height !== anchor.blockHeight) {
      throw new RollbackDetectedError("record.height != anchor.blockHeight: substituted or stale blob");
    }
    if (record.encodingVersion !== envelope.encodingVersion) {
      throw new RollbackDetectedError("record.encodingVersion != envelope.encodingVersion");
    }
    // v7 (Priorities 2+3), REPLACES v6's separate `manifestHash`-vs-`record.manifestHash` check.
    // Recompute the small, re-encryption-invariant format commitment from the ACTUALLY-LOADED
    // manifest metadata -- only `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` feed it (§7.3.1 point 7;
    // `encKdfVersion`/`manifestSectionChunkCount` are deliberately excluded -- they are already
    // self-detecting via AES-GCM's own authentication tag, see §7.3.1's "self-detecting vs.
    // needs-explicit-protection" analysis). This value is NOT compared against anything disclosed
    // in the clear -- it is folded into `expectedCommitment` below, exactly like `recomputedSnapshotRoot`,
    // so tampering it fails the SAME commitment-equality check that already gates everything else,
    // rather than a separate disclosed-witness comparison. There is no longer a `record.manifestHash`
    // field to compare against at all (§2.5.3/§8) -- `manifestHash` (Domain S, full chunk-hash-covering
    // value) was removed from `attestLeaf`/`AttestRecord` entirely in v7, closing both the privacy
    // leak and the key-rotation break round 6's mechanism introduced.
    const recomputedFormatMetadataCommit = computeFormatMetadataCommit(loaded.manifestMetadata);   // §7.3.1 point 7

    // v5 (Priority 4): salt derivation keys off `attestOrdinal` (renamed from the overloaded `seq`)
    // -- its role as hiding-commitment randomness is unchanged from v3/v4, only the name changed to
    // stop implying it doubles as the checkpoint locator. `record.attestOrdinal` is available here
    // because `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation` returns the whole on-chain record, exactly as before.
    const salt = deriveSalt(identity.skAttest, record.attestOrdinal);
    // `recomputedSnapshotRoot` was already computed above, BEFORE L1 ran -- reused here unchanged,
    // never recomputed at this point. This is what makes the v5 fix's correctness independent of
    // where in the function this L3 block happens to run. v7: `recomputedFormatMetadataCommit` is
    // folded in alongside it, matching §2.5.3's `commitment := persistentCommit(snapshotRoot,
    // formatMetadataCommit, salt)` equation exactly -- a tampered `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`
    // in the loaded manifest metadata now changes THIS value, which fails the existing
    // `record.commitment === expectedCommitment` check below, with no separate check needed.
    const expectedCommitment = persistentCommit(recomputedSnapshotRoot, recomputedFormatMetadataCommit, salt);

    // v3 (item 2): reconstruct the FULL attestLeaf per §2.5.3's canonical equation -- genesis/
    // network id, wallet kind, block hash/height, tree root, end index, encoding version,
    // statement version, dbSeq, attestOrdinal, previous commitment -- not just `commitment`/`height`.
    // v5: binds `dbSeq` and `attestOrdinal` explicitly (Priority 4). v7: `manifestHash` REMOVED (was
    // bound directly here in v6) -- format-metadata tamper-evidence now flows through `commitment`
    // itself, above, not through a separate disclosed attestLeaf field.
    const expectedLeaf = attestLeafHash({
      genesisHash: conn.genesisHash, walletKindTag: envelope.walletKindTag, id,
      encodingVersion: envelope.encodingVersion, blockHash: anchor.blockHash,
      blockHeight: anchor.blockHeight, R_N: anchor.zswapMerkleTreeRoot, endIndex: anchor.zswapEndIndex,
      commitment: expectedCommitment, dbSeq: record.dbSeq, attestOrdinal: record.attestOrdinal,
      prevCommitment: record.prevCommitment, statementVersion: record.statementVersion,
    });

    const matches = record.attestLeaf === expectedLeaf
      && record.commitment === expectedCommitment
      && record.height <= tipHorizon.blockHeight;

    if (!matches) {
      // v3 (item 1b): PRESENT-but-mismatched is a distinct, hard-failing path -- a positive
      // rollback/substitution signal per §3.6's own divergence definition -- never a silent
      // downgrade the way genuine absence is.
      throw new RollbackDetectedError("attestation record present but does not match this envelope");
    }

    level = "L0+L1+L3";
    // v6 (Priority 4): height-keyed, NOT dbSeq-keyed -- REPLACES v5's `updateLocalHighWaterMark
    // (record.dbSeq, tipHorizon.blockHeight)`. `record.height` is the contract-CAS-enforced
    // monotonic value (§8); it is provably equal to `anchor.blockHeight` by the explicit cross-check
    // a few lines above, so using either is equivalent here -- `record.height` is used for clarity
    // that this is the CHAIN-ATTESTED value, not a DB-supplied one. See §12 D14 for the traced race
    // this replacement resolves.
    updateLocalHighWaterMarkHeight(record.height, record.attestOrdinal);
  }
  // else: probe did not return a present record -- v4 (Priority 4): this is the FIRST-EVER-attestation
  // case in the common/expected sense, but it is only as trustworthy as fetchAuthenticatedAttestation's
  // absence handling actually is -- see that function's doc comment. Still the only case that
  // downgrades silently to "L0+L1", now clearly distinguished from a present-but-mismatched record.

  // v6 (Priority 2, the mixed-time-wallet fix): the wallet is built DIRECTLY from `sections`,
  // UNMODIFIED -- the exact object `recomputedSnapshotRoot` was hashed from above, with no field
  // substituted. This REPLACES v5's `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }` construction:
  // there is no more `advancedFrontier` to substitute (L1, above, is now validation-only and returns
  // nothing). The returned wallet is fully checkpoint-N-scoped, for every verificationLevel alike --
  // "L0", "L0+L1", and "L0+L1+L3" restores all return the SAME KIND of object (differing only in how
  // much of it has been independently checked), and the caller proceeds through the SAME `[N, tip]`
  // live-catch-up mechanism (§1's baseline, §3.6's verified-at-finalized-head -> caught-up transition)
  // regardless of which verificationLevel it received. This is what "resolves the mixed-time state"
  // means concretely: there is no longer a special-cased tip-advanced substitution for the L3 path to
  // diverge from the L0/L0+L1 paths' contract.
  const wallet = await startFirst(Wallet, sections);
  return {
    wallet, verificationLevel: level,
    horizon: { checkpoint: checkpointHorizon, tip: tipHorizon },
    residuals: RESIDUALS_FOR[level],   // L3-reaching levels include the §2.5.5 owned-notes-base residual
                                        // AND (v4) the L3-absence/tip-freshness residuals named above
  };
}
```

**Trace: a concrete non-empty-tail restore, updated for v6's discard-`advancedFrontier` fix (Priority 2).** Let checkpoint N = block 1,000 (`anchor.zswapEndIndex = 5_000`, i.e. 5,000 leaves in the zswap tree at N) and the current finalized tip = block 1,200 (`tipHorizon.endIndex = 5_400`, i.e. 400 more leaves have landed since N — a genuinely non-empty `[N, tip]` tail, the normal case for any restore that isn't instantaneous). Walk the function above against this scenario:

1. `sections = decodeSections(...)` decodes `sections.treeFrontierAtN` as the **5,000-leaf** frontier — exactly what was serialized into the envelope at N, untouched by anything that happens later, and (v6) wrapped in `FrozenFrontier` so no downstream reader can mutate it even by accident.
2. L0a: `rehashFrontier(sections.treeFrontierAtN.bytes)` rehashes those same 5,000 leaves (a defensive copy, per `FrozenFrontier`) and compares against `anchor.zswapMerkleTreeRoot` — the root the chain committed **at block 1,000**. Matches, by construction.
3. `recomputedSnapshotRoot = computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` runs **here**, reading the still-5,000-leaf frontier plus the other Domain P sections, and produces the **N-scoped** semantic root — the exact value the on-chain `commitment` authenticates.
4. `tipHorizon` is fetched (endIndex 5,400). L1 calls `verifyTailComplete(sections.treeFrontierAtN, ..., 5_000, tipHorizon)` — this reads the 5,000-leaf frontier **by value** (via `.bytes`, a fresh copy), applies the collapsed update for `[5_000, 5_400)` to that **local working copy**, checks the copy's rehash equals `tipHorizon.R_N`, and — **v6 change** — **discards the working copy** rather than returning it. The function's only externally-visible effect is "passed" or `throw TailIncompleteError`. `sections.treeFrontierAtN` is unaffected either way (it always was, under v5's fix too — the v6 change is about what happens to the *result* of the tail-scan, not about re-litigating v5's mutation fix).
5. The L3 step derives `expectedCommitment` from `recomputedSnapshotRoot` — computed in step 3, unaffected by step 4. This equals the on-chain `commitment` for a genuinely honest checkpoint, so the L3 equality check **passes**.
6. **v6 change from here on:** the returned wallet is built from `sections` **directly**, still 5,000-leaf-scoped — not from a 5,400-leaf `advancedFrontier` substitution. The function returns with `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"` and a wallet that is, deliberately, exactly the checkpoint-N state. **The caller now performs the SAME `[N, tip]` live incremental sync every restore already requires (§1's baseline)** — applying the `[5_000, 5_400)` collapsed update *again*, this time through the wallet's normal, already-existing resume/catch-up code path (`Sync.ts`'s `resumeFrom`, unchanged, §7.1(b) closing prose), not through a bespoke substitution invented inside `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`. This is mildly less "free" than v5's approach (the collapsed-update computation genuinely happens twice — once inside `verifyTailComplete`'s validation, once inside the normal resume path) but is the direct trade this design makes for consistency: every restore, regardless of `verificationLevel`, ends in the identical `verified-at-finalized-head` state (§3.6) and reaches `caught-up` through the identical mechanism, with no second, parallel "tail already applied" wallet shape for any code (present or future) to have to special-case.

**`fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s absence-proof mechanism — honesty-corrected in v4 (Priority 4, GPT-5.6 Sol's finding).** v3's comment claimed `probe.present === false` is "a cryptographically backed 'genuinely absent,' not merely 'this endpoint chose not to return one.'" **No concrete mechanism for that claim was ever specified, and this document should not have implied one exists.** What a `state_getReadProof` against `tipHorizon.blockHash`'s state root can genuinely authenticate today is: (a) a **top-level** read — e.g. `pallet_midnight::StateKey` — checked against the header's own `state_root`, exactly as §4's `verifyFinalizedTuple` already does for `R_N`/`endIndex`; that part is real and already specified. What it would take to authenticate *absence of one specific key* (`attestations[id]`) inside a Compact contract's own `Map` ledger field is a **second, deeper traversal** — from the contract's state root down into whatever trie/MPT encoding the Compact compiler uses for `Map` fields, producing a genuine non-membership proof for `id` specifically. **This document never specified that second traversal, and — checked against this same document's own §5.1 item 2 — for the closest analogous structure (the nullifier set) it explicitly says the underlying primitive doesn't have an exposed API yet: "`merkle_patricia_trie.rs` has `insert/lookup/remove` but no `prove`/`verify`."** There is no evidence in briefs 01–11 that Compact-level `Map` non-membership proofs are available today either. **Honest v1 scoping, not a claimed close:**
- The **present** case is real: a `state_getReadProof`-backed inclusion check for `attestations[id]` against `tipHorizon`'s state root, same discipline as the rest of §4. Nothing about this case is weakened in v4.
- The **absent** case has no cryptographic non-membership primitive available in v1. `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation` degrades to a **Tier-0-style k-of-n cross-check** for this case only — query ≥2 independently-operated endpoints for `attestations[id]` at `tipHorizon` and require all of them to agree the key is absent, mirroring the existing Tier-0 finality fallback (§4) rather than inventing a new trust model. This is **federated, bounded trust** for the absence claim specifically, not a reduction to a consensus commitment — named exactly as such, not dressed up as "cryptographically backed."
- This is carried forward as a new, explicit §10 residual (item 9) and as a `residuals` entry on any `AnchoredRestoreResult` at `"L0+L1"` (i.e. every restore that took the silent-absence branch), so callers cannot mistake "no attestation found" for "provably no attestation exists."
- **If/when a genuine Compact-level Map non-membership primitive becomes available** (the same primitive gap named for nullifiers in §5.1), `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s absent case should be upgraded to use it directly — this is a named future improvement, not assumed to already exist.

**"Fresh tip" tightened — v4 (Priority 4, GPT-5.6 Sol's finding).** `verifyFinalizedTuple(conn, claimedFinalizedHead)` proves `claimedFinalizedHead` genuinely **is** a finalized block (the GRANDPA justification check is real and sound for that claim) — it does **not** prove `claimedFinalizedHead` is the chain's current **latest** finalized block. An eclipsing or stale endpoint can serve a genuinely-finalized-but-older head, complete with a valid justification and (per the point above) a valid absence proof for *that* older state — the wallet would correctly conclude "no attestation exists as of this finalized block," which is true, while a newer attestation (or a newer rollback-relevant record) exists past the point this endpoint chose to show. Every place this document says "fresh finalized view" or "current finalized tip" means precisely "a block this restore independently verified as finalized," not "provably the most recent one the network has finalized" — that stronger claim would require either a live/continuously-updated light-client session (Tier-2, deferred, §4) or multi-endpoint height cross-checking to catch an endpoint serving a suspiciously-stale-but-valid tip. **v1 mitigation, named not hidden:** the Tier-0 k-of-n cross-check above (for L3 absence) and the existing Tier-0 fallback (for finality generally, §4) both incidentally raise the bar against a single stale-serving endpoint, but neither closes it to a cryptographic guarantee. §10 item 2 is updated to state this precisely.

**`assertContractVkPinned` — honesty-corrected in v4 (Priority 6, GPT-5.6 Sol's finding, plus prior rounds).** v3's text above presented this as a conditional check — "if the API exists, hard-fail on mismatch; if not, fall back to structural" — worded in a way that let `conn.attestCircuitVkHash` look like it does real verification work in the common case. **It does not, as of this writing, and this document should say so plainly rather than leave a field that looks load-bearing but isn't.** No per-contract deployed-verifier-key-hash chain-read API has been confirmed to exist on Midnight as of this design (this is still an open item on §12's Secondary list — "whether the node/ledger actually exposes a per-contract deployed-verifier-key-hash read... needs confirming... flagged rather than assumed" — and no evidence surfaced in any research brief 01–11 that one does). **Given that, v1 ships `assertContractVkPinned` as a structural-only check, full stop:** it verifies the client is configured to talk to the single hard-pinned `conn.contractAddress` (§3.5) and nothing else. **`conn.attestCircuitVkHash` is retained in the config type as a forward-compatible placeholder — typed, threaded through, but NOT consulted by any check in v1.** If a genuine per-contract vk-hash read is later confirmed to exist (or is added to Midnight's contract-state API), `assertContractVkPinned` should be upgraded at that point to actually query and hard-fail against it — but that upgrade is not built, and this document must not claim it is. `attestStatementVersion` is different and unaffected: it *is* a concrete per-record value the L3 step in §7.1(b) actually checks against `record.statementVersion` at every restore, so that half of the "prose-only" gap genuinely is closed. **This is now named explicitly as a §10 residual** (see §10 item 4's vk/contract-pin sub-bullet): v1's protection against a substituted attestation *circuit* (as opposed to a substituted attestation *contract address*, which the structural check does catch) rests entirely on the immutable-pin-plus-audited-client-software argument of §3.5, not on any on-chain vk-hash comparison — because no such comparison is currently implementable.

This is a gate in front of the existing resume path — no change to `Sync.ts`'s `resumeFrom` (brief 04 §4b). It finally *calls* `applyCollapsedUpdate`, which the ledger crate exposes but the wallet never invokes (brief 04 §2, brief 06 §7). Once `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"` is returned, the wallet transitions to `verified-at-finalized-head` in §3.6's state machine; callers proceed through `caught-up → active` and must wire in §3.6's periodic/pre-spend recheck.

**(c) `SnapshotStorage` interface** — mirror the reader/writer split of the existing `TransactionHistoryStorage` (`abstractions/src/TransactionHistoryStorage.ts:215-216`), which is a plain injected interface with **no in-memory assumption baked in**. Today the `serialize()`/`restore()` blob is a bare `string` the caller must persist itself — there is no pluggable snapshot-storage seam the way there is for tx-history (brief 04 §4c). Adding `SnapshotStorage` lets UmbraDB back *both* snapshot and tx-history through one facade constructor arg.

**(d) `restoreLegacyUnverified()` — new in v2, the explicit unverified path required by item 2. Extended in v3 (item 11) with a pre-restore L3 pointer probe, closing the legacy-downgrade risk. Corrected in v4 (Priority 8) to target the real legacy shape.** A separately-named static factory for envelopes tagged `envelopeVersion === 1` — the real, currently-shipping shape (`src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts`, `ENVELOPE_VERSION = 1`), not "no `envelopeVersion` field," which v3 asserted but which does not correspond to anything the real codebase has ever produced (verified this session, §7.1(a)):

**The v3 gap this closes:** a hostile DB could serve a legacy-shaped (anchor-less) envelope to a wallet that in fact *has* a real, valid on-chain attestation — forcing it through this unverified path even though `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` was genuinely available and would have caught a rollback. Nothing about an envelope's own claimed shape should be trusted to decide how much verification the wallet gets, since that shape is exactly what a hostile DB controls. **Fixed:** when `identity.skAttest` is available, this path now performs an independent, cheap pre-restore probe of the L3 pointer *before* accepting the legacy path, refusing to proceed silently if a real record is found:

```ts
static async restoreLegacyUnverified(
  serialized: string,
  conn?: { indexerHttpUrl: string; grandpaEndpoints: string[]; contractAddress: string; genesisHash: Bytes32 },
  identity?: { skAttest: Bytes32 },        // NEW v3 (item 11) -- optional: legacy callers that
                                            // genuinely have no key material yet can't run this
                                            // probe, and that gap is named below, not hidden
): Promise<{ wallet: Wallet }> {
  if (conn && identity) {
    // v3 (item 11): independent of anything the envelope itself claims -- a hostile DB cannot
    // downgrade a wallet that HAS a real attestation just by serving an anchor-less blob, because
    // this probe doesn't consult the envelope at all.
    const tipHorizon = await verifyFinalizedTuple(conn, await fetchClaimedFinalizedHead(conn));
    const id = derivePseudonymId(identity.skAttest);
    const probe = await fetchAuthenticatedAttestation(conn, id, tipHorizon);
    if (probe.present) {
      // a real on-chain record exists for this wallet -- refuse the unverified path outright;
      // the caller must obtain a v2 envelope and use restoreAnchoredCheckpoint() instead.
      throw new LegacyRestoreRefusedError(
        "on-chain attestation exists for this wallet -- legacy/unverified restore is refused; " +
        "obtain a v2 envelope and use restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()",
      );
    }
  }
  // No conn/identity supplied, OR the probe found genuine absence: proceed unverified. The
  // no-conn/no-identity case is a named residual, not a silent gap -- see prose below.
  const deserialized = deserializeLegacy(serialized);   // the pre-v2 shape only
  // deliberately NO anchor/finality/L1/L3 checks -- there is nothing to check against
  return { wallet: await startFirst(Wallet, deserialized) };
}
```

This return type has **no** `verificationLevel` field at all — it cannot be confused, structurally, with a verified result. Callers are expected to flag wallets restored this way for a forced re-anchor at next save (§7.1(a)'s migration policy) and, if the deployment is remote/untrusted, to treat the restored state as unverified until that re-anchor completes.

**Named residual (v3, item 11; characterization corrected in v4, Priority 9 — GPT-5.6 Sol's finding.)** The pre-restore probe requires the *caller* to supply `identity.skAttest` — a wallet that genuinely has no key material available yet (e.g. very first-ever restore before any keys are derived) cannot run it, and in that specific case this path still proceeds unverified with no independent check, same as before v3. **v3's text went further and claimed this gap is "vacuous" for any case other than a genuinely-keyless from-scratch wallet — that overclaims and is corrected here.** The gap is *not* limited to the from-scratch case: nothing about `restoreLegacyUnverified`'s signature *requires* the caller to pass `identity` even when the wallet in question does, in fact, have real on-chain attestation history and the caller does, in fact, have `skAttest` available — a caller that simply omits the optional `identity` argument (a missed integration, a code path that hasn't been threaded through yet, a caller intentionally choosing the cheaper unverified path) hits the exact same no-probe branch as a genuinely keyless wallet, silently, even though a real attestation exists and the probe *could* have caught a downgrade. **This is not closed by this design** — it is an API-shape residual (the check is opt-in via an optional parameter, not enforced), named honestly here rather than characterized as vacuous. Mitigation is process/caller-discipline (SDK callers restoring an existing wallet should always thread `identity` through when it is available), not a cryptographic guarantee; §10 carries this forward as an explicit sub-item.

### 7.2 Indexer PR — `midnight-indexer` (additive, `@beta` where dust)

- **`TreeAnchor` on the ledger-event types** — the prerequisite reverse map. A restoring wallet has an event-cursor `appliedIndex`, not an endIndex/height; there is no field today mapping "event id → the committed root when I reached it" (brief 04 §2). Add `zswapAnchor: TreeAnchor!` on `ZswapLedgerEvent` (and `@beta` dust variants) via a `#[ComplexObject]` resolver following the existing FK chain `ledger_events → transactions → regular_transactions` — the anchor columns (`zswap_merkle_tree_root`, `zswap_start/end_index`, dust indices) **already exist**, so **zero new migration** (brief 04 §3, `indexer-common/migrations/postgres/001_initial.sql:47-59`):
  ```graphql
  type TreeAnchor { endIndex: Int!, root: HexEncoded!, block: Block! }
  ```
- **`unshieldedUtxos(address, offset): UnshieldedUtxoProof`** — the genuinely new authenticated surface, **Tier-F / federated-quorum trust per §2.6**, not consensus-reduced. **Not** a bare `[UnshieldedUtxo!]!` (that carries no completeness proof) but `{ utxos, boundaryLo, boundaryHi, merklePaths, root, rootSignature }` (brief 06 §4.3, §7). Needs the new MB-tree materialized view (§4.2 of brief 06), a signer (Signed-Tree-Head), and ideally a monitor cross-checking `R_utxo` against the consensus utxo-subtree root. `R_utxo` anchoring options, honestly ranked (brief 06 §4.4): (1) whole-set root-match vs the `utxo`-subtree root in `midnight_ledgerStateRoot` — strongest, would be consensus-reduced, but needs the node to expose that root + an MPT serialization the wallet can rehash (doesn't exist today); (2) **signed STH + monitor cross-check + k≥2 indexers — Tier-F, v1's actual mechanism**; (3) consensus change — cleanest, deferred.
- **CI:** weave both into `native_e2e.rs` (byte-identical reference stream vs a real `midnight-node` container) and the `qa/tests` schema-introspection/deprecation smoke test (brief 04 §5). Signed CLA + Apache-2.0 headers (brief 04 §5).

### 7.3 The UmbraDB persistence substrate

*Corrected in v2: the v1 draft's claims about encryption status and the `manifestHash`/`snapshotRoot` relationship were both wrong; both are fixed here, cross-referencing §2.5 and §7.3.1.*

- **`CheckpointStore`** (`src/interfaces/checkpoint-store.ts`) is content-addressed, chunked, and **always fully rehashes+verifies every chunk on `load()`** before returning (throwing `ChunkIntegrityError`/`ChunkMissingError`/`ManifestCorruptError`). Verified directly against `git show origin/main:src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts`: `PgCheckpointStore.save()` splits `data` into chunks, SHA-256s each chunk, SHA-256s the ordered chunk-hash list into `manifestHash`, and stores the **raw bytes as given** — no encryption step exists in this file or anywhere else in the checkpoint path today. `manifestHash` is a **Domain S (storage/ciphertext-when-encryption-ships)** value per §2.5.2 — it is **not** the same value as, and must never be substituted for, the **Domain P** `snapshotRoot` that L3 actually attests to. (The v1 draft's claim that "its `manifestHash` … is exactly the `snapshotRoot`" is retracted; see §2.5.1 for why that equation was actively harmful.) Its per-`(walletId,networkId)` monotonic `CheckpointSequence` is the natural home for §2.5.3's `dbSeq` field (v5, renamed from the stale `seq` reference this sentence previously carried — corrected in v6, Priority 5iii) — a **storage locator only** (§7.1(b)/§3.6, v6 Priority 4): L2's own anti-rollback high-water mark is keyed on chain-validated `height`, not on `dbSeq`, since `dbSeq` does not carry a monotonicity guarantee across devices (§12 D14).
- **Sprint-7 `PgTransactionHistoryStorage`** implements the SDK's `TransactionHistoryStorage<WalletEntry>` — brief 04 §4c confirms this needs **zero SDK change** (the interface is unprivileged and injected). The new `SnapshotStorage` (7.1c) is the symmetric seam for the snapshot blob itself.
- The **CheckpointStore `WalletState` envelope** carries the serialized local state + the new L0 anchor manifest + the Domain P sections `snapshotRoot` is recomputed from (§2.5.2, §7.1(a) — no longer a transported `snapshotRoot` field) as one atomic unit; L2's AES-GCM (§7.3.1, **not yet implemented — v1 blocking requirement**) encrypts each chunk **inside** `saveImpl`'s own atomic transaction, after chunking and after `seq` **and** `nonceBase` allocation (v3 item 7 for the ordering, v4 Priorities 2+3 for why nonce material is now a *second*, non-transactional allocation distinct from `seq` — see §7.3.1); L3's attestation commits `snapshotRoot` (Domain P), never `manifestHash` (Domain S).

### 7.3.1 AES-256-GCM v1 requirement — new in v2, replaces the retracted "already implemented" claim (item 10); construction fixed and sequence-ordering verified in v3 (item 7); nonce-reuse-under-abort defect fixed and seq-embedding defect resolved together in v4 (Priorities 2+3); nonce source moved fully client-side and AAD circular dependency fixed in v5 (Priorities 2+3); construction restructured around per-device key separation and manifest authentication added in v6 (Priorities 1+3); **the local-store-restore beacon redesigned around a genuinely evolving mirrored counter (round 6's own beacon found structurally broken by an identical concrete counterexample from 2 of 3 reviewers), manifest authentication redesigned around a small re-encryption-invariant format commitment instead of the ciphertext-covering `manifestHash` (closing a privacy leak and a key-rotation break round 6's own fix introduced), KDF/bootstrap metadata completed, and the padding scheme finalized byte-exactly in v7 (Priorities 1, 2, 3, 4, 6)**

**The v3 construction's defect (GPT-5.6 Sol's finding, round 3 — CRITICAL, a real AES-GCM nonce-reuse vulnerability, not theoretical).** v3 derived the per-chunk nonce as `uint64(seq) || uint32(chunkIndex)`, with `seq` coming from the SAME `ckpt_sequence_counters` atomic upsert-increment `saveImpl` already uses, allocated *inside* the same transaction that inserts the (now-to-be-encrypted) chunk rows. The exploit: chunks for attempt 1 are encrypted using a nonce derived from `seq = 42` and `INSERT`ed — a hostile DB/operator, simply by being the party the `INSERT ... VALUES (...)` statements are executed against, can observe that ciphertext **regardless of whether the surrounding transaction ever commits.** If a *later* statement in that same transaction then fails for any reason (constraint violation, connection drop, deadlock, an aborted `AbortSignal`) the whole transaction rolls back — **including the `ckpt_sequence_counters` row**, because it was incremented inside the same transaction. The very next `save()` attempt — for the same or different plaintext — allocates `seq = 42` again, unaware attempt 1 ever touched it, and re-encrypts under the identical nonce `uint64(42) || uint32(chunkIndex)` and the same key. **Two different ciphertexts under the same (key, nonce) pair is the textbook AES-GCM catastrophic failure** — it can leak the authentication subkey `H` and, from there, forge authentication tags for arbitrary future ciphertext under that key. v3's own construction notes ("gapless and monotonic under concurrency by construction... an aborted `save()` never burns a sequence number") *documents the exact mechanism* that makes the reuse possible, without noticing it does.

**v4's fix (a dedicated, non-transactional `ckpt_nonce_ctr` Postgres `SEQUENCE`) did not actually establish "never reissued, forever," and round 5 found two independent reasons why (Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, converging from opposite directions).** v4 reasoned that `nextval()` on a native `SEQUENCE` is non-transactional (true, standard documented Postgres behavior) and concluded `nonceBase` could therefore never repeat. Two gaps survived:

1. **Hostile-DB framing (Fable 5).** The DB is this design's own named adversary throughout (L2 = remote/untrusted-DB hardening, §2). A malicious DB operator does not need to exploit any real Postgres crash-recovery subtlety at all — it can simply **lie about, or directly manipulate, what `nextval('ckpt_nonce_ctr')` returns** (return a previously-seen value, or run `setval()` to rewind the sequence) if that operator controls the Postgres instance itself, which this design's own threat model already assumes it might. Any DB-supplied value, however it is generated inside a *genuine* Postgres instance, is not trustworthy nonce material against a DB that is itself the adversary.
2. **Honest-Postgres framing (GPT-5.6 Sol, with a real citation) — strictly worse, since it needs no adversary at all.** PostgreSQL's own documentation for `CREATE SEQUENCE`/sequence behavior warns that a sequence's cached/advanced state can be left in an uncertain condition if a crash occurs before the sequence's own advancement is durably flushed to disk — sequences are optimized for throughput specifically by *not* being fully crash-safe in the way ordinary table rows inside a transaction are. This means even a **fully honest, non-malicious** Postgres instance, on an ungraceful crash/restart at the wrong moment, could re-issue a previously-allocated `nonceBase` — no hostile behavior required, just normal operational reality for a production database.

Both findings point the same direction: **the DB must not be in the nonce-generation trust path at all**, in either direction (nonce material neither supplied by, nor trusted from, nor durable-because-of the DB).

**v5's fix (client-side `deviceId`‖`localCounter` nonce material) removed the DB from the trust path correctly, but round 6 found its own probability claim was backwards, not merely imprecise (Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, independently computed, converging exactly).** v5 computed `P(deviceId collision) ≈ 4.66×10⁻⁸` for a realistic `D = 20`-device wallet lifetime and asserted this "comfortably clears NIST's ≤2⁻³² collision-probability guidance." **Recomputed and verified this session:** `4.66×10⁻⁸ ÷ 2.33×10⁻¹⁰ (= 2⁻³²) ≈ 200`. v5's own number was **~200× above (worse than)** the bound it claimed to clear — the arithmetic that produced `4.66×10⁻⁸` was correct, but the sentence characterizing what that number means relative to `2⁻³²` had the comparison backwards. Separately, v5's claim that requiring matching `localCounter` values "narrows the probability further" was also wrong: `localCounter` starts at the same value (0) on every device and increments once per save in the same order events occur, so two devices that happen to share a `deviceId` do not merely become *more likely* to eventually collide — they collide **immediately, on the first save either makes** (`nonceBase = deviceId‖1` for both), because their counters are in lockstep from the start. Conditioning on `deviceId` collision does not narrow anything; it is already the whole event.

**Fixed in v6 — `deviceId` is bound into key derivation, not relied on purely as nonce-space partitioning, dissolving the shared-key nonce-collision question rather than re-tuning the same probability target (Priority 1, both reviewers' suggested direction).** The root cause of needing a birthday-bound argument at all was that v5 (like v4 before it) had every device encrypt under **one shared key**, so any two devices' nonce spaces had to be kept disjoint by construction — which is exactly what a birthday bound over `deviceId` is a bound *on the failure of*. v6 instead gives each device its **own derived key**, via HKDF domain separation on `deviceId` (§7.3.1 point 4 below). Under distinct keys, AES-GCM's nonce-uniqueness requirement — the property NIST's `≤2⁻³²` guidance is about — simply does not apply *across* devices at all: nonce reuse is only a security-relevant event *within a single key*. This removes the multi-device nonce-collision question as a probabilistic argument and replaces it with a structural one: the only way two devices could ever nonce-collide is if they first **key**-collide, i.e. draw the identical `deviceId` — a strictly rarer, and now separately and precisely bounded, event (below).

1. **A per-device, per-`(walletId, networkId)` state pair, held in the same trusted local store this design already assumes for the L2 anti-rollback high-water mark (§2 L2 bullet 2):**
   - `deviceId` — a **128-bit** (widened from v5's 32-bit — Priority 1), cryptographically-random value, generated **once**, the first time this device ever encrypts a checkpoint for this `(walletId, networkId)`, and persisted durably. The width increase is deliberate hygiene on top of the structural key-separation fix, not a substitute for it (see the corrected math below) — 128 bits is comfortably within the "sufficiently large random fixed field" NIST SP 800-38D §8.2.1 calls for in a deterministic-construction nonce scheme, so a `deviceId` collision is negligible even considered on its own, before the key-separation argument is invoked at all. Regenerated whenever this device's own trusted local store is detected to have been restored from a backup rather than continuing fresh (§7.3.1's local-store-restore defense, below, **rewritten in v7 — see below**) — this is the fix for the separate, independently-found (Opus/Fable 5/GPT-5.6 Sol, 3/3) restore-from-backup vector.
   - `localCounter` — a **64-bit** (widened from v5's 32-bit) monotonic counter, starting at 0, incremented and **durably fsynced BEFORE** each encryption operation that will use the new value (reserve-then-use, never lazily updated after the fact). **MUST requirement, made explicit in v6 (Priority 1): if this fsync fails for any reason, the encryption/save operation MUST abort — the client MUST NOT proceed to encrypt using a `localCounter` value it could not durably persist first.** This is the discipline the whole non-repetition guarantee below rests on; a best-effort or fire-and-forget fsync silently reopens the exact reuse-on-retry defect this construction exists to close.
   - **`hkdfSalt`** — a **32-byte random value, one per `(walletId, networkId)` pair** (v7, Priority 4, new — not one per device, not one per manifest/checkpoint; this is the pinned, unambiguous answer to the salt-lifetime question round 6 left open). Generated **once**, at the first checkpoint save ever made for this `(walletId, networkId)` pair (by whichever device makes that first save), and — critically, unlike `deviceId`/`localCounter` — carried in **`ManifestMetadata`** (unencrypted, per-manifest, travels with every checkpoint in `CheckpointStore`), not only in the originating device's local store. This is what makes the existing "any restoring device that knows the wallet seed can deterministically re-derive `key_device` for any `deviceId` it observes in a manifest's metadata" claim (point 4, below) actually true: a *different* device, decrypting a checkpoint it did not itself write, needs both the writer's `deviceId` **and** this salt, and can only get the salt from the manifest if it was never local-store-only. A device MAY also cache `hkdfSalt` locally for efficiency, but the manifest copy is authoritative — a device with no prior local state (e.g. a genuinely first-ever restore) reads it from the manifest it is decrypting.
2. **Per-device key derivation (v6, structural fix, Priority 1; canonical `info` encoding specified in v7, Priority 4):** `key_device := HKDF-SHA256(ikm = seed-derived attest-adjacent secret, salt = hkdfSalt (point 1, above), info = infoBytes)`, where `infoBytes` is the **length-delimited, fixed-width, big-endian** encoding (v7, closing the round-6 ambiguity — an unprefixed string concatenation is injectable, e.g. `("ab","c")` and `("a","bc")` would otherwise concatenate identically):
     ```
     infoBytes := ASCII("umbradb:snapshot:v4:enc:")           // fixed literal tag, no length prefix needed
               || u16be(len(walletId))  || utf8(walletId)      // 2-byte BE length prefix + UTF-8 bytes
               || u16be(len(networkId)) || utf8(networkId)     // (max 65535 bytes each -- ample; an
               || u16be(len(scope))     || utf8(scope)         //  encoder MUST reject longer inputs)
               || deviceId                                     // fixed 16 bytes, no prefix needed (width alone disambiguates)
     ```
     Every field is either a fixed-width literal/binary value (the tag, `deviceId`) or an explicit 2-byte-length-prefixed variable-width value (`walletId`/`networkId`/`scope`) — this prefix-free-by-construction scheme is what makes `infoBytes` unambiguous: two different `(walletId, networkId, scope, deviceId)` tuples can never encode to the same `infoBytes`, closing the injection ambiguity round 6 left unspecified. Binding `deviceId` into `info` — not merely into the nonce — is what makes cross-device nonce-space partitioning structurally unnecessary rather than merely improbable: every device that draws a distinct `deviceId` gets a distinct, independent AES-GCM key, and GCM's nonce-uniqueness requirement is a per-key property.
3. **Nonce layout — simplified in v6, no longer needs a `deviceId` component:** `nonce := uint64(localCounter) || uint32(chunkIndex)` — 96 bits total, GCM's standard nonce width, purely local to the encrypting device. Because uniqueness is now enforced by key separation, the nonce itself only has to be unique *within one device's own key* — which the fsync-before-use, strictly-monotonic `localCounter` already guarantees deterministically (below), with no `deviceId` bits needed inside the nonce at all.
4. **`seq` (`CheckpointStore`'s own per-`(walletId,networkId)` sequence) is completely unaffected by this change** — it was already decoupled from nonce material in v4 and stays decoupled in v6; it is read only for the attestation locator (`dbSeq`, §2.5.3/§3.6.1), never for anything nonce- or key-related, in any version from v4 onward.
5. **Concurrent-save counter-reservation protocol (v6, new, Priority 1 — the round's explicit ask for an actual protocol, not an informal assumption).** `localCounter`'s reserve-then-fsync step is performed under an **advisory exclusive lock**, scoped to `(walletId, networkId)`, held by the trusted local store itself (an OS-level file lock, a local mutex, or the equivalent single-writer primitive already available to any local-store implementation). Concretely: `reserveLocalCounter(walletId, networkId)` acquires the lock, reads the current durable `localCounter`, computes `next = localCounter + 1`, durably fsyncs `next`, releases the lock, and returns `next`. Any concurrent caller on the same device (multiple processes/tabs/threads racing to save at once) blocks on the lock until it is released, so no two callers can ever observe or reserve the same counter value — this makes the reserve step linearizable, not merely "usually fine in practice."
