6. **Counter exhaustion — explicit, mandatory fail-closed rule (v6, new, Priority 1 — replacing an informal estimate with a MUST).** A device **MUST** refuse to perform any further encryption for a given `(walletId, networkId)` once `localCounter` reaches a fixed safety threshold well below its 64-bit ceiling (e.g. `2⁶³`, half the space) — at that point the device MUST redraw a fresh `deviceId` (equivalent to the local-store-restore rekey path below) and reset `localCounter` to 0 before any further save, rather than silently continuing toward wraparound. At any realistic save cadence this threshold is not reachable within any device's operational lifetime (§7.3.1's corrected math, below) — the rule exists so the design has a specified, mandatory answer rather than relying on that informality being permanently true.

**Corrected collision-probability math for the v6 construction, computed concretely, with v5's number rechecked against the bound it was compared to (the round's explicit requirement — two prior rounds' arithmetic in this exact section has already been found wrong, so this is re-derived from first principles, not adjusted from the prior text).**

- **Re-checking v5's own number first, since it was cited as evidence of a prior error.** v5 computed `P(deviceId collision, D=20) = D²/(2×2³²) = 400/8{,}589{,}934{,}592 ≈ 4.657×10⁻⁸`. That arithmetic is correct — verified independently this session: `400 / (2 × 2^32) = 4.6566×10⁻⁸`. What was wrong is the sentence built on top of it: `4.6566×10⁻⁸ ÷ 2⁻³² = 4.6566×10⁻⁸ ÷ 2.3283×10⁻¹⁰ ≈ 200`. **v5's own construction's collision probability was ~200× larger than (i.e., ~200× worse than) the `2⁻³²` bound it claimed to "comfortably clear."** This is the error this revision fixes — not by re-deriving a smaller number for the *same* construction, but by changing the construction (above) so this comparison stops being the relevant one.
- **Intra-device, v6 construction (deterministic, not probabilistic — unaffected by the key-derivation change, strengthened by the width increase):** given the fsync-before-use, single-writer-locked discipline above holds, `localCounter` **cannot** repeat until 2⁶⁴ (≈1.845×10¹⁹) encryption operations have been performed by a single device under its own key for a single `(walletId, networkId)` — deterministic non-repetition, not a probability. At an absurdly generous sustained rate of 10 saves/second continuously, exhausting even the old 32-bit space took ≈13.6 years (v5's estimate, still correct as a lower bound); the 64-bit space widens this by a further factor of 2³² (≈4.3×10⁹), placing exhaustion far beyond any physically meaningful timescale. The §7.3.1-point-6 fail-closed rule above is the mandatory backstop regardless.
- **Cross-device, v6 construction (now a bound on *key* collision, not *nonce* collision under a shared key — the structural change that matters):** because each `deviceId` derives its own AES-GCM key (point 2 above), nonce reuse across two devices is possible only if those two devices first derive the *same* key, which — HKDF-SHA256 being a secure PRF, so key equality reduces to `info`-string equality for all practical purposes — happens if and only if they drew the identical 128-bit `deviceId`. Birthday-bound approximation over the widened space: `P(deviceId collision) ≈ D²/(2×2¹²⁸)`. For `D = 20` (the same realistic figure v5 used): `P ≈ 400/(2×3.403×10³⁸) ≈ 5.88×10⁻³⁷`. Even for an extreme, unrealistic `D = 1{,}000`: `P ≈ 10⁶/(6.805×10³⁸) ≈ 1.47×10⁻³³`. Both figures are computed directly from the formula, not asserted.
- **Comparison against the same NIST `≤2⁻³²` (≈2.33×10⁻¹⁰) bound v5 cited, done correctly this time:** `5.88×10⁻³⁷ ÷ 2.33×10⁻¹⁰ ≈ 2.5×10⁻²⁷` — the v6 construction's collision probability is **about 2.5×10⁻²⁷ of** the bound, i.e. roughly **10²⁶ times smaller than** the threshold, not ~200× larger than it. This is what "dissolving the question" means concretely: the fix is not a closer approach to the bound, it is several dozen orders of magnitude of margin, because the failure mode being bounded (key collision) is now both structurally rarer in kind (requires an identical 128-bit draw, not merely an identical 32-bit one) and consequence-narrower (even a key collision alone does not immediately imply active harm the way v5's shared-key nonce collision did — see below).
- **Exact value, v7, Priority 8 — the `D²/(2n)` figure above is a conservative approximation, stated exactly this time rather than left as a third instance of this document's own previously-flagged false-precision pattern (round 6's own §7.3.1 revision-history entry already named this pattern twice for this exact section).** The `D²/(2n)` formula (`400/(2×2¹²⁸) ≈ 5.8775×10⁻³⁷`) over-counts slightly relative to the exact birthday-collision probability, `P = 1 − ∏ᵢ₌₀¹⁹(1 − i/2¹²⁸)`, which for `D ≪ √n` is tightly approximated by `D(D−1)/(2n)` rather than `D²/(2n)` (the standard birthday-bound refinement: `∑ᵢ₌₀¹⁹ i = 190`, not `200`). Computed exactly: `D(D−1)/(2n) = 380/2¹²⁹ ≈ 5.5836×10⁻³⁷`. The document's `D²/(2n)` approximation (`≈5.8775×10⁻³⁷`) is therefore **~5.26% higher** than the exact value (`5.8775/5.5836 ≈ 1.0526`) — consistent with, and the exact source of, that gap: `D²` vs. `D(D−1)` in the numerator (`200/n` vs. `190/n`). **Both figures are stated here, explicitly labeled:** `5.8775×10⁻³⁷` is the simpler, *conservative upper-bound* approximation, kept elsewhere in this section for readability; `5.5836×10⁻³⁷` is the exact value. Either way the conclusion above (≈10²⁶ times smaller than the `2⁻³²` bound) is unaffected — the ~5.26% difference between the two figures is immaterial at this many orders of magnitude of margin; the correction here is about not making a false-precision claim, not about the conclusion changing.
- **Residual defense-in-depth (not required for the number above, disclosed for completeness):** even in the astronomically unlikely event of an actual `deviceId`/key collision, the two colliding devices would still need their `localCounter`s to reach the same value for a live nonce collision under that shared key — the same lockstep-from-zero dynamic v5 mischaracterized as "narrowing" the risk, correctly acknowledged here as *not* narrowing it (a collision, if it occurred, would be immediate, per the round's finding) — but this scenario is already contained by the local-store-restore defense below (an independent `deviceId` redraw trigger) and does not change the headline probability, which is already negligible on its own.

**Trace through GPT-5.6 Sol's exact honest-crash-then-restart scenario, re-run against the v6 construction.** Device has `localCounter = 41` (already consumed for prior saves), durably persisted, deriving `key_device` from its own `deviceId`. A new `save()` begins: the device acquires the local exclusive lock, durably increments-and-fsyncs `localCounter` to `42` **before** performing any encryption (the reserve step; per the new MUST rule, a failed fsync here aborts the save outright rather than proceeding) — `nonce = 42‖chunkIndex` is then used to encrypt this save's chunks under `key_device`, which are `INSERT`ed (observable by the DB). At any point after that — mid-transaction, before Postgres commits, an OS crash, a Postgres crash, anything — the attempt fails. Two things are independently true: (a) Postgres's own transaction (including its `ckpt_sequence_counters`/`seq` row) rolls back or is never committed, exactly as before, handled by ordinary retry; (b) the client's own local store already durably recorded `localCounter = 42` as consumed, independent of Postgres. On retry, the client reads `localCounter = 42`, increments to `43`, fsyncs, and uses `nonce = 43‖chunkIndex` under the *same* `key_device` for the retry. `nonce = 42‖chunkIndex` under `key_device` is **never reissued** — unaffected by anything Postgres's crash-recovery semantics do, because Postgres is not in the nonce- or key-generation path at all. This conclusion is unchanged from v5's version of this trace; the fix in this round changes *why the cross-device case is safe*, not this intra-device argument.

**The local-store-restore-from-backup vector (Opus/Fable 5/GPT-5.6 Sol, 3/3 convergence in round 6) — v6's fix found STRUCTURALLY BROKEN in round 6's own follow-up review, not merely narrow (Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol, an identical concrete counterexample, independently constructed).** The scenario, restated precisely: a device's trusted local store (holding `deviceId`, `localCounter`, and derived-key material) is backed up by the OS/cloud (a routine, non-malicious event — iCloud/Google account backup, a full-disk image, an MDM-managed restore) at a point where `localCounter = 100`. The device continues operating normally, reaching `localCounter = 250` (150 more genuine saves). The device is later restored from that earlier backup (app reinstall after data loss, migration to a "new" device image that is really a restore of the old one, etc.) — `deviceId` is preserved (it was already in the backup) but `localCounter` regresses to `100`.

**Why v6's beacon does not catch this.** v6 wrote a `storeInstanceId` (a static, generated-once, never-updated identity token) to both the primary store and a backup-excluded beacon, and checked only whether the two IDs still **matched**. In the scenario above: at T0, primary and beacon both hold `storeInstanceId = X`. The device continues to `localCounter = 250` — but v6's beacon records only identity, never progress, so nothing about reaching 250 ever touches the beacon; it still holds `X`, untouched, exactly as it did at T0. The primary is restored to the T0 backup — still `X`. **v6's check — "IDs match → continuous state, proceed normally" — fires**, because it was never designed to detect *how far* the device advanced, only *whether it is still the same device*. The very next save reserves `localCounter = 101`, a value already consumed by a genuine, already-encrypted ciphertext chunk 150 saves earlier under the same `deviceId`/key — deterministic AES-GCM nonce reuse, undetected. **This is not a scope gap (Opus's characterization) — it is a structural defect in what the beacon was designed to compare**, and it fires on this document's own headline example: an iOS app reinstall after data loss, where Keychain data (a candidate `ThisDeviceOnly` beacon location) commonly survives an app-data reset while the app's own primary storage does not.

**Fixed in v7 — the beacon carries genuinely monotonic, evolving state, not a static identity token.** The fix mirrors the reserved `localCounter` value itself into the beacon location **on every reservation**, and replaces "IDs match" with a **magnitude** check: "primary's `localCounter` must be ≥ beacon's mirrored counter." A mismatch — primary *behind* beacon — is the fresh-store-redraw signal, not identity disagreement.

**1. State shape.** Both the primary store and the beacon now hold `{ deviceId: Bytes16, counter: Uint64 }` — the beacon's `counter` field is a direct **mirror** of the primary's `localCounter`, not a separate opaque token; `storeInstanceId` is retired (redundant with `deviceId`, which already serves as the identity anchor for key derivation).

**2. Crash-safe dual-write reservation protocol (v7, Priority 1(a) — the round's explicit ask for a specified write ordering and reconciliation rule).**

```
reserveLocalCounter(walletId, networkId):
  acquire exclusive lock(walletId, networkId)     // same advisory lock as point 5 below, now scoped
  try:                                             // to cover primary+beacon as one atomic step
    primaryVal := readPrimary().counter
    beaconVal  := readBeacon().counter
    if beaconVal > primaryVal:
      // Genuine inconsistency: primary has regressed past what the beacon has witnessed --
      // exactly the restore-from-backup signature. MUST NOT reserve or return a value here.
      throw BackupRestoreDetected                  // caller redraws deviceId; see state machine below
    if beaconVal < primaryVal:
      // An earlier reservation's PRIMARY write succeeded but its BEACON write did not complete
      // (crash/power-loss between the two writes -- see the crash-window analysis below). By
      // construction, NO encryption can have happened under `primaryVal` yet, because encryption
      // only proceeds after BOTH writes durably succeed (point 3, below). Safe to complete the
      // mirror without consuming a new counter value.
      durablyWrite beacon.counter := primaryVal; fsync   // if this fsync fails: ABORT the save (MUST, point 3)
      return primaryVal
    // beaconVal == primaryVal: normal steady state -- reserve the next value.
    next := primaryVal + 1
    durablyWrite primary.counter := next; fsync     // if this fsync fails: ABORT the save (MUST, point 3)
    durablyWrite beacon.counter  := next; fsync      // if this fsync fails: ABORT the save (MUST, point 3) --
                                                       //   primary is now durably AHEAD of beacon; the NEXT
                                                       //   reservation attempt (this device, on retry) takes
                                                       //   the `beaconVal < primaryVal` branch above and
                                                       //   completes the mirror -- self-healing, not a
                                                       //   dangling inconsistency
    return next
  finally: release lock
```

**Write ordering: primary first, then beacon (v7, resolving Priority 1(a)'s explicit ask).** This ordering is deliberate, not arbitrary: it guarantees the invariant `beacon.counter <= primary.counter` holds at every quiescent (non-crashed) instant for a device that has not been restored from an earlier backup — which is exactly the polarity the "primary ≥ beacon → proceed" check needs to pass in the honest, continuously-operating case. **Crash-window analysis (both possible interruption points, both proven safe):** (a) crash after the primary write succeeds but before the beacon write completes — primary is durably ahead; per the protocol above, encryption for the reserved value has **not yet happened** (it only proceeds after both writes succeed, point 3), so the value was reserved but never consumed, and the next reservation attempt safely completes the mirror without any value ever being reused; (b) crash before the primary write (nothing durable changed) — the retried reservation simply re-reads the same `primaryVal`/`beaconVal` and proceeds normally. **No crash window at either interruption point causes a value to be both reserved-and-consumed under a beacon value that hasn't witnessed it** — the "beacon lags primary by at most one in-flight reservation, self-healing on the next attempt" invariant is what makes the ordering choice provably safe rather than merely conventional.

**3. MUST-abort rule, extended to the beacon write (v7, Priority 1(b)).** The existing v6 MUST-abort rule ("if `localCounter`'s fsync fails, the save MUST abort") is extended to cover **both** durable writes in the reservation step above: **encryption MUST NOT proceed unless both the primary `counter` write and the beacon `counter` write have durably succeeded.** This is what makes the crash-window analysis above sound — no ciphertext is ever produced under a counter value unless the beacon has already durably witnessed it, so a crash mid-reservation can only ever strand an *unconsumed* value, never a consumed-but-unwitnessed one.

**4. Locking (v7, Priority 1(c)).** The existing advisory exclusive lock (point 5, below) is extended to scope the *entire* read-compare-write sequence above (both the consistency check and the reservation) as one atomic critical section per `(walletId, networkId)` — not just the counter increment in isolation. Concurrent callers on the same device block on the same lock already specified for counter reservation; no new locking primitive is introduced.

**5. Full state-machine, including the two cases v6 left unspecified (v7, Priority 1(d)):**
- **Primary absent, beacon absent** → genuinely fresh install: draw a fresh `deviceId`, write `{deviceId, counter: 0}` to both primary and beacon (both writes durable, per the MUST-abort rule) before any encryption proceeds.
- **Primary present, beacon present, same `deviceId`, `primary.counter >= beacon.counter`** → continuous state; proceed normally through the reservation protocol above.
- **Primary present, beacon present, same `deviceId`, `primary.counter < beacon.counter`** → **the core v7 fix's detection case.** Redraw a fresh `deviceId`, reset `counter := 0`, write both locations durably before any further encryption. (A **different** `deviceId` between primary and beacon is treated identically — redraw — since it is at least as strong a restore/migration signal as a counter regression.)
- **Primary absent, beacon present (v7, new — the case v6 never specified).** This is the scenario this document's own headline example produces directly: an iOS reinstall where Keychain (`ThisDeviceOnly`) survives but the app's own sandboxed primary storage does not. The device has **no** durable record of what counter values are safe to consider consumed beyond whatever the beacon witnessed — reusing the beacon's `deviceId`/counter as a resumption point would be unsound, since the primary (the only record of what was actually *encrypted*, as opposed to merely *reserved*) is gone. **Resolution: treat identically to a detected mismatch — redraw a fresh `deviceId`, `counter := 0`, write both locations.** This is always safe regardless of what the lost primary might have contained, because a freshly-drawn `deviceId` derives a key that has never been used for any prior encryption, so there is no counter range to protect continuity with.
- **Primary present at `counter == 0`, beacon absent or mismatched (v7, new — the case v6 never specified).** `counter == 0` means, by construction (encryption only ever uses reserved values `>= 1`; `0` is the unconsumed starting value), that **zero encryptions have ever happened** under this primary's `deviceId`. There is therefore nothing to protect continuity with, and unlike the two cases above, a fresh `deviceId` redraw is unnecessary overhead: **safe to simply (re)write the beacon to match the primary's `{deviceId, counter: 0}`** and proceed — reconciling the mismatch without discarding a brand-new, never-used identity. (Distinguishing this from the general "counter regression" case above is exactly why the check is a magnitude comparison and not a bare presence/absence check: a fresh primary at counter 0 is definitionally safe to adopt.)

**6. Fail-closed requirement when no reliable backup-excluded primitive exists at all (v7, Priority 1(e), the explicit case round 6 left unspecified).** On a platform where the runtime cannot access **any** primitive genuinely excluded from ordinary backup/migration (no Keychain/Keystore-hardware-backed equivalent, no TPM, no reliably-excludable file location — e.g., a maximally restricted sandboxed/embedded environment with no persistent storage control at all), the client **MUST** refuse to encrypt entirely — throw `NoReliableBeaconPrimitiveError` and fail closed — rather than operate the deterministic-nonce AES-GCM construction with no rollback-detection signal underneath it. This is a new, explicit MUST rule; v6 left this case unspecified.

**7. Platform primitives, corrected for desktop (v7 — the round's explicit finding that a bare "marker file outside backup directories" does not survive a full-disk-image restore, which this design's own threat model already names).**
- **Mobile (unchanged from v6, already adequate):** iOS Keychain with `kSecAttrAccessibleWhenUnlockedThisDeviceOnly` (genuinely excluded from iCloud/iTunes backup and from device-to-device Quick-Start migration); Android Keystore-backed, non-exportable, ideally hardware/StrongBox-backed key or marker material (excluded from Android Auto Backup by construction, not merely by manifest flag).
- **Desktop/server, hardware-backed tier (v7, new — closes the gap rather than accepting it unconditionally).** Where a TPM 2.0 (or platform equivalent — Secure Enclave on Apple Silicon, a hardware-backed Windows KSP) is available, seal the beacon to it: Windows via a TPM-backed `NCRYPT`/Platform Crypto Provider key; macOS via a Secure-Enclave-backed, non-`iCloud`-synchronizable Keychain item; Linux/server via TPM 2.0 sealed storage (`tpm2-tools`/`tss2`) where a TPM is present and accessible. A hardware-sealed value defends against both ordinary OS/cloud backup-restore (sealed material does not export in a generic backup) **and** migration to different hardware (a TPM will not unseal data sealed to a different TPM) — genuinely closing the desktop gap the round flagged, not merely matching mobile's weaker guarantee.
- **Fallback tier, where no hardware-backed primitive is accessible (v7, honestly scoped, not silently accepted).** Fall back to a marker file placed outside any configured backup/sync directory, exactly as v6 specified — and **explicitly name full-disk-image restore as an accepted residual for this tier**, since a full-disk image captures literally every file, including ones a marker-file convention tries to exclude by location alone. This residual is disclosed in §10, not left implicit.
- **Residual that survives even the hardware-backed tier (disclosed, not hidden):** a full-disk-image restore performed onto the **same physical machine** (same TPM) will successfully unseal the "old" beacon value along with the "old" primary, since the TPM has no way to distinguish "this is the current, legitimate boot" from "this is a restored image of my own earlier state" — this narrow case (same-machine, same-TPM, full-disk-image restore) remains an accepted residual even in the hardware-backed tier, distinct from and narrower than the fallback tier's broader "any backup mechanism that happens to capture the marker file" residual.
- **AES-GCM-SIV recommended as defense-in-depth specifically for these named residuals (v7, retained from v6's suggestion, now scoped precisely to where it actually helps).** For exactly the two residual cases above — same-machine full-disk-image restore in the hardware-backed tier, and any-backup-capturing-the-marker-file in the fallback tier — a misuse-resistant AEAD (AES-GCM-SIV) degrades gracefully under nonce reuse (revealing only plaintext equality between the reused-nonce pair, not the catastrophic authentication-subkey leak plain AES-GCM suffers) rather than catastrophically. This remains a named, not-built-for-v1 hardening recommendation, specifically for the residual the beacon cannot close by construction, not a substitute for the beacon mechanism itself (which is what closes the general case, not just this narrower one).

**Re-running the round-6 counterexample against the v7 fix, to confirm it is actually blocked.** T0: primary and beacon both hold `{deviceId: X, counter: 100}` (in sync, per the steady-state invariant). The device continues saving: **each** of the 150 subsequent reservations durably writes primary-then-beacon per the protocol above, so by `counter = 250`, `beacon.counter = 250` too (self-consistent throughout, not merely "eventually" — every single reservation updates both locations). The primary is restored from the T0 backup: `primary.counter` reverts to `100`; the beacon — excluded from the backup by construction — is untouched and still reads `250`. The next reservation attempt reads `primaryVal = 100`, `beaconVal = 250`: **`beaconVal > primaryVal` → `BackupRestoreDetected`, thrown before any reservation completes and before any encryption proceeds.** The device redraws a fresh `deviceId`, resets `counter := 0`, writes both locations. The very next encryption operation happens under a **new** `deviceId`, hence a **new** `key_device` (per point 2's `info` binding), so counter values 101–250 under the *old* `deviceId`'s key are never touched again, by anyone, under any key. **The exact failure mode the counterexample describes — counter 101 reserved and reused under the same key as the original counter-101 save — cannot occur**, because the check that would have silently passed under v6's identity-only comparison now correctly detects the regression via magnitude, before the device ever gets the chance to reserve 101 again.

**Both original citations this section resolves, restated precisely (unchanged from v6).** GPT-5.6 Sol's Postgres-crash-recovery citation: resolved because Postgres is not in the nonce- or key-generation path. Fable 5's hostile-DB framing: resolved because the DB has nothing to replay, forge, or manipulate that influences nonce or key material. The round-6 local-store-restore vector: now genuinely resolved by the v7 mirrored-counter beacon above, not merely by a mechanism that happened to share the same name.

**KDF / domain separation, AAD, and key-rotation epoch model — updated in v6 to add `deviceId` to key derivation (Priority 1) and extend manifest authentication (Priority 3, below); canonical byte-exact encoding and the `formatMetadataCommit` redesign added in v7 (Priorities 2/3/4).**

The rest of the v3/v4 construction stands: `saveImpl` restructured to split plaintext into chunks (position-only, no crypto yet — unchanged), open the transaction, allocate `seq` via the existing atomic upsert-increment (unchanged — this is what §7.1(b)'s `candidateSeq`/`record.dbSeq` cross-check needs, and unlike the nonce it is *supposed* to roll back with its transaction, since a checkpoint that never durably saved should not occupy a sequence slot in the attested history), obtain `deviceId` and reserve the next `localCounter` from the client's own local store (v5 introduced the local-store-only sourcing; v6 replaces `nonceBase` with `localCounter` directly and adds `deviceId`-keyed key derivation, §7.3.1 above — no Postgres call either way), then encrypt each chunk and hash the **ciphertext** (not plaintext) for the content-addressed chunk table, in the same loop that currently just hashes-and-inserts plaintext chunks.

**What was actually found in current source, verified directly (not trusted from prior prose):**

```
$ git show origin/main:src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts   # saveImpl()
  chunkHashes = chunks.map(sha256)
  manifestHash = sha256(Buffer.concat(chunkHashes))
  INSERT INTO ckpt_chunks (hash, data) VALUES (chunkHashes[i], chunks[i])   -- raw bytes, unencrypted
```

No `encrypt`, `AES`, or `GCM` symbol appears anywhere in `src/interfaces/checkpoint-store.ts` or `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts`. The only hit for `getOrCreateSalt` in the whole `origin/main` tree is in `design/design.md`'s description of `PgPrivateStateProvider`'s per-`(accountId, scope)` salt — an entirely separate subsystem (Midnight contract *private state* storage, not wallet snapshots). The v1 draft's §2 claim that "UmbraDB already implements this" was false; corrected throughout (§2, §7.3).

**v3 re-verification of `saveImpl`'s actual sequence-allocation order (re-checked directly against `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts:139-173` this session, not trusted from the v2 prose above):** confirmed. `saveImpl` computes `chunks = splitChunks(data, chunkSize)` and `chunkHashes = chunks.map(sha256)` **before** `this.txLayer.withTransaction(...)` is ever called. Only *inside* that transaction — after the chunk-insert loop has already run — does it allocate `seq`:

```ts
// saveImpl, current source, annotated:
const chunks = splitChunks(data, chunkSize);        // <- chunking happens BEFORE the tx opens
const chunkHashes = chunks.map(sha256);              // <- chunk hashes computed BEFORE the tx opens
return await this.txLayer.withTransaction(async (tx) => {
  for (...) { INSERT INTO ckpt_chunks ...; }          // chunk rows written first
  const seqRows = await sql`
    INSERT INTO ckpt_sequence_counters (w, net) VALUES (${walletId}, ${networkId})
    ON CONFLICT (w, net) DO UPDATE SET next_seq = ckpt_sequence_counters.next_seq + 1
    RETURNING next_seq - 1 AS claimed_seq`;            // <- seq allocated AFTER chunks already exist
  const seq = seqRows[0].claimed_seq;
  ...
});
```

This confirms the round-2 finding exactly: an external encryption wrapper sitting in front of `save()` cannot construct a `(seq, chunkIndex)`-derived nonce, because `seq` does not exist yet at the point such a wrapper would need to encrypt. This rules out "encrypt-then-hand-to-`save()`" as a viable v1 shape for a per-chunk-nonce, sequence-derived construction — encryption must move to a point in the code that *has* `seq`, i.e. inside `saveImpl` itself, after the sequence-allocation step. (The chunk-insert loop currently running *before* sequence allocation is not itself a problem to fix — it's reordered below as part of moving encryption in, not because the current order is unsafe on its own.)

**v1 construction (blocking, not yet built) — chunk-then-encrypt, per-device key derivation, chunking section-aligned and padded (v6, Priorities 1+3, revised in v7 Priorities 1/2/3/4/6 — supersedes v5's shared-key/`nonceBase`-partitioned construction; format-metadata authentication redesigned around `formatMetadataCommit` rather than a chain-facing `manifestHash`; padding finalized byte-exactly; KDF/AAD encoding made canonical):**

The v2 text specified a per-chunk nonce while simultaneously implying the plaintext is encrypted as one blob before `CheckpointStore` ever sees it — those two statements cannot both be true. **chunk-then-encrypt** remains the resolution, matching the existing content-addressed chunk-store architecture:

1. `saveImpl` restructured: split plaintext into **section-aligned, bucket-padded** chunks (v5 introduced section-alignment; v6 adds padding — point 6 below), open the transaction, allocate `seq` via the existing atomic upsert-increment (unchanged — `seq` keeps its role as the attested checkpoint sequence, surfaced to the attestation layer as `dbSeq`, §2.5.3/§7.1(b)). Obtain `deviceId` (redrawing it first if the local-store-restore beacon check above flags an inconsistency) and reserve the next `localCounter` (via the locked reserve-then-fsync protocol above) from the client's own local store — still no Postgres call. Derive `key_device` from `deviceId` (point 4 below). Then encrypt each chunk and hash the **ciphertext** (not plaintext) for the content-addressed chunk table.
2. **Nonce layout — simplified in v6:** `nonce := uint64(localCounter) || uint32(chunkIndex)` — 96 bits (12 bytes), GCM's standard nonce width. No `deviceId` component: uniqueness across devices is now a property of `key_device` being distinct per device (point 4), not of the nonce encoding a device identifier.
3. **Why the DB-decoupled construction, not a Postgres-side fix (unchanged reasoning from v5):** no choice of Postgres primitive closes the hostile-DB or honest-crash-recovery framings, because both are about the DB being in the nonce/key-generation path *at all*. This is unaffected by v6's further change (moving from a shared key to per-device keys) — that change addresses a different gap (the cross-device probability argument), not this one.
4. **KDF / domain separation — v6, `deviceId` bound into `info`; canonical encoding + salt lifetime pinned in v7 (Priorities 1+4).** `key_device := HKDF-SHA256(ikm = seed-derived attest-adjacent secret, salt = hkdfSalt, info = infoBytes)` — the full canonical `infoBytes` encoding and `hkdfSalt`'s pinned one-per-`(walletId,networkId)` lifetime are specified above (the "per-device, per-`(walletId,networkId)` state pair" list, point 1–2), not restated here to keep one canonical location. `hkdfSalt` is a **new, dedicated** value — explicitly **not** `getOrCreateSalt`, which belongs to the unrelated private-state-provider subsystem and must not be reused across subsystems. Any restoring device that knows the wallet seed can deterministically re-derive `key_device` for any `deviceId` it observes in a manifest's (unencrypted) metadata, using the manifest's own carried `hkdfSalt` (v7 — required precisely because the salt is not local-store-only, per point 1 above) — key derivation is symmetric across devices sharing the same seed, so multi-device *decryption* of any other device's checkpoints is unaffected by this per-device *encryption* key separation.
5. **Key-rotation epoch model — unchanged from v3/v4 (item 7d).** `encKdfVersion` is a small monotonic integer stored **per-manifest**, naming the key-derivation epoch (which in turn determines the `info` string's non-`deviceId` components, e.g. a rotation-epoch tag) under which *that manifest's* chunks were encrypted. A client holds a small local table `epoch → key material`; `load()` reads `encKdfVersion` off the manifest row before attempting to decrypt. **v7 note (Priorities 2+3):** `encKdfVersion` is, by definition, exactly what changes on a legitimate re-encryption — it is deliberately **excluded** from the new chain-facing `formatMetadataCommit` (point 7, below) for exactly that reason; its own tampering is self-detecting via AES-GCM's authentication tag (wrong epoch → wrong key → tag failure on decrypt), which needs no additional chain-facing mechanism.
6. **Section-length privacy padding — new in v6 (Priority 3, the privacy-leak finding), finalized byte-exactly in v7 (Priority 6, full spec in §2.5.4).** Section-aligned chunking (v5) makes each Domain P section's chunk count directly proportional to its true byte length — for `ownedNotesPlain`/`nullifiersPlain` specifically, this leaks an approximate owned-note/nullifier count to the DB, a financially-sensitive signal. **Chosen fix (padding, not disclosure):** before chunking, each section's plaintext is padded — minimum bucket size 2 chunks, `0x00` padding bytes, canonical-padding validation on decode, `2³²`-byte per-section maximum, `trueLength` excluding its own field's bytes — up to the next power-of-two multiple of the chunk size (§2.5.4 has the complete, disambiguated spec; this bullet is a pointer, not a duplicate source of truth). This coarsens the leaked signal from "exact note/nullifier count" to "which power-of-two bucket" — a `log₂`-scale reduction in precision, at the cost of up to ~2× storage overhead in the worst case. **Why fix rather than disclose:** unlike the coarser "total manifest byte length" residual (point 9 below, which this design already accepts as unavoidable for any chunked store), a *per-section* count is specifically an approximate note/nullifier count — closer to balance/activity information than generic storage shape — and the fix is cheap relative to the sensitivity of what it hides.
7. **Format-metadata authentication — REDESIGNED in v7 (Priorities 2+3), replacing v6's chain-facing `manifestHash` witness, which round 6's own follow-up review found created a privacy leak and a key-rotation break.** v5 promoted `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion` to unencrypted per-manifest metadata to solve the AAD circular dependency (point 8, below); v6 tried to make all of them (plus a new `manifestSectionChunkCount` field) tamper-evident by folding an extended, ciphertext-chunk-hash-covering `manifestHash` into the chain-facing `attestLeaf` — but a chunk-hash-covering hash is an effectively unique fingerprint (privacy leak: a hosted DB holding the ciphertext manifest can recompute it and correlate its own blob to the on-chain identity), and it changes on every re-encryption (key-rotation break: it made the historically-attested `attestLeaf` unreconstructable after a routine re-encryption of the same checkpoint, contradicting this document's own pre-existing "re-encryption never invalidates a prior attestation" rule, §2.5.1/§2.5.2). **v7 re-derives what genuinely needs chain-facing protection, from first principles:** `encKdfVersion` (point 5, above) and `manifestSectionChunkCount` (below) are **self-detecting** — both feed either key derivation or per-chunk AAD (point 8, below), so tampering either produces an immediate AES-GCM authentication-tag failure on the very next decrypt attempt, no chain check needed. Only `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` are true decode-dispatch fields outside both AAD and key-derivation `info`, and both are **re-encryption-invariant** (same plaintext, same format, regardless of key/device/epoch). **Fixed:** these two, and only these two, are folded into a new `formatMetadataCommit := H_dom("umbradb:snapshot:v1:format", envelopeVersion, encodingVersion)`, itself folded **inside** the existing hiding `persistentCommit(snapshotRoot, formatMetadataCommit, salt)` construction (§2.5.3) — never disclosed in the clear, never placed in `attestLeaf` directly, and `manifestHash` (the full, ciphertext-chunk-hash-covering value) is removed from `attestLeaf`/`AttestRecord` entirely, reverting to the original, pre-round-6 rule that it is local-only and never chain-facing. `manifestSectionChunkCount` remains a small unencrypted integer naming exactly how many of the manifest's leading chunks (chunk index `0..manifestSectionChunkCount-1`) belong to `manifestSectionPlain` (`sectionId = 0`) before the second-pass sections begin — readable before any decryption — but is protected purely by its self-detecting AAD role (point 8, below), not by any explicit hash or chain-facing mechanism; no separate authentication step is needed for it. See §2.5.2/§2.5.3/§8 for the full equation and the traced confirmation that this closes both round-6 defects without reintroducing either.
8. **Authenticated data (AAD) — shape unchanged from v5's fix; encoding made byte-exact in v7 (Priority 4).** `AAD := aadBytes(walletId, networkId, seq, nonce, chunkIndex, chunkCount, sectionId)`, where `aadBytes` uses the same fixed-width, length-delimited, big-endian discipline specified for `infoBytes` above: `u16be(len(walletId)) || utf8(walletId) || u16be(len(networkId)) || utf8(networkId) || u64be(seq) || (nonce, 12 raw bytes, already fixed-width) || u32be(chunkIndex) || u32be(chunkCount) || u32be(sectionId)` — every numeric field big-endian, fixed-width; every variable-width field explicitly length-prefixed; no field's encoding can be confused with an adjacent field's, closing the same class of injection ambiguity `infoBytes` closes. `sectionId` remains well-defined for every chunk (section-aligned chunking, v5), `manifestSectionPlain`'s own chunks still bootstrap with the fixed `sectionId := 0` constant, and `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion` remain outside per-chunk AAD (unencrypted metadata; `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` are now covered by point 7's `formatMetadataCommit` instead, `encKdfVersion` by its own self-detecting role in key derivation — the correct fix for each gap is the mechanism that actually closes it, not stuffing everything back into per-chunk AAD and reopening the v5 circular dependency it was moved out to fix).
9. **Content-addressed dedup — permanently gone, unchanged conclusion, now for the v6 reason (nonce material is `localCounter`-derived per encryption operation under a per-device key, but the "essentially never fires" conclusion is the same).** Because the nonce is unique **per encryption operation on a given device**, `ckpt_chunks`' own `ON CONFLICT (hash) DO UPDATE` content-addressed dedup will **essentially never fire** once encryption ships — every encrypted chunk's ciphertext is unique by construction. **Disclosed storage-efficiency regression, unchanged from v3–v5:** pre-encryption, identical plaintext chunks deduped for free; post-encryption, every chunk consumes fresh storage every save. The residual that survives, narrowed by point 6's padding: an operator can observe total manifest byte length/chunk-count *bucket* (not exact count) per checkpoint — an unavoidable shape signal for any chunked store, now coarsened rather than exact for the sections that mattered most.

---

## 8. Compact / circuit sketches (illustrative, uncompiled)

**L3 — Attested Manifest Root (brief 05 §4.1, V1b+V2). Sub-zswap circuit; all constructs in current stdlib.** *Updated in v2 to match §2.5.3's canonical equation (statementVersion, encodingVersion, full-record history leaf) and §3.5's pinned-vk immutability commitment. Updated in v5 (Priority 4) to take `dbSeq` as an explicit disclosed public input and rename the contract's internal counter to `attestOrdinal`, per §2.5.3/§3.6.1's reconciliation-protocol fix. Updated in v6 (Priority 3), then REVISED in v7 (Priorities 2+3): v6 took `manifestHash` as a new disclosed public input; round 6's own follow-up review found this created a privacy leak and a key-rotation break (§2.5.3), so v7 removes `manifestHash` from this contract entirely and instead has the caller supply `formatMetadataCommit` — a small, pre-hidden value the caller folds into `snapshotRoot()`'s own witness commitment before calling `attest()`, never disclosed to the contract in the clear. `dbSeq` remains explicitly re-documented as a locator, never a monotonicity witness (v6 Priority 4, §12 D14) — no contract-logic change for that fix, since `height`'s existing CAS assertion is already the correct enforcement point.*
```compact
struct AttestRecord {
  attestLeaf: Bytes<32>;      // H(genesisHash, walletKindTag, id, encodingVersion, blockHash,
                               //   height, R_N, endIndex, commitment, dbSeq, attestOrdinal,
                               //   prevCommitment, statementVersion) -- the FULL record (§2.5.3)
                               //   v7: manifestHash REMOVED from this hash's inputs (was here in v6)
  commitment: Bytes<32>;      // v7: persistentCommit(snapshotRoot, formatMetadataCommit, salt) -- BOTH
                                //   Domain P AND the hidden format-metadata commitment are folded in
                                //   here (§2.5.3); manifestHash (Domain S) is NEVER an input, in any version
  height: Uint<64>;            // the ONLY field this contract enforces as monotonic (C7 below) -- the
                                //   sole anti-rollback high-water-mark signal downstream code may rely on
  dbSeq: Uint<64>;             // v5 (Priority 4) -- the caller-disclosed CheckpointStore locator for the
                                //   specific checkpoint this attestation is for. NOT incremented or
                                //   validated by the contract, and (v6, Priority 4) NOT monotonic across
                                //   attestations by construction -- a storage locator only, never compared
                                //   for freshness/ordering by any correct client-side check (§7.1(b)/§3.6).
  attestOrdinal: Uint<64>;     // v5: RENAMED from `seq`. Purely internal, contract-incremented,
                                //   gapless CAS-adjacent counter -- salt randomness only, never
                                //   compared against any client-side value.
  prevCommitment: Bytes<32>;
  statementVersion: Uint<32>; // pinned in client config per §3.5 -- this contract/circuit is v1-immutable
  encodingVersion: Uint<32>;  // §2.5.4 -- unchanged, pre-existing disclosed field (ALSO folded, hidden,
                                //   into formatMetadataCommit inside `commitment` -- the clear-text copy
                                //   here remains a convenience dispatch field, not the authoritative check)
  // v7: manifestHash field REMOVED from AttestRecord entirely -- see §2.5.3 for why
}
export ledger attestations: Map<Bytes<32>, AttestRecord>;   // pseudonym id -> latest
export ledger history: MerkleTree<32, Bytes<32>>;           // every attestLeaf (full record hash), V1b
witness attestSecretKey(): Bytes<32>;                        // dedicated HD path, not the spend key
witness snapshotRoot(): Bytes<32>;                           // Domain P Merkle root over plaintext sections (§2.5.2)
witness formatMetadataCommit(): Bytes<32>;                    // v7, NEW: H(envelopeVersion, encodingVersion) --
                                                                //   computed CLIENT-SIDE (the contract never
                                                                //   sees envelopeVersion/encodingVersion in
                                                                //   the clear as inputs to this witness), and
                                                                //   folded into `c` below, never disclosed raw

// v5 (Priority 4): `dbSeq` is an explicit parameter -- the caller states, at attest time, exactly
// which CheckpointStore-sequenced checkpoint this attestation is for. The contract does not derive
// or validate it against anything (it has no visibility into CheckpointStore at all) -- it simply
// discloses it into the record, the same way `height` already was. This is what makes the checkpoint
// locator immune to any gap/orphan in how many attest() calls succeeded in between (§3.6.1).
// v7 (Priorities 2+3): manifestHash is NO LONGER a parameter here (was in v6) -- format-metadata
// tamper-evidence is now achieved by folding formatMetadataCommit into the HIDING commitment `c`
// itself (below), not by disclosing a chunk-hash-covering value as a separate witness.
export circuit attest(height: Uint<64>, dbSeq: Uint<64>): [] {
  const sk = attestSecretKey();
  const id = disclose(persistentHash([pad(32,"umbradb:attest:v2:id"), sk]));   // C8 pseudonym
  const isUpdate = attestations.member(id);
  const prev = isUpdate ? attestations.lookup(id) : default;
  if (isUpdate) assert(prev.height < height, "attestation must advance");      // C7 CAS anti-rollback --
                                                                                 //   the ONLY monotonicity
                                                                                 //   check this contract
                                                                                 //   performs; dbSeq is
                                                                                 //   never checked here
  const salt = persistentHash([pad(32,"umbradb:attest:v2:salt"), sk, ordinalAsBytes(prev.attestOrdinal + 1)]);
  const c = persistentCommit([snapshotRoot(), formatMetadataCommit()], salt);   // v7: BOTH witnesses folded
                                                                                  //   into the hiding commit (C3)
  const leaf = persistentHash([pad(32,"umbradb:attest:v5:leaf"), genesisHash, walletKindTag, id,
                                encodingVersion, blockHash, disclose(height), rN, endIndex, c,
                                disclose(dbSeq), ordinalAsBytes(prev.attestOrdinal + 1),
                                prev.commitment, statementVersion]);             // v7: manifestHash param REMOVED
  history.insertHash(leaf);                                                    // full record, not bare c
  attestations.insert(id, AttestRecord { attestLeaf: leaf, commitment: c, height: disclose(height),
                                         dbSeq: disclose(dbSeq),
                                         attestOrdinal: disclose(prev.attestOrdinal + 1),
                                         prevCommitment: prev.commitment,
                                         statementVersion: disclose(statementVersion),
                                         encodingVersion: disclose(encodingVersion) });
                                         // v7: manifestHash field REMOVED from the inserted record
}
```
This contract's address and `attestCircuitVkHash`/`statementVersion` are **pinned, immutable client config for v1** (§3.5, option a) — no in-circuit or contract-governed succession mechanism ships in v1. The successor-certificate shape for a later, explicitly-ratified v1.1+ (§3.5 option b) is a separate `migration` record type, not sketched here since it is not being built now.

**L3 — offline v-lightweight ZK certificate (brief 07 §2.1). Hand-written zkir; public inputs `{hash(S), R_N, N, id}`; ∝ owned notes; k≈20; verify in ms.**
```
for each owned note i:  ownership: k*_i = c_i · esk (EcMul); assert plain_i[0]==0 (Poseidon-CTR decrypt)  // "mine"
                        membership: c^cc_i = PersistentHash("midnight:zswap-cc[v1]", info_i, pk)         // 1 SHA-256
                                    assert merkle_path_root(path_i, c^cc_i) == R_N                        // ≤32 Poseidon
binding:  assert hash(S) == TransientHash(canonical_encode({info_i, index_i}))
id:       public  TransientHash("umbra:07:id", sk)
```
Proves inclusion + ownership + value-binding at finalized N; **does not** prove completeness — see §5.0/§5.1 for the precise, corrected scope of what completeness means here. Verified off-chain by `VerifierKey::verify` (`transient-crypto/src/proofs.rs:545-558`).

**L3 research — IVC ratchet state (brief 08 §2.1):** `AssignedState = (checkpoint cursor N, Poseidon frontier commitment, R_N + finalizedHash anchor field)`; `Witness = the L1 ADS delta (N,N+1]`; `circuit_transition` **internalises the collapsed-update completeness check** (pure Poseidon, brief 08 §3.4). O(1) proof/verify; O(delta) per step. Native-Rust prover, not `:6300`.

---

*Updated in v2: encryption row corrected (item 10), unshielded/dust rows relabeled Tier-F (item 8), canonical encoding promoted to blocking (item 1), envelope versioning and restore-API rows added (items 2, 6). Updated in v3: owned-notes binding row added (item 0), authenticated L3 lookup row added (item 1), AES-GCM row's construction corrected (item 7).*

| Client-side AES-GCM | L2 | ❌ **NOT implemented today, verified against source [item 10]; v1 blocking, spec §7.3.1; construction fixed to chunk-then-encrypt inside `saveImpl`'s transaction, injective nonce, corrected dedup-leak claim [v3 item 7]; nonce material moved fully client-side [v5 Priority 2, D11]; further restructured in v6 to bind `deviceId` into per-device KEY derivation (not merely the nonce), widen `deviceId`/`localCounter` to 128/64 bits, add a local-store-restore-from-backup detection/redraw mechanism, an explicit fsync-MUST-abort rule, a concurrent-save locking protocol, and a counter-exhaustion fail-closed rule — the v5 construction's own collision-probability claim was found ~200× worse than the NIST bound it claimed to clear, not merely imprecise [v6 Priority 1, D11 revised]; **v6's beacon found structurally broken by an identical concrete counterexample from 2 of 3 round-6 reviewers — replaced in v7 with a mirrored-counter beacon, crash-safe dual-write protocol, full state machine, and platform-primitive fail-closed rule [v7 Priority 1, D11 revised again]**; AAD restructured to eliminate a circular decrypt-before-you-can-decrypt dependency via unencrypted per-manifest version metadata + strictly section-aligned chunking [v5 Priority 3]; **format-metadata authentication redesigned around a small, re-encryption-invariant `formatMetadataCommit` folded into the existing hiding commitment, replacing v6's chain-disclosed `manifestHash` witness, which introduced a privacy leak and a key-rotation break [v7 Priorities 2+3, D13 revised]**; section-length padding finalized byte-exactly [v7 Priority 6]; `deviceId`/`hkdfSalt` added to `ManifestMetadata` with canonical length-delimited encoding for `info`/AAD [v7 Priority 4]; dedup-loss cost explicitly disclosed [v4 items 1/2]** | | |

## 10. Honest residual trust (after all v1 layers)

*Rewritten in v2: adds the vk/circuit-pin item (item 4, absent before — itself a gap the audit flagged) and the unshielded/dust federated-trust item (item 8); tightens vocabulary throughout to match this section's own pre-existing rigor (item 5) rather than weakening it; folds in the AES-GCM dedup-leak residual (item 10) and the BFT-CRDT communication precondition (item 11).*

The floor, stated plainly (brief 03 §7, brief 06 §6, brief 10 §0):

1. **Consensus/finality.** Correctness reduces to an on-chain root; that root's trust reduces to **GRANDPA not reverting blocks ≤ N**. The certificate *inherits* this, it does not remove it. Tier-1 makes it *verifiable* rather than *assumed*, down to one irreducible weak-subjectivity seed (the genesis authority set, trusted once) (brief 10 §0). This is the sense in which "the chain is trusted" in this document — a designated root of trust *within this threat model*, not an unconditional guarantee independent of GRANDPA's own safety assumptions (v1 draft's phrasing overstated this; corrected in §3).
2. **Restore-time and ongoing freshness (A5).** The wallet must obtain the *genuine* finalized R_N — a light-client problem, mitigated (not eliminated) by Tier-1 + multi-endpoint, strongest with a local node (brief 05 §9, brief 07 §6.2). **Extended in v2 (§3.6):** freshness is not a one-time restore-time check — an already-active wallet must keep rechecking (pre-spend, periodic) against the L3 pointer, or a rollback accepted at cold-boot and never rechecked is functionally the same gap recurring silently. **Tightened in v4 (Priority 4, GPT-5.6 Sol's finding):** everywhere this document says a restore consults the "fresh finalized tip," that means precisely "a block this restore independently GRANDPA-verified as finalized" — **not** "provably the chain's current latest finalized block." An eclipsing or stale-serving endpoint can serve a genuinely-finalized-but-older head, complete with a valid justification and a valid (even cryptographically-real, where that exists) absence proof *for that older state* — the wallet correctly concludes "nothing newer as of this block" while something newer genuinely exists past what the endpoint chose to show. Tier-0 multi-endpoint cross-checking (§4) and the k-of-n absence check (item 9 below) raise the bar against a single adversarial endpoint but do not close this to a cryptographic guarantee; only a continuously-updated light-client session (Tier-2, deferred) would.
3. **Unshielded and dust verification are federated-quorum trust (Tier-F/Tier-F-lite), not consensus-reduced trust — new in v2, §2.6.** This is a scope acknowledgment, not a deferred bug: v1 ships real value over "trust the DB blindly," but it must never be described with the same "verified"/"trustless" language the shielded path earns. True reduction requires the node/protocol changes named in §7.2.
4. **Attest-time honesty (L3-c) / circuit-and-pin correctness (L3-a, and the vk pin itself) — expanded in v2, §3.5; extended in v3, §2.5.5.** The attestation transports correctness forward but cannot create it — a wallet compromised *at attest time* pins bad state (an explicit non-goal; brief 05 §1). The offline proof only means "the statement *this vk's circuit* encodes holds" — the hand-written IR must be audited and its vk pinned (brief 07 §6.3). **New in v2:** the L3-c contract/vk pin itself (§3.5) is a named residual — v1 clients trust that their hard-pinned `contractAddress`/`attestCircuitVkHash`/`statementVersion` were pinned correctly and that the client software delivering that pin is honest; a compromised software update that silently changes the pin is the attack this design is *not* trying to solve, same class as "the client software is honest" generally, but now named explicitly for this component because a bad pin has outsized blast radius (silent acceptance of a malicious successor circuit). **Sharpened in v4 (Priority 6):** as of this writing, no confirmed Midnight chain API exists to read a per-contract deployed-verifier-key-hash, so `assertContractVkPinned` (§7.1(b)) enforces the `contractAddress` pin structurally only — `conn.attestCircuitVkHash` is carried in config as a typed, forward-compatible placeholder but is **not consulted by any v1 check.** Concretely: v1's actual protection against a substituted attestation *circuit* (as distinct from a substituted contract *address*, which the structural check does catch) is the immutable-pin-plus-audited-client-software argument above, alone — not an on-chain vk-hash comparison. This was previously implied to be conditionally real; it is not, and this item is the authoritative statement of that. **New in v3 (item 0, §2.5.5):** the newly-committed `ownedNotesPlain` section's *base value at N* is transported forward under this exact same attest-time-honesty umbrella — a wallet whose owned-note bookkeeping was already wrong or incomplete at attest time will attest, and re-verify at restore, a self-consistent but wrong base. This is not a new class of trust — it is the pre-existing item-4 residual, now explicitly named against the specific commitment section it applies to, per the round-2 audit's request not to leave this unspecified. The risk from this residual does **not** compound over time: §2.5.5's mechanism (b) means every note added after N is independently re-derived by the restoring device's own live trial-decryption over `[N, tip]`, never inherited from the attestation.
5. **Ciphertext-delivery + spend completeness — restated precisely per §5.0.** Open in v1 (§5) — Zcash-parity, bounded by NxN + only-spend-own-notes (scoped correctly, §5.0) + first-spend re-validation (scoped correctly, §5.1), fully closed only by a node change. This is the *same* residual as "L0+L1 don't bind wallet identity" (item 7) — not a second, independent gap. **Distinct from item 4's owned-notes-base residual (v3):** this item is about *completeness* of what the wallet's trial-decryption can see; item 4's new sub-item is about *correctness of the base commitment as transported forward*, even assuming trial-decryption saw everything it was shown. §2.5.5 has the full distinction.
6. **Privacy.** Rests on the seed's ≥256-bit entropy and the secrecy of the seed-derived key (brief 03 §7). The remote scanner still learns ownership until the detection-tag overlay ships (§6). **New in v2, corrected in v3 (item 7e):** the v2 text claimed a content-addressed dedup equality leak across checkpoints of the same wallet; that claim was inconsistent with the fresh-per-`save()` nonce construction §7.3.1 specifies (v6: client-side per-device key derivation + durable local counter, superseding v5's shared-key/`deviceId`-partitioned nonce space — fresh `localCounter` on every save under a device's own key ⇒ ciphertext is never identical across two different checkpoints, even for byte-identical plaintext) — there is **no** cross-checkpoint equality leak under the corrected construction. **Narrowed further in v6 (Priority 3):** the per-*section* chunk-count leak (an approximate owned-note/nullifier count, financially sensitive) is now closed by padding each section to the next power-of-two chunk-count bucket (§7.3.1 point 6) rather than left as an accepted residual — the residual that survives is the coarser total-manifest-byte-length/bucket shape (unavoidable for any chunked store) plus (v5, Priority 3) small unencrypted per-manifest version-tag integers (`envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion`/`manifestSectionChunkCount`, v6 adds the last) — all unavoidable/standard-practice-level disclosures, not content or ownership leaks, and (v6) now chain-tamper-evident via the extended `manifestHash`/`attestLeaf` binding (item 4-adjacent, §12 D13) even though they remain unencrypted.
7. **Multi-device split-view detection requires an active communication precondition — new in v2, §2 L2 bullet 3 / item 11.** Hash-chained, signed deltas detect tampering only between devices (or a device and the L3 pointer) that actually compare notes on some cadence; a malicious DB can otherwise show indefinitely divergent forks to devices that never exchange history. Device-key membership/revocation and non-commutative merge-rule specification remain explicitly out of scope for v1.
8. **Trusted-setup + proving-system soundness** (KZG BLS12-381 SRS, Halo2) — shared with the entire chain, not new to us (brief 07 §6.5-6).
9. **L3 attestation absence is federated-trust-bounded, not cryptographically proven — new in v4, §7.1(b) (Priority 4).** `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s present-record case is a genuine state-read-proof-backed inclusion check. Its absent case is not backed by any confirmed Midnight non-membership primitive today — the same primitive gap already named for nullifiers (§5.1 item 2) applies here — so v1 falls back to a Tier-0-style k-of-n cross-indexer agreement for "this wallet has no attestation," a federated/bounded trust claim, not a consensus-reduced one. Every restore that reaches `"L0+L1"` via the silent-absence branch carries this as a named `residuals` entry. Upgrade path: adopt a real Compact-level Map non-membership proof if/when one becomes available.
10. **The legacy pre-restore probe (§7.1(d), item 11) is opt-in, not enforced — characterization corrected in v4, Priority 9.** The probe only runs when a caller supplies `identity.skAttest`; nothing in the API forces this. A caller restoring a wallet that genuinely has real on-chain attestation history, but simply omits `identity` (a missed integration, not necessarily a from-scratch wallet), silently takes the same unverified path as a wallet with no key material at all. This is process/caller-discipline, not a closed gap — v3 incorrectly characterized it as vacuous outside the genuinely-keyless case.
11. **The `seq`/`record.seq` reconciliation is now protocol-specified (§3.6.1, v5, Priority 4), but rests on a required companion implementation fix this design document cannot itself make.** Verified directly against `origin/main:src/postgres/wallet-state-envelope.ts` this session: `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()` reads the checkpoint's storage-native `record.sequence` internally but discards it before returning, surfacing only the decoded envelope to its caller. `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`'s `loaded.storeSequence` input (§7.1(b)) is not obtainable from this real call site until `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`'s return shape is widened to surface it. This is named here as a concrete, blocking dependency for implementation — out of this design document's own scope (it specifies the wallet-SDK/attestation-contract design, not this storage-adapter class) but not silently assumed to already be true. Additionally, an **orphaned checkpoint** (a durably-saved checkpoint whose `attest()` call never succeeded, §3.6.1) is an accepted, non-fatal, by-design residual: such a checkpoint carries no L3 guarantee and is invisible to `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`'s L3 path (it simply isn't the `dbSeq` any successful attestation names), though it remains available as ordinary, unverified fallback data if ever needed.
12. **`dbSeq` is a storage locator only and carries no monotonicity guarantee — new in v6, Priority 4, correcting an error in every prior round's text.** v2 through v5 variously used `dbSeq` (or its predecessor `seq`) as though comparing it across attestations were a valid freshness/ordering check — it is not: `dbSeq` reflects `CheckpointStore` save order, a purely local, per-`(walletId,networkId)` sequence, which can legitimately diverge from attestation-*arrival* order across devices with different attestation latency (a device that saves first but attests slowly can have its later, height-superior attestation land with a numerically *lower* `dbSeq` than an attestation that arrived first from a device that saved later — §12 D14 traces this concretely). The only field the attestation contract's own CAS actually enforces as increasing is `height` (§8's `assert(prev.height < height)`); every place in this document that needs a monotonicity/freshness signal — the L2 local anti-rollback high-water mark (§7.1(b)), §3.6's pre-spend/periodic recheck and divergence condition — now keys on `height`, and `height` **alone** (v7 straggler fix, Priority 7: this sentence previously read "`height` (or, redundantly, the contract-internal `attestOrdinal`)," offering `attestOrdinal` as an alternate signal despite this document elsewhere stating `height` is *sole* — while `attestOrdinal` does happen to co-vary with `height` for any attestation that actually lands, per the contract's CAS discipline, naming it here as an interchangeable alternative invites exactly the kind of ambiguous-signal drift this design has already had to fix twice for `dbSeq`; `height` is the one, unambiguous, contract-enforced signal, full stop), never `dbSeq`. `dbSeq`'s only remaining role, everywhere in this document, is as a storage locator (`CheckpointStore.load(walletId, networkId, record.dbSeq)`) and a substitution-detection witness (`record.dbSeq === candidateSeq`, confirming a restore loaded the exact checkpoint the attestation being checked refers to) — never ordering.

13. **Liveness-beacon platform-primitive residual — new in v7, §7.3.1.** Even with the mirrored-counter beacon fix (§7.3.1), the underlying backup-excluded storage primitive is platform-dependent: on the hardware-backed tier (TPM/Secure-Enclave/hardware-Keystore), a same-machine, same-TPM full-disk-image restore remains an accepted residual (the TPM has no way to distinguish "current legitimate boot" from "restored image of my own earlier state"); on the fallback tier (marker file outside backup directories, used only where no hardware-backed primitive is accessible), any backup mechanism that happens to capture the marker file's location is an accepted residual, broader than the hardware-backed tier's. A platform offering **no** backup-excluded primitive at all fails closed (`NoReliableBeaconPrimitiveError`) rather than silently operating unprotected. AES-GCM-SIV is named as a recommended, not-built-for-v1 defense-in-depth mitigation specifically for the two disclosed residual cases.
14. **Intentional historical restore's own named residuals — new in v7, §3.6.2.** The `history`-tree inclusion-proof mechanism (§3.6.2) proves a historical attestation is genuine and chain-included, but does not itself guarantee the checkpoint blob it points to (`record.dbSeq`) has survived retention/pruning policy — an operator wanting to support deep historical restore must set `CheckpointStore` retention accordingly, named as an operational dependency, not assumed. The historical-lookup indexer query is untrusted-for-correctness (the inclusion-proof-plus-self-hash check catches a wrong or lying answer) but not untrusted-for-availability (a down/malicious indexer can still refuse to answer) — the same availability-only trust this design already places in the DB/indexer everywhere else (item below).

The DB itself is trusted for **availability only** — strengthened by plain multi-host replication extending the NxN habit to the blob (brief 11 §3; erasure-coding/DAS explicitly rejected as disproportionate at wallet-snapshot scale). **TEE attestation is rejected** as a substitute (attests code identity, not chain-relative data; its own root of trust has broken repeatedly — Foreshadow/SGAxe/Downfall, and the wallet-shaped Secret Network consensus-seed extraction — brief 11 §1); acceptable only as an orthogonal at-rest confidentiality layer *underneath* the anchor.

---

## 11. Post-implementation testing strategy

Every design claim must map to a test that could falsify it. Organized by layer and by the adversary each defends against. *v2 adds tests for the state machine (§3.6), envelope fail-closure (§7.1), coupled-tuple finality (§4), the AES-GCM spec (§7.3.1), and the corrected L0/L1/L0+L1+L3 claims (§5.0, §7.1(b)). v3 adds tests for owned-notes binding (§2.5.5), authenticated/present-vs-absent L3 lookup (§7.1(b)), full `attestLeaf` reconstruction, `seq` unification, the now-non-trivial L1 tail range, the revised AES-GCM construction (§7.3.1), and the legacy-path pre-restore probe (§7.1(d)). v4 adds the direct regression test for the restore-predicate-doesn't-recompute defect found in three consecutive rounds (§7.1(b)), the nonce-reuse-under-abort regression test (§7.3.1), a real-`envelopeVersion:1`-dispatch test (§7.1(a)/(d)), the L1 lower-bound-inflation test (§7.1(b)), and a test asserting the L3 absence path is NOT treated as cryptographically proven (§7.1(b)/§10 item 9). v5 adds the sections-mutation and AAD-bootstrap regression tests (§7.1(b)/§7.3.1). v6 adds the `FrozenFrontier` structural-enforcement test, the wallet-construction-scope test for the mixed-time-wallet fix (§7.1(b)), the local-store-restore-from-backup and concurrent-save-contention tests (§7.3.1), the `manifestHash`/`manifestSectionChunkCount` tamper-evidence and section-length-padding tests (§7.3.1/§2.5.3), and the Device A/B `dbSeq`-regression race test (§7.1(b)/§3.6).*

### 11.1 Unit + property tests
- **L0 collapse-invariant (the load-bearing fact):** property test that `serialize → deserialize → rehash().root()` is bit-identical to the on-chain root at the same `endIndex`, across randomized note sets and `firstFree` values (brief 01 §6.2). Falsifies the "offline recompute" claim if it ever diverges.
- **L0's precise scope (item 7; corrected in v6, Priority 5iv, stale-test fix):** a test snapshot with a correct global tree frontier but tampered/truncated owned-notes bookkeeping must pass L0 alone. **It is caught by the L3 commitment-equality check (§2.5.2's `ownedNotesPlain` binding, §7.1(b)'s recomputed-`snapshotRoot`-vs-`commitment` check) when an on-chain attestation exists to compare against — NOT by "L1 + local trial-decryption," which this test previously (incorrectly) named as the catching mechanism.** That prior wording contradicted this document's own established residual (§2.5.5/§10 item 4): L1 and live trial-decryption only independently re-derive notes *added after* checkpoint N; they never re-verify the *base* owned-note set's correctness at N, which is attest-time-honesty-only. A companion assertion in this same test confirms that when *no* attestation exists to check against (verificationLevel stays `"L0+L1"`), the tampered base owned-notes bookkeeping is caught by **nothing** in this design — an explicit negative assertion for the residual, not merely a positive assertion for the L3-present case.
- **L1 completeness algebra:** property test that `applyCollapsedUpdate` over `[endIndex_N, endIndex_tip)` is a monoid homomorphism and that any *omitted/reordered/inserted* commitment in the range makes the rehashed root diverge from the tip root (brief 06 §2.1). Fuzz the collapsed-update bytes.
- **L1 unshielded boundary proof — labeled Tier-F:** property test that the MB-tree non-membership proof accepts iff `A⁻ < A < A⁺` are genuinely adjacent, and rejects any forged `[]` for a present address or any dropped UTXO within a present address's list (brief 06 §4.3); a companion test asserts the SDK never labels this result "consensus-verified" (§2.6).
- **L2 anti-rollback monotonicity (v7 straggler fix, Priority 7): keyed on `height` alone, never `seq`/`dbSeq`.** property test that a snapshot with `height` below the highest-ever-accepted is rejected; that the chain-freshness check rejects `anchorHeight <` last-known-finalized. **v7 correction:** this test previously read "a snapshot with `seq`/height below the highest-ever-accepted is rejected" — per §12 D14's traced Device A/B race, a `seq`/`dbSeq`-keyed version of this test would **wrongly reject** Device A's legitimate, freshest attestation (higher `height`, lower `dbSeq` than Device B's already-accepted one); the test is corrected to assert rejection on `height` alone, and a companion assertion confirms the Device A outcome from that race is correctly **accepted**, not rejected, closing the gap between what this test asserted and what the height-only design actually requires.
- **L2 BFT-CRDT — with the communication precondition (item 11):** property test for fork*-consistency under periodic exchange — signed hash-chained deltas converge under causal delivery when devices actually compare notes; a companion **negative** test confirms that two devices that never exchange history/pointer checks remain indefinitely divergent and undetected, documenting the precondition rather than hiding it.
- **L3 attestation CAS:** unit test that a replayed old `attest` tx fails against advanced state (transcript re-run), and that height-monotonicity `assert` holds (brief 05 §4.3).
- **L3 canonical equation (§2.5.3):** property test that `manifestHash` (Domain S) changing under key rotation never changes `snapshotRoot` (Domain P) or any attested `commitment` — the direct regression test for the fixed contradiction (item 1).
- **L3 pinned `statementVersion` (§3.5) — corrected in v5 (Priority 5d, stale-test fix).** unit test that a client configured with a pinned `attestStatementVersion` rejects any attestation record whose `statementVersion` doesn't match, even if the contract address matches (guards against a silently-swapped successor). **`attestCircuitVkHash` is explicitly NOT covered by this test** and no test in this suite should assert it is chain-checked: per §7.1(b)/§10 item 4 (Priority 6), `attestCircuitVkHash` is a typed, forward-compatible config placeholder in v1, threaded through but never consulted by any check — v3's original wording here implied both fields were enforced together, which overclaimed what `assertContractVkPinned` actually does.
- **L3 ZK circuit:** negative tests that a note not decrypting to `esk`, a commitment not under `R_N`, or a tampered `hash(S)` all fail proof generation/verification (brief 07 §2.1); `CircuitModel` cost-model run to confirm k≈20 for m=50–200 notes.
- **Owned-notes binding (new in v3, item 0/§2.5.5) — the direct regression test for the round-2 defect:** property test that two envelopes with identical `cursorPlain`/`nullifiersPlain`/`R_N^tree`/`dustPlain`/`manifestSectionPlain` but *different* `ownedNotesPlain` produce **different** `snapshotRoot` values. This must fail against the pre-v3 equation (documented as the regression baseline) and pass against §2.5.2's v3 equation — the falsifying test for exactly the defect both Fable 5 and GPT-5.6 Sol independently found.
- **`restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` actually recomputes (new in v4, Priority 1) — the direct regression test for the defect found in THREE consecutive rounds:** unit test that calls `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` with an envelope whose `sections.ownedNotesPlain` has been tampered while `envelope.snapshotRootHint` is left set to the value that would have been honestly attested for the ORIGINAL (untampered) notes. This must throw `RollbackDetectedError` at the L3 commitment-equality step. This test would have **passed incorrectly** (i.e. returned a tampered wallet with `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"`) against v3's implementation, which trusted `envelope.snapshotRoot` directly — it is the specific falsifying test the round-1/round-2/round-3 audits were asking for and that no prior round's test suite actually contained (the existing "owned-notes binding" test above only exercises the *equation*, §2.5.2, never the *predicate*, §7.1(b)). A companion test confirms the returned `wallet` and the value hashed into the recomputed `snapshotRoot` are constructed from the identical `sections` reference, not merely equal-by-coincidence values.
- **`attestLeaf` full reconstruction (new in v3, item 2; field names updated in v5, Priority 4; `manifestHash` added in v6, Priority 3, REMOVED again in v7, Priorities 2+3):** unit test that `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` rejects a record whose `attestLeaf` doesn't match a full §2.5.3 reconstruction even when `commitment` and `height` alone would have passed — i.e. a record with a correct `commitment`/`height` but a tampered `genesisHash`, `walletKindTag`, `blockHash`, `R_N`, `endIndex`, `encodingVersion`, `dbSeq`, `attestOrdinal`, or `prevCommitment` inside the leaf must still be rejected. Regression test for the v2 gap where only `commitment`/`height` were checked. **v7 note:** `manifestHash` is no longer a leaf field to test here at all — its replacement, `formatMetadataCommit`, is tested via the *commitment*-equality path instead (below), not a separate leaf-field comparison, since it is folded inside `commitment` rather than disclosed alongside it.
- **`record.dbSeq` / `candidateSeq` unification (new in v3, item 4 as `record.seq`; re-sourced in v4, Priority 3; renamed and reconciliation-protocol-hardened in v5, Priority 4) — substitution/locator role only, corrected in v6.** unit test that a well-formed record with `record.dbSeq !== candidateSeq` (`candidateSeq` sourced from `CheckpointStore`'s storage metadata, not a decoded envelope field) is rejected via `RollbackDetectedError`, even when `commitment`/`attestLeaf` would otherwise match under the (wrong) salt. **Corrected in v6 (Priority 4, stale-test fix): the companion test previously asserted "the local high-water mark is updated from `record.dbSeq`" — this is now WRONG and is replaced.** The corrected companion test confirms the local high-water mark is updated from **`record.height`** (never `record.dbSeq`, never DB-supplied storage metadata) after a successful L3-verified restore — see the new Device A/B race test below for why `dbSeq` is unsuitable for this role. A companion test (unchanged from v5) confirms that an *orphaned* checkpoint (a `dbSeq` that was durably saved but never successfully attested, §3.6.1) does NOT cause a false-positive `RollbackDetectedError` on a LATER restore against the checkpoint that eventually WAS attested.
- **`formatMetadataCommit` tamper-evidence (v7, Priorities 2+3, REPLACES v6's `manifestHash` tamper-evidence test):** unit test that a manifest whose unencrypted `envelopeVersion` or `encodingVersion` metadata has been altered (chunk bytes/hashes, `encKdfVersion`, `manifestSectionChunkCount` unchanged) causes `computeFormatMetadataCommit` to diverge from the value folded into the on-chain `commitment`, and that `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` rejects with `RollbackDetectedError` at the *existing* `record.commitment !== expectedCommitment` check — for a v2 anchored checkpoint with a real attestation. A companion test with NO attestation present (verificationLevel stays `"L0+L1"`) confirms the same tampering is **not** caught (an honest disclosure of the residual, not a claim the check applies universally). A **second** companion test confirms `encKdfVersion`/`manifestSectionChunkCount` tampering is caught **without** any chain check at all — the decrypt attempt itself throws (`ChunkIntegrityError`/GCM authentication failure), verifying the "self-detecting, no explicit mechanism needed" argument for those two fields directly, not merely asserting it in prose.
- **`formatMetadataCommit` privacy — no fingerprinting (v7, Priority 2, new, the direct regression test for the round-6 privacy leak):** test that computes `formatMetadataCommit` for N simulated wallets all on the same client-software version (same `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`) and confirms they are all **byte-identical** — i.e. a hosted DB recomputing this value locally cannot distinguish one wallet's blob from another's on the same software version, closing the fingerprinting concern directly rather than asserting it. A companion test confirms `commitment` itself (which additionally folds in `snapshotRoot` and `salt`) remains genuinely unique per wallet, so the fix does not weaken the wallet-identity-hiding property `commitment` already provided.
- **Re-encryption invariance under key rotation (v7, Priority 3, new, the direct regression test for the round-6 key-rotation break):** test that re-encrypts an already-attested checkpoint's ciphertext under a new `encKdfVersion`/`deviceId` (simulating a key-rotation or re-encryption pass), confirms `manifestHash` (Domain S, local-only) changes as expected, and confirms `formatMetadataCommit`/`commitment`/`attestLeaf` for that checkpoint are **byte-identical** before and after — i.e. the historical attestation remains valid for the re-encrypted blob without any new `attest()` call.
