This must **FAIL** against v6's implementation (which folded the full `manifestHash`, including `encKdfVersion`, into `attestLeaf`) and **PASS** against v7's.
- **`manifestSectionChunkCount` boundary (new in v6, Priority 3, unaffected by the v7 redesign — this field's protection mechanism changed, the field itself and this test did not):** unit/integration test that a decoder given only the manifest's unencrypted metadata (no decryption performed yet) can correctly identify exactly which leading chunk indices belong to `manifestSectionPlain` using `manifestSectionChunkCount` alone, across manifests where that section spans 1, 2, and >2 chunks — regression test for the "structurally first identifies the start but not the end" gap.
- **Section-length padding, finalized byte-exactly in v7 (Priority 6):** property test that two checkpoints with `ownedNotesPlain` sets of different sizes falling in the *same* power-of-two chunk bucket (minimum bucket size 2 chunks) produce **identical** chunk counts for that section, while sets falling in *different* buckets remain distinguishable only down to the bucket boundary, never the exact count; a companion test confirms the decoder correctly strips padding via the section's self-declared `trueLength` and recovers the exact original plaintext; a **new v7 companion test** confirms canonical-padding validation actually rejects a section whose padding bytes are not all `0x00` (`NonCanonicalPaddingError`), and that a genuinely empty section (`trueLength = 0`) still pads to the 2-chunk minimum rather than 0 chunks.
- **Device A/B `dbSeq`-regression race (new in v6, Priority 4) — the direct regression test for the false-rollback-rejection bug:** integration test reproducing §12 D14's traced scenario — Device A saves a fresher checkpoint (`height = 500`) but attests slowly; Device B saves a slightly staler checkpoint (`height = 480`, but a numerically *higher* `dbSeq` than A's, since B saved *after* A) and attests quickly, landing first. Confirm: (a) both attestations land on-chain successfully (the contract's height-only CAS does not reject either); (b) a device whose local high-water mark was set from B's attestation, upon later restoring against A's now-canonical (higher-height) attestation, does **NOT** throw a false-positive rollback error, because the v6 high-water-mark check compares `height` (500 > B's 480, correctly recognized as forward progress), not `dbSeq` (100 < B's 101, which the pre-v6 check would have wrongly rejected). This must **FAIL** (incorrectly reject A's legitimate, freshest attestation) against a `dbSeq`-keyed high-water-mark check, and **PASS** against v6's `height`-keyed one.
- **`HorizonTuple` completeness (new in v3, item 5):** type-level/unit test that both `checkpoint` and `tip` horizons expose `R_N` and `endIndex`, and that L1's tail-check and L0's on-chain-agreement check each consume the correct one of the two (not silently swapped).
- **L1 lower-bound inflation (new in v4, Priority 5):** unit test that an envelope whose `anchor.zswapEndIndex`/`anchor.blockHeight` do not match `checkpointHorizon.endIndex`/`checkpointHorizon.blockHeight` (a hostile envelope inflating the tail's claimed lower bound to shrink or empty the L1 scan range) is rejected with `SnapshotAnchorMismatchError` before `verifyTailComplete` ever runs — regression test for the missing check GPT-5.6 Sol found.
- **Nonce-reuse-under-abort (new in v4, Priority 2; construction superseded in v5, Priority 2 — DB-side sequence replaced by client-side local counter) — the direct regression test for the round-3 CRITICAL finding, updated for the round-5 fix:** integration test that (a) begins a `save()` (the client has already durably fsynced `localCounter`'s incremented value BEFORE this point, per §7.3.1), (b) forces the Postgres transaction to abort *after* chunk rows have been inserted but *before* commit (e.g. inject a failure in the manifest-insert step), (c) confirms `ckpt_sequence_counters`'s row for that `(walletId, networkId)` rolled back to its pre-attempt value (still gapless, unaffected by this fix) while the client's own local-store `localCounter` value remains at its already-fsynced, post-increment value (Postgres's rollback has no effect on it, since it was never inside that transaction), and (d) retries `save()` for different plaintext and confirms the resulting nonces share no `(localCounter, chunkIndex)` pair with the aborted attempt's, under the same device key. This must FAIL against v3's `uint64(seq)||uint32(chunkIndex)` construction (seq rolls back and is reallocated identically) and against v4's `ckpt_nonce_ctr` construction under a simulated Postgres-crash-before-sequence-flush (the honest-Postgres counterexample GPT-5.6 Sol cited in round 5), and PASS against v5/v6's client-side construction in both cases, since Postgres's own crash/rollback semantics no longer participate in nonce generation at all.
- **Real-envelope-version dispatch (new in v4, Priority 8):** unit test that a well-formed `envelopeVersion: 1` envelope (the actual shape `src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts` produces today) routes to `restoreLegacyUnverified()`, never to `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint()` and never throws `SnapshotEnvelopeUnverifiableError` — regression test against v3's incorrect "legacy = no version field" definition, which this exact envelope would have failed under.
- **L3 absence is not treated as cryptographic proof (new in v4, Priority 4):** unit/integration test confirming that a restore reaching `verificationLevel: "L0+L1"` via `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s absent branch carries the `"L3-absence-is-federated-not-cryptographic"` residual string, and a companion test confirming the k-of-n cross-indexer absence check is actually invoked (not skipped) before that branch is taken.

### 11.2 Integration tests (against a real `midnight-node` + indexer, testcontainers)
- End-to-end `serialize → CheckpointStore.save → load → restoreAnchoredCheckpoint → start` on a live devnet, extending the existing `serializationAndRestoration.integration.test.ts` two-step restore-then-start flow (brief 04 §1); assert the returned `verificationLevel` is exactly `"L0+L1+L3"` for a properly-attested checkpoint.
- **Envelope fail-closure (item 2; corrected in v5, Priority 5a, stale-test fix):** a hand-fabricated envelope claiming `envelopeVersion: 2` but omitting `anchor` must throw `SnapshotEnvelopeUnverifiableError` from `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`, never fall through to an unverified `startFirst`; a genuinely **legacy `envelopeVersion === 1`** envelope (the real, currently-shipping shape — NOT "no `envelopeVersion` field," which v3's text incorrectly used here and v4 already corrected everywhere else, §7.1(a)/(d) Priority 8) must route only through `restoreLegacyUnverified` and never produce a `verificationLevel`; a companion test confirms an envelope with a genuinely missing/non-numeric `envelopeVersion` is now correctly rejected as malformed (`EnvelopeCorruptError`/`EnvelopeVersionUnsupportedError`), never silently routed to the legacy path.
- **Coupled finality tuple (item 9):** integration test with a mock endpoint that serves a genuinely-finalized-but-different block's justification alongside the target block's state-read-proof — `verifyFinalizedTuple` must reject, proving the coupling actually holds and isn't just two calls that happen to agree in the happy path.
- Indexer `TreeAnchor` resolver and `unshieldedUtxos` proof woven into `native_e2e.rs` byte-identical reference stream (brief 04 §5); schema-introspection smoke test must not trip on the new fields.
- Tier-1 finality: verify `grandpa_proveFinality(N)` + `state_getReadProof` against a real node, including an authority-set-change spanning warp-sync fragment (brief 10 §1-3).
- **AES-GCM (§7.3.1, items 10/7; nonce construction updated in v5, Priority 5c, and again in v6, Priority 1; format-metadata test revised in v7, Priorities 2+3):** round-trip encrypt/decrypt through the real `CheckpointStore`; nonce-uniqueness property test across a large save volume for one wallet **under a single `deviceId`'s key**, confirming no `(localCounter, chunkIndex)` pair repeats — the intra-device, deterministic half of §7.3.1's argument; a **separate** property test across multiple simulated `deviceId`s confirms each derives a **distinct key** (`key_device` differs whenever `deviceId` differs) — the v6 replacement for v5's cross-device nonce-uniqueness test, since uniqueness across devices is now a key-separation property, not a shared-nonce-space property (§7.3.1's corrected math); **confirm `manifestHash`'s *chunk-hash-list* component (Domain S, local-only) changes across a key-rotation re-save of identical plaintext, while `snapshotRoot`/attested `commitment`/`attestLeaf` do NOT change (v7: this now includes `formatMetadataCommit`'s two inputs, `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`, which are re-encryption-invariant by construction — REPLACES v6's version of this assertion, which incorrectly expected the extended `manifestHash`, including `encKdfVersion`, to be part of what stays invariant; `encKdfVersion` changing on rotation is correct and expected, and is exactly why it was excluded from `formatMetadataCommit`, per §7.3.1's self-detecting-vs-needs-protection analysis)**; confirm two different `save()` calls of byte-identical plaintext for the same wallet produce **different** ciphertext; confirm AAD tampering (swapped `chunkIndex`, wrong `sectionId`) fails GCM authentication; confirm `encKdfVersion` tampering fails GCM authentication via the wrong-key path, not via any chain-facing check (v7 — replaces v6's "covered by the manifest-header authentication test" framing, since that mechanism no longer exists); confirm `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` tampering is caught by the `formatMetadataCommit`-vs-`commitment` check (§11.1); confirm a simulated local-store crash between `localCounter` fsync and chunk `INSERT` never causes the RETRIED attempt to reuse the reserved `localCounter` value — the honest-Postgres-crash-recovery regression test, updated in v6 only in that the reused value is now `localCounter` (not v5's `nonceBase`, which no longer exists as a distinct concept).
- **Authenticated L3 lookup, present-vs-absent (new in v3, item 1; absent-case description corrected in v5, Priority 5b, stale-test fix):** integration test with a mock endpoint that serves a stale-but-genuinely-finalized old checkpoint block alongside an unauthenticated (non-read-proof-backed) attestation record — `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation` must reject the record as unauthenticated rather than accept it; a companion test confirms that a **Tier-0 k-of-n cross-indexer agreement that `id` is absent** at the fresh tip height (NOT "a state-read-proof correctly proving non-membership" — no such cryptographic primitive exists in v1, §7.1(b)/§10 item 9, Priority 4; this test's prior wording overclaimed a mechanism this design does not have) produces `probe.present === false` (the only case still allowed to downgrade silently to `"L0+L1"`, and only after the k-of-n cross-check genuinely ran, per the companion test in §11.1), while a state-read-proof for a *present-but-mismatched* record throws `RollbackDetectedError`, never downgrades silently.
- **L1 tail check non-triviality (new in v3, item 6):** integration test asserting `checkpointHorizon.endIndex !== tipHorizon.endIndex` in the normal case (i.e. the tip has actually advanced past the checkpoint), and that `verifyTailComplete` is invoked with a genuinely non-empty range — regression test for the v2 no-op bug.
- **Legacy pre-restore probe (new in v3, item 11):** integration test where a wallet with a real on-chain attestation is served an anchor-less (legacy-shaped) envelope; `restoreLegacyUnverified(serialized, conn, identity)` must throw `LegacyRestoreRefusedError` rather than silently restoring unverified; a companion test confirms `restoreLegacyUnverified(serialized)` (no `conn`/`identity`) still proceeds unverified, documenting the named residual for that sub-case.

### 11.3 Real-preprod exercise
- Restore a wallet from an UmbraDB snapshot taken at a **finalized** preprod checkpoint N, verify the anchor against preprod's committed `zswapMerkleTreeRoot`, catch up `[N, tip]` live, and confirm balance parity with a from-genesis replay control. (Note the memory-file caveat: our own preprod experience shows the installed wallet-SDK API can differ from in-tree tooling — pin versions.)
- Dust anchor exercised separately and flagged: dust roots are `@beta`, Tier-F-lite, and **not** node-cross-checked (brief 04 §3) — assert the softer trust posture explicitly, and assert the SDK never labels a dust-only restore `"L0+L1+L3"` without the dust caveat surfaced.

### 11.4 Failure / recovery (cold-boot — the core scenario, plus the post-activation scenario new in v2)
- **Cold-boot from zero local state:** wipe all local wallet memory, restore purely from UmbraDB, confirm `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` reconstructs correct state; confirm that *without* the L3 on-chain attestation a rolled-back snapshot is undetectable, and *with* it the cold-booted wallet detects the rollback via the chain pointer (the argument in §3 — this is the test that justifies L3 being v1).
- **Post-activation rollback discovery (§3.6, new in v2):** resume from a stale-but-genuine snapshot with no attestation check available at restore time (or one that passed because it was the honestly-latest state at that moment), advance to `active`, then have a sibling device (or the test harness) advance the on-chain pointer past what this device's active state descends from; confirm the periodic recheck (or the mandatory pre-spend recheck, tested separately) transitions the wallet to `quarantined`, freezes outbound operations, and completes the §3.6 recovery sequence without data loss beyond the documented residual.
- **Pre-spend recheck (§3.6):** confirm a spend attempted immediately after an off-band pointer advance is blocked by the mandatory pre-spend recheck, not merely by the periodic one (tests the stricter of the two triggers independently).
- Corrupted chunk / manifest → `ChunkIntegrityError`/`ManifestCorruptError` surfaces and restore falls back to replay (never bricks — brief 05 §8).
- Partial/interrupted `save` (AbortSignal) → no half-written manifest; monotonic `seq` unbroken.

### 11.5 Adversarial tests (each maps to a threat in brief 05 §3)
- **Omission (A1/completeness):** malicious indexer stub that (a) omits a *committed* leaf → L1 root check must catch; (b) downgrades a ciphertext to `None` → must be caught only by NxN cross-indexer disagreement, and the test **documents** it is NOT caught by the single-indexer root check nor by L0/L1 (the honest, unified §5.0/§5 residual).
- **Rollback (A2):** DB serves an old-but-genuine snapshot → L3 CAS pointer rejects for a cold-booted wallet; L2 monotonic rejects for a running wallet; §3.6's periodic/pre-spend recheck rejects for an already-`active` wallet that missed the initial detection.
- **Cross-wallet swap (A3):** hosted multi-tenant DB serves another tenant's genuine attested snapshot → fails the per-wallet salt/id commitment check.
- **Attestation forgery (A4):** plant an on-chain attestation for an attacker-chosen hash → fails without `sk_attest`.
- **Envelope fabrication (new in v2, item 2):** a freshly fabricated envelope with no `anchor` (mimicking either a legacy snapshot or an attacker's attempt to skip verification) is proven to be structurally incapable of producing a `verificationLevel` result via any code path.
- **Successor/vk substitution (new in v2, item 4):** an attestation record referencing a different `statementVersion`/contract than the pinned client config is rejected outright, even if otherwise well-formed — proving v1's immutability commitment is enforced, not just documented.
- **Tag-collision (§6 overlay):** two addresses producing colliding detection tags → confirm the wallet still trial-decrypts correctly and no false-negative note loss; confirm a malicious indexer omitting a *tag* is bounded by NxN (the §6 residual).
- **Split-view / equivocation (multi-device):** DB shows different snapshots to two devices → each device's independent anchor check accepts only chain-correct states; BFT-CRDT hash chain detects the horizontal divergence **only once the devices actually exchange histories or check the shared L3 pointer** (item 11) — a companion test with communication permanently withheld documents the divergence going undetected, as an honest residual rather than a silent gap.
- **Owned-note-set substitution (new in v3, item 0; sharpened in v4, Priority 1, to the EXACT GPT-5.6 Sol scenario):** a hostile DB serves an otherwise-valid envelope with a substituted/tampered `sections.ownedNotesPlain` (e.g. an extra note, or the true owner's notes replaced by an attacker's) while keeping cursor/nullifiers/tree-root/dust/manifest identical **and** setting `envelope.snapshotRootHint` to the genuine, honestly-attested `snapshotRoot` string (i.e. the exact string that WOULD pass v3's defective check) → `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` must recompute `snapshotRoot` from `sections` (never trust `snapshotRootHint`), the recomputed value must diverge from what the honest hint claims, the derived `expectedCommitment` must diverge from the on-chain `commitment`, and the function must reject with `RollbackDetectedError` at the L3 step — and, separately, must never return a `Wallet` constructed from the tampered `sections` under any verification level. This is the adversarial-side companion to the 11.1 property test and is the literal reproduction of the round-3 audit's concrete exploit; it must FAIL (i.e. incorrectly succeed) against v3's implementation and PASS (i.e. correctly reject) against v4's.
- **Present-but-mismatched attestation (new in v3, item 1; field name updated in v5, Priority 4):** DB serves a genuine, present on-chain attestation record for this wallet's `id` that does not match the served envelope (wrong `commitment`, wrong `attestLeaf` fields, or wrong `dbSeq`) → must throw `RollbackDetectedError`, never silently downgrade to `"L0+L1"`; a companion test with a genuinely-absent record (first-ever attestation) confirms that case alone still downgrades quietly, proving the two paths are actually distinguished, not just documented as distinguished.

### 11.6 Claim-to-test matrix (the correctness gate)
The correctness-audit spec gate must confirm each design claim has a falsifying test before implementation: (C1) offline recompute = on-chain root → 11.1 collapse-invariant + 11.3; (C2) tail scan verifiably complete (tree-level, per §5.0's scoping) → 11.1 L1 + 11.5 omission; (C3) rollback detectable on cold-boot AND post-activation → 11.4 + 11.5 A2; (C4) finality verifiable not assumed, as one coupled tuple → 11.2 Tier-1 + coupled-tuple test; (C5) remote DB is availability-only for the consensus-reduced (shielded) tier, and Tier-F/Tier-F-lite federated-quorum (not consensus-reduced) for unshielded and dust respectively (§2.6, v4 straggler fix — this line previously and incorrectly bundled dust into the "(shielded/dust)" consensus-reduced parenthetical while simultaneously listing it under federated-quorum) → 11.5 A1-A4; (C6) completeness residual is exactly the unified ciphertext-delivery/wallet-identity-binding gap of §5.0 + spend-hiding → 11.5 omission documents the non-caught cases; (C7, new) the Domain P/Domain S separation holds under key rotation → 11.1 canonical-equation test; (C8, new; narrowed in v5, Priority 5d, stale-test fix) the **contract-address and `statementVersion`** pins are enforced, not advisory (`attestCircuitVkHash` is config-only, not chain-checked, per §10 item 4 — this line previously overclaimed "the vk/contract pin is enforced" as though `attestCircuitVkHash` were included) → 11.5 successor-substitution test; **(C9, new in v3)** `snapshotRoot` binds the owned-note set (a substitution changes the root) → 11.1 owned-notes-binding property test + 11.5 owned-note-set substitution; **(C10, new in v3)** a present-but-mismatched L3 record hard-fails distinctly from a genuinely-absent one → 11.2 authenticated-lookup test + 11.5 present-but-mismatched test; **(C11, new in v3)** the L1 tail check is non-trivial in the normal case → 11.2 L1 tail non-triviality test; **(C12, new in v4)** the restore predicate recomputes `snapshotRoot` from decoded plaintext and constructs the wallet from that same object, rather than trusting a transported field → 11.1 recompute-regression test + 11.5 owned-note-set substitution (exact-exploit form); **(C13, new in v4)** the AES-GCM nonce cannot repeat even under an aborted/retried `save()` → 11.2 nonce-reuse-under-abort test; **(C14, new in v4)** L3 absence is never presented as cryptographically proven → 11.1 absence-is-not-proof test; **(C15, new in v5)** `computeSnapshotRoot` always reads the checkpoint-N frontier and is never affected by anything L1's tail verification does, for a restore with a genuinely non-empty `[N, tip]` tail → 11.1 sections-mutation regression test (below) + the §7.1(b) traced walkthrough; **(C16, new in v5)** the AES-GCM nonce cannot repeat even under an honest Postgres crash/restart with no DB involvement in nonce generation at all → 11.2 AES-GCM local-store-crash test; **(C17, new in v5)** per-chunk AAD is always computable without first decrypting anything (no circular dependency) and `sectionId` is always well-defined for every chunk (no straddling) → 11.2 AES-GCM AAD-bootstrap test (below); **(C18, new in v5)** an orphaned checkpoint (save succeeded, attest never did) never causes a false-positive `RollbackDetectedError` against a later, successfully-attested checkpoint → 11.1 `record.dbSeq`/`candidateSeq` unification companion test. **(C19, new in v6)** the AES-GCM construction's actual collision probability, correctly compared against the NIST `≤2⁻³²` bound, is negligible for the per-device-key construction (not merely for a re-tuned version of the shared-key one) → §7.3.1's recomputed math + 11.2 nonce-uniqueness test, updated for per-device keys. **(C20, new in v6)** a local-store restore-from-backup that regresses `localCounter` is detected and redraws `deviceId` before any further encryption → 11.1/11.2 local-store-restore test (below). **(C21, new in v6)** `sections.treeFrontierAtN` cannot be mutated even by a caller that tries, not merely "isn't mutated by the current implementation" → 11.1 `FrozenFrontier` structural-enforcement test (below). **(C22, new in v6)** `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` returns a fully checkpoint-N-scoped wallet at every `verificationLevel`, never a mixed-time object → 11.1 wallet-construction-scope test (below) + the §7.1(b) traced walkthrough. **(C23, new in v6; REVISED in v7, Priorities 2+3)** the format-dispatch fields (`envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`) genuinely needing chain-facing protection are tamper-evident via `formatMetadataCommit`, folded into `commitment` — REPLACES v6's claim that the full `manifestHash` is chain-authenticated via a disclosed `attestLeaf` field (that mechanism is removed in v7) → 11.1 `formatMetadataCommit` tamper-evidence test (below). **(C24, new in v6)** the local anti-rollback high-water mark is never regressed by an honest `dbSeq`/attestation-arrival-order divergence across devices → 11.1 Device A/B race test (below). **(C25, new in v7)** the local-store-restore beacon detects the exact round-6 counterexample (primary regressed to an earlier `localCounter` while a static-identity beacon would show no change) → §7.3.1's traced counterexample + 11.1/11.2 local-store-restore test (below, revised). **(C26, new in v7)** `formatMetadataCommit` carries negligible fingerprinting power (byte-identical across wallets on the same client-software version) → 11.1 `formatMetadataCommit` privacy test (below). **(C27, new in v7)** `commitment`/`attestLeaf` for an already-attested checkpoint are invariant under re-encryption (key rotation, `deviceId` change, `encKdfVersion` change) → 11.1 re-encryption invariance test (below). **(C28, new in v7)** a historical `AttestRecord` retrieved via `fetchHistoricalAttestation` is only accepted if it both self-hashes to `attestLeaf` and verifies via Merkle inclusion against the chain-read `history` root — a lying or unavailable indexer cannot forge acceptance → 11.2 historical-restore test (below).

- **`treeFrontierAtN` never mutated (new in v5, Priority 1; structural-enforcement companion added in v6, Priority 2) — the direct regression test for the sections-mutation defect GPT-5.6 Sol found in round 5:** unit test that calls `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` against an envelope with a genuinely non-empty `[N, tip]` tail (i.e. `tipHorizon.endIndex > anchor.zswapEndIndex`) and confirms (a) the restore succeeds with `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"` for an honestly-attested checkpoint, and (b) `sections.treeFrontierAtN.bytes` (captured before `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` is called) is byte-identical before and after the call returns. **New companion test (v6, C21):** construct a `FrozenFrontier` and have a deliberately-adversarial test double for `verifyTailComplete` attempt to mutate the `Uint8Array` it receives from `.bytes` in place (`arr[0] = 0xFF`) — confirm this mutation has **zero effect** on subsequent reads of `sections.treeFrontierAtN.bytes`, proving the enforcement is structural (a defensive copy was mutated, not the canonical stored bytes), not merely "the current call graph happens not to attempt a mutation."
- **AAD bootstrap / no circular dependency (new in v5, Priority 3):** integration test that decrypts a full checkpoint using ONLY (a) the manifest's own unencrypted metadata (`envelopeVersion`, `encodingVersion`, `encKdfVersion`, per-chunk `chunkIndex`/`chunkCount` from the chunk-hash list) and (b) the fixed `sectionId = 0` bootstrap constant for `manifestSectionPlain`'s own chunk(s) — confirming decryption never requires having already decrypted anything else first; a companion test constructs a deliberately section-straddling chunk boundary and confirms the *encoder* rejects it at encode time (chunking must be section-aligned by construction, not merely by convention).
- **Wallet-construction scope (new in v6, Priority 2, C22) — the direct regression test for the mixed-time-wallet defect:** unit test that calls `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` against an envelope with a genuinely non-empty `[N, tip]` tail and confirms the returned `wallet`'s frontier is byte-identical to `sections.treeFrontierAtN` (i.e. still N-scoped, 5,000 leaves in the §7.1(b) trace's numbers) — **not** tip-advanced. This must FAIL (incorrectly return a tip-advanced 5,400-leaf frontier) against v5's implementation and PASS against v6's. A companion test confirms the wallet returned at `verificationLevel: "L0+L1"` (no attestation available) and the wallet returned at `"L0+L1+L3"` (attestation available, same underlying checkpoint) have byte-identical frontiers — proving `verificationLevel` no longer changes *what* is returned, only how much of it has been independently checked, closing the "L3-reaching restores get a subtly different contract" gap.
- **Local-store-restore-from-backup detection (REVISED in v7, Priority 1, C25 — the direct regression test for round 6's own concrete counterexample, which v6's original version of this test did NOT actually reproduce):** integration test that (a) initializes a fresh local store (beacon + primary both created, matching `{deviceId, counter: 0}`), (b) performs several saves, advancing `counter` well past 0 (e.g. to 100) — **critically, each of these saves durably mirrors `counter` into the beacon too, per the v7 protocol**, (c) simulates an OS/cloud backup-and-restore by snapshotting the *primary* store's state at `counter = 100`, continuing to perform 150 further genuine saves (advancing `counter`, and the beacon mirror, to 250), then restoring the *primary* store back to the `counter = 100` snapshot while leaving the beacon untouched at 250 (reproducing the exact round-6 counterexample — a static-identity-only beacon would show no change here, since `deviceId` is unchanged; the v7 magnitude check is what must catch it), and (d) confirms the next `save()` attempt detects `beaconVal(250) > primaryVal(100)`, throws `BackupRestoreDetected` **before any reservation completes**, redraws a fresh `deviceId`, resets `counter` to 0, and that the resulting nonce/key material shares no `(nonce, key)` pair with anything encrypted under the old `deviceId`. **This must FAIL (incorrectly proceed with `counter = 101`, reusing a consumed value) against v6's `storeInstanceId`-equality check, since v6's beacon never recorded the 150 intervening saves, and PASS against v7's mirrored-counter check.** A companion test confirms a *genuinely fresh install* (both primary store and beacon absent) does **not** spuriously trigger the redraw path. Two **new v7 companion tests** cover the previously-unspecified state-machine cases: (i) primary absent, beacon present (e.g. simulating an iOS reinstall where Keychain survives) → confirms a fresh `deviceId`/`counter := 0` redraw, never a resumption from the beacon's stale counter; (ii) primary present at `counter == 0` with an absent or mismatched beacon → confirms the beacon is simply reconciled to match the primary (no redraw), since zero encryptions have occurred under this `deviceId`.
- **Crash-window safety of the dual-write reservation protocol (new in v7, Priority 1):** integration test that injects a crash/process-kill between the primary-counter durable write and the beacon-mirror durable write (both possible orderings around the injection point) and confirms, in every case, (a) no ciphertext was produced under the reserved-but-unmirrored counter value, and (b) the very next reservation attempt on retry either completes the interrupted mirror (if primary is durably ahead) or proceeds normally (if the crash was before any durable change) — never reserves-and-consumes a value the beacon has not durably witnessed. A companion test confirms a beacon-write fsync failure (with the primary write having already succeeded) causes the `save()` attempt to abort outright (per the extended MUST rule), not proceed to encrypt.
- **Concurrent-save counter contention (new in v6, Priority 1; lock scope extended in v7 to cover primary+beacon as one critical section) — the direct regression test for the round's "actual protocol, not an assumption" ask:** integration test that fires N concurrent `save()` calls (simulating multiple processes/tabs on one device racing) against the same local store and confirms (a) every resulting `counter` value is unique (the lock genuinely serialized the full reserve-then-fsync-both-locations step, no two callers observed the same pre-increment value), and (b) the resulting ciphertext chunks pairwise share no `(nonce, key)` collision. A companion test confirms a fsync failure injected mid-reservation (either the primary write or the beacon write) causes the corresponding `save()` attempt to abort outright (per the extended MUST rule) rather than proceeding to encrypt with an unpersisted or unmirrored counter value.
- **Historical restore, real inclusion proof (new in v7, Priority 5, C28):** integration test that calls `restoreAtHistoricalCheckpoint(targetHeight, ...)` against a wallet with multiple historical attestations and confirms it returns the correct (latest-at-or-before-`targetHeight`) record, verified against a real chain-read `history` root. A companion **adversarial** test has a mock indexer return (a) a record whose fields don't self-hash to the claimed `attestLeaf` — must reject before ever checking the inclusion path; (b) a self-consistent record with a forged/absent inclusion path — must reject with `HistoricalRecordNotIncludedError`; confirming a lying or unavailable indexer cannot forge acceptance of a historical restore. A third test confirms the checkpoint-retention residual is surfaced distinctly (`CheckpointNotFoundError`, not confused with an inclusion-proof failure) when the attestation itself verifies but the underlying blob has been pruned.

---

## 12. Open decisions for the design council to ratify

**D0 (new, blocking) — canonical versioned snapshot-section encoding (CBOR/CDDL), promoted from the v1 draft's "secondary" list.** Ratify §2.5.4: without a byte-exact canonical encoding per plaintext section, `snapshotRoot` (§2.5.2) is not well-defined and every downstream equality check is unsound. This must land before any V2 implementation work, not alongside or after it.

**D1 (top) — L3 primary = the Compact Attested Manifest Root, and it is v1, not optional, for the remote case.** Ratify that a cold-booted wallet restoring from an untrusted DB genuinely needs a consensus-held monotonic pointer (§3), so the on-chain attestation ships in v1 for remote/hosted deployments (optional only for purely-local single-writer). Ratify V1b+V2 shape with `prevCommitment` from day one, using the canonical attestation equation of §2.5.3 (not the v1 draft's looser, contradictory version). Accept the §1 framing as a written non-goal: we defend against a hostile *DB*, not a wallet compromised *at attest time* (brief 05 Q3, also now §10 item 4) — or the feature over-claims.

**D2 — ship v1 with the documented Zcash-parity completeness residual (§5, precisely scoped per §5.0).** Ratify that ciphertext-delivery + spend-hiding remain open in v1 — understood as the *same* underlying wallet-identity-binding gap identified independently as item 7, not two separate gaps — bounded by NxN + only-spend-own-notes (correctly scoped) + first-spend re-validation (correctly scoped, §5.1), and are closed only by a Midnight node change we will formally request (body-inclusion proof / header ciphertext-accumulator / nullifier accumulator). This is the industry-standard position (brief 09 §8); the alternative is blocking v1 on a protocol change we don't control.

**D3 — privacy-from-scanner: overlay-now vs consensus-later (§6).** Ratify shipping the overlay detection tag as v1.x (privacy win, completeness still bounded), and formally requesting the consensus-emitted clue key (FMD) from Midnight as the principled close of both privacy and ciphertext-delivery completeness. Accept that an overlay tag is itself omittable (brief 09 §10).

**D4 (new) — vk/circuit succession: v1 ships fully immutable, hard-pinned (§3.5, option a).** Ratify that v1 client config hard-pins `contractAddress` + `attestCircuitVkHash` + `attestStatementVersion`, that v1 clients never auto-follow a governance-selected successor, and that this pin is a named §10 residual-trust item rather than an implicit assumption. Ratify the successor-certificate mechanism (§3.5, option b) as the specified, not-yet-built v1.1+ upgrade path, to be re-ratified separately before it ships.

**D5 (new; wording corrected in v5, Priority 6/straggler fix) — unshielded/dust are Tier-F (federated quorum), not consensus-reduced, and must be labeled as such everywhere (§2.6).** Ratify that v1 ships the signed-STH + k-of-n monitor mechanism for unshielded and continues serving `@beta` dust roots, but that "verified"/"trustless" language is reserved for the **consensus-reduced shielded path alone** — dust is Tier-F-lite (§2.6), not consensus-reduced, despite sharing the same ADS mechanism as shielded — and is never applied unqualified to either unshielded or dust. (v5 correction: the prior wording here read "...the consensus-reduced shielded/dust-root path...," bundling dust back into "consensus-reduced" language that §2.6 and every other instance in this document correctly splits out — found independently by Opus and GPT-5.6 Sol in round 5, the one remaining dust-labeling straggler v4's own item-6 grep-and-check pass missed.)

**D6 (new, v3) — `snapshotRoot` binds `ownedNotesPlain`, and the restore-time correctness question is resolved via option (b) + a named (a)-residual for the base (§2.5.5).** Ratify: (1) the canonical `snapshotRoot` equation (§2.5.2) includes a required `ownedNotesPlain` section, closing the round-2-identified defect that the equation didn't actually bind the wallet's owned-note set despite §3's prose claiming it did; (2) the restore-time correctness of that section is established by the live `[N, tip]` catch-up sync independently re-deriving owned notes going forward (option b — no new mechanism, this is §1's existing baseline catch-up), bounding attest-time-honesty reliance (option a) to exactly the base set at N, which is named explicitly as a §10 item-4 sub-residual rather than left implicit. Ratify that this closes *binding* (a substituted/tampered owned-note set changes the root) and is explicitly orthogonal to the pre-existing *completeness* residual (§5/§5.1, unchanged).

**D7 (new, v4, blocking) — the restore predicate must recompute `snapshotRoot` from decoded plaintext and construct the returned wallet from that same decoded object; a transported `snapshotRoot` field is never security-relevant (§7.1(a)/(b), Priority 1).** Ratify that `envelope.snapshotRootHint` (renamed from v3's `snapshotRoot`) is optional, non-authoritative, and used only as a local fast-fail cache; the equality check that actually gates `verificationLevel: "L0+L1+L3"` must compare an on-chain-fetched `commitment` against a value derived exclusively from the same `sections` object the returned `Wallet` is built from. This is the direct, structural fix for a defect found independently in three consecutive design-council rounds; ratifying it as its own numbered decision (rather than folding it into D6, which addressed the *equation*, not the *predicate*) is deliberate, so a future round can verify this specific gap by name.

**D8 (new, v4; SUPERSEDED in v5 — see D11) — AES-GCM nonce material was derived from a dedicated, non-transactional `ckpt_nonce_ctr` Postgres sequence, decoupled from the attested `seq` (§7.3.1, Priorities 2+3).** Round 5's audit (Fable 5 + GPT-5.6 Sol) found this did not actually establish "never reissued, forever" against either a hostile DB or an honest Postgres crash/restart — see D11 below for the replacement decision. Retained here, struck through in effect, for the historical record of what was ratified and then superseded, per this document's own practice of not silently erasing prior decisions.

**D9 (new, v4) — `fetchAuthenticatedAttestation`'s absence case is named, bounded, federated-trust — not claimed as a cryptographic non-membership proof (§7.1(b), §10 item 9, Priority 4).** Ratify shipping v1 with a Tier-0-style k-of-n cross-indexer check for the absent case, explicitly not consensus-reduced, until a real Compact-level Map non-membership primitive is confirmed to exist and is adopted.

**D10 (new, v5, blocking; REVISED in v6, Priority 2) — the root-computation input (`sections.treeFrontierAtN`) must never be mutated by anything, at any point, in `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint`, AND the returned wallet must be fully checkpoint-N-scoped, never a mixed-time object (§7.1(a)/(b), Priorities 1+2).** Ratify: (1) the schema field is named `treeFrontierAtN` to make its "as-of-checkpoint-N" role explicit; (2) **(v6, revised)** its type is `FrozenFrontier`, a defensive-copy-on-read wrapper — "never mutated" is now structurally enforced (no caller, including a future change to `verifyTailComplete`, can mutate the canonical bytes even by trying), not a documentation convention resting on an unenforceable `Schema.Uint8Array`/`readonly` annotation (JS/TS `Object.freeze()` does not prevent writes to a typed array's indexed elements); (3) `computeSnapshotRoot(sections)` runs strictly before any tail-verification step; (4) **(v6, revised, supersedes v5's clause 4)** `verifyTailComplete` is now purely a validation check — it confirms the tail rehashes to the tip root and returns nothing (no `advancedFrontier`); the wallet returned by `restoreAnchoredCheckpoint` is built **directly from unmodified `sections`**, identically at every `verificationLevel`, never from a tip-advanced substitution. **Round 6 found v5's own clause-4 mechanism (returning a wallet built from `{ ...sections, treeFrontier: advancedFrontier }`) introduced a NEW defect — a mixed-time wallet state (checkpoint-N-scoped everywhere except a tip-advanced frontier) inconsistent with this design's own `[N, tip]` live-resume baseline (§1).** Two options were considered: (a) discard the tip-advanced value, returning a fully N-scoped wallet that proceeds through the *same* `[N, tip]` catch-up every restore already requires; (b) specify a new, complete, atomic tail-application mode advancing every wallet component in lockstep. **Ratified: (a)** — it reuses existing mechanism rather than inventing and auditing a second wallet-construction mode, and it makes every restore path converge on an identical post-restore contract regardless of `verificationLevel`. Traced concretely in §7.1(b); the FrozenFrontier fix is likewise a direct, structural fix for a real correctness bug plus a real audit finding (unenforced convention), not merely additional hardening.

**D11 (new, v5, blocking, supersedes D8; REVISED in v6, Priority 1; the local-store-restore clause REVISED AGAIN in v7, Priority 1 — v6's own beacon mechanism found structurally broken, not merely narrow) — AES-GCM nonce material is generated fully client-side, with `deviceId` bound into per-device KEY DERIVATION rather than relied on purely as nonce-space partitioning, never supplied by, derived from, or trusted from the DB in either direction (§7.3.1, Priority 1).** **Round 6 found v5's own probability claim was not merely imprecise but backwards: v5 computed `P(deviceId collision, D=20) ≈ 4.66×10⁻⁸` (arithmetic correct, independently re-verified this session) and asserted this "comfortably clears NIST's ≤2⁻³² guidance" — it does not; `4.66×10⁻⁸ ÷ 2⁻³² ≈ 200`, i.e. v5's own construction's collision probability was ~200× WORSE than the bound it claimed to clear.** Ratify the v6 replacement, clauses (1)–(3) and (5)–(7) unchanged, clause (4) REVISED in v7: (1) each device derives its own AES-GCM key via `HKDF-SHA256(..., info = ... || deviceId)` — `deviceId` bound into key derivation, not merely nonce material, so GCM's nonce-uniqueness requirement (a per-key property) simply does not apply across devices with distinct keys, dissolving the shared-key cross-device collision question structurally rather than re-tuning the same probability target; (2) `deviceId` is widened 32→128 bits and `localCounter` 32→64 bits (hygiene on top of the structural fix, not a substitute for it); (3) the residual cross-device risk (now a *key*-collision bound, requiring an identical 128-bit `deviceId` draw) is recomputed correctly: `P ≈ 5.88×10⁻³⁷` for `D=20` (exact value `5.5836×10⁻³⁷`, v7 Priority 8), roughly **10²⁶ times smaller than** the `2⁻³²` bound — not merely under it; **(4) REVISED in v7: the v6 "liveness beacon" compared a static, generated-once `storeInstanceId` and was found, by an identical concrete counterexample independently constructed by Fable 5 and GPT-5.6 Sol, not to detect the restore-from-backup scenario it exists to catch — a beacon that never records the device's subsequent progress cannot tell "restored to an earlier state" from "still the same device." The v7 replacement mirrors the reserved `localCounter` value itself into the beacon on every reservation, and checks magnitude (`primary.counter >= beacon.counter`) rather than identity — traced through the exact round-6 counterexample in §7.3.1 to confirm it is now blocked. A full crash-safe write-ordering protocol (primary-then-beacon, with a proven-safe reconciliation rule for the interrupted case), an extended MUST-abort rule, the two previously-unspecified state-machine cases (primary-absent/beacon-present; primary-at-counter-0/beacon-mismatched), and an explicit fail-closed rule for platforms with no reliable primitive are all newly specified (§7.3.1). The desktop marker-file gap (does not survive a full-disk-image restore) is closed where a TPM/hardware-backed primitive is available, and named as a narrower residual where it is not; AES-GCM-SIV remains a named, not-built-for-v1 defense-in-depth recommendation for exactly those residuals.** (5) fsync failure during the reserve step is now an explicit MUST-abort condition, extended in v7 to cover the beacon write too; (6) concurrent same-device saves are serialized via an explicit advisory-lock reservation protocol, extended in v7 to scope the full primary+beacon reservation as one atomic step; (7) counter exhaustion gets an explicit, mandatory fail-closed/rekey rule. This closes the hostile-DB framing (Fable 5), the honest-Postgres-crash-recovery framing (GPT-5.6 Sol), and — genuinely, as of v7 — the local-store-restore framing (Opus/Fable 5/GPT-5.6 Sol) simultaneously.

**D12 (new, v5, blocking) — the attestation contract's internal ordering counter and the `CheckpointStore` checkpoint locator are two separately-named, separately-disclosed values, never assumed to coincide implicitly (§2.5.3, §3.6.1, §8, Priority 4).** Ratify: (1) `seq` is split into `attestOrdinal` (purely internal, contract-incremented, salt-randomness role only) and `dbSeq` (a new, explicit, client-disclosed public input to `attest()` naming exactly which checkpoint this attestation is for); (2) an "orphaned checkpoint" (save succeeds, attest never does) is an explicitly named, non-fatal, expected state with a specified retry protocol (§3.6.1), never silently assumed not to happen; (3) `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`'s failure to surface `record.sequence` to its caller (verified directly against source this session) is named as a required, blocking companion implementation fix, not silently assumed already resolved (§10 item 11). **(v6 note: D12 established the `dbSeq`/`attestOrdinal` split; it did not itself claim either was a monotonicity signal — D14 below fixes a separate defect where OTHER parts of this document incorrectly treated `dbSeq` as one.)**

**D13 (new, v6, blocking; REVISED in v7, Priorities 2+3 — v6's own mechanism found to introduce a privacy leak AND a key-rotation break, both closed together) — format-metadata tamper-evidence is achieved without disclosing a ciphertext-fingerprinting value on-chain and without breaking re-encryption invariance; a concrete, unencrypted, pre-decryption chunk-count field closes the `manifestSectionPlain` boundary gap; section-length padding, finalized byte-exactly, closes the per-section count privacy leak (§2.5.2, §2.5.3, §7.3.1, §8, Priorities 2/3/6).** **Round 6's follow-up review (GPT-5.6 Sol) found v6's mechanism (extending `manifestHash` to cover all four of `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion`/`encKdfVersion`/`manifestSectionChunkCount` and disclosing it in `attestLeaf`) broken in two ways: (a) a chunk-hash-covering hash is an effectively unique fingerprint, letting a hosted DB holding the ciphertext manifest correlate its own blob to the on-chain identity — directly contradicting this document's own pre-existing hiding-commitment rationale (§3); (b) the disclosed value changes on every re-encryption (since it covers chunk hashes and `encKdfVersion`), breaking the historically-attested `attestLeaf` for any checkpoint that is later re-encrypted — directly contradicting this document's own pre-existing "re-encryption never invalidates a prior attestation" rule (§2.5.1/§2.5.2), present since v2.** Ratify the v7 replacement: (1) `encKdfVersion` and `manifestSectionChunkCount` are recognized as **already self-detecting** — both feed either key derivation or per-chunk AAD, so tampering either is caught by AES-GCM's own authentication tag on the next decrypt attempt, needing no chain-facing mechanism at all; (2) only `envelopeVersion`/`encodingVersion` — genuinely un-authenticated-by-AAD-or-key-derivation, and genuinely re-encryption-invariant — are folded into a new, small `formatMetadataCommit`, itself folded **inside** the existing hiding `persistentCommit(snapshotRoot, formatMetadataCommit, salt)` construction, never disclosed in the clear and never placed directly in `attestLeaf`; (3) the full, ciphertext-chunk-hash-covering `manifestHash` (Domain S) is removed from `attestLeaf`/`AttestRecord` entirely, reverting to the original rule that it is local-only; (4) `manifestSectionChunkCount` remains a small unencrypted integer naming how many leading chunks belong to `manifestSectionPlain`, protected by its self-detecting AAD role, needing no separate hash; (5) each Domain P section is padded, before chunking, to the next power-of-two chunk-count bucket with an explicit 2-chunk minimum, `0x00` padding, mandatory canonical-padding validation, and a `2³²`-byte per-section maximum (§2.5.4, finalized byte-exactly in v7, Priority 6) — chosen over disclosing the per-section-count leak as accepted residual because owned-note/nullifier counts are financially sensitive and the fix is cheap. This closes both round-6 defects simultaneously (traced through concretely in §2.5.3): the privacy leak, because `formatMetadataCommit` ranges over only a handful of values across an entire user base; the key-rotation break, because neither folded field changes under re-encryption.

**D14 (new, v6, blocking) — `dbSeq` is stripped of any monotonicity/freshness role everywhere in this document and used strictly as a storage locator; `height` (already contract-CAS-enforced) is the sole anti-rollback high-water-mark signal (§7.1(b), §3.6, §8, Priority 4).** **Round 6 found a concrete honest race (GPT-5.6 Sol): Device A saves a fresher checkpoint (`height = 500`) but attests slowly; Device B saves a slightly staler checkpoint (`height = 480`, but a numerically HIGHER `dbSeq` than A's, since B saved after A) and attests quickly, landing first. When A's attestation later lands with `height > B`'s but `dbSeq < B`'s, the contract accepts it (height increased, its only CAS check) and the on-chain pointer's `dbSeq` value moves backward — breaking any check that (incorrectly) used `dbSeq` as a freshness/ordering signal.** Traced through the fix: both A's and B's attestations succeed regardless (the contract's `assert(prev.height < height)` check is unaffected by this decision, since it never examined `dbSeq`); the fix is entirely client-side — `assertSeqNotBelowHighestAccepted(candidateSeq, ...)` and `updateLocalHighWaterMark(record.dbSeq, ...)` (§7.1(b)) and §3.6's pre-spend/periodic/divergence checks are replaced with `height`-keyed equivalents. Re-run against the race: a device whose high-water mark was set from B's attestation (`height=480`) correctly accepts A's later, canonical attestation (`height=500`) as forward progress — no false-positive rollback rejection. **What happens to a genuinely-CAS-rejected ("loser") attestation is unchanged and needed no new mechanism:** if a strictly-staler-by-height attestation is submitted *after* a fresher one has already landed, the contract's existing CAS correctly rejects it; the losing device's checkpoint becomes an "orphaned checkpoint" and is handled by the pre-existing §3.6.1 retry/reconciliation protocol, which was already `height`-oriented and required no change for this fix. Ratify option (b) of the two offered (the alternative, making the contract additionally enforce increasing `dbSeq`, was not adopted — it would require a contract change to enforce a value the contract has no way to independently validate, where the client-side fix requires none).

**D15 (new, v7, blocking) — intentional point-in-time historical restore is a real, specified mechanism, not a named-but-unbuilt future capability (§3.6.2, Priority 5).** Round 6's audit found this document had claimed, since v2, that the on-chain `history` tree "turns intentional point-in-time restore into a verifiable first-class op," while no restore code path through v6 ever consumed the tree for that purpose — only the latest `attestations[id]` record was ever fetched. Two options were on the table: (a) specify the missing mechanism for real, given the tree already exists specifically to enable it; (b) honestly downgrade the claim to a named future capability. **Ratified: (a).** A new indexer capability indexes every `history` insertion by position and by wallet `id`; a new `fetchHistoricalAttestation(id, targetHeight)` retrieval returns the historical `AttestRecord` plus a genuine Merkle inclusion proof against the `history` tree's root, read via the same GRANDPA-justified `state_getReadProof` coupling discipline §4 already uses for every other chain-read value in this design; a new `restoreAtHistoricalCheckpoint()` reuses the existing L0/L1 verification core against the retrieved, chain-verified historical record. This is ordinary Merkle inclusion-proof plumbing, not a new cryptographic primitive — genuinely easier than the still-open non-membership gap named for nullifiers/L3-absence (§10 item 9), which needs a primitive this design has never claimed exists. Named residuals (checkpoint-blob retention, indexer-availability-not-correctness) are disclosed, not hidden (§10 item 14).

**Secondary (flag, not blocking):** finality Tier-0 → Tier-1 sequencing (§4); `R_utxo` anchoring option 2 vs waiting for a consensus utxo-root (brief 06 §4.4); HD path for `sk_attest` and interaction with key rotation (brief 05 Q7); BFT-CRDT device-key membership/revocation and non-commutative merge-rule design (§2 item 11, explicitly deferred, not silently assumed solved); minimum multi-device history-exchange cadence, or reliance on the L3 pointer as a connectivity-free shared head (§2 item 11); whether the node/ledger actually exposes a per-contract deployed-verifier-key-hash read for `assertContractVkPinned` (§7.1(b), item 3) to check against at session start — **v4 (Priority 6): resolved for v1 scope, not left open** — v1 ships assuming no such read exists and enforces the pin structurally only (§7.1(b), §10 item 4); this secondary item now tracks only whether a *future* version should upgrade to a real chain-level check, not whether v1 needs one to ship.

**The biggest risk.** Over-claiming completeness — unchanged from v1, but now backed by the corrected §5.0 claim rather than the retracted one, and by v3's actual owned-notes binding rather than a claim about it that the governing equation didn't yet implement. The design's honesty rests on stating, everywhere "verified" appears, that v1 proves *commitment*-completeness (of the shared, global tree) + *binding* of the attested owned-note set (v3) + inclusion + rollback-resistance (conditional on the residuals in §10) + finality-anchoring (as one coupled tuple), but **not** ciphertext-delivery or spend completeness, **not** correctness of the owned-notes base at N beyond attest-time honesty (v3, §10 item 4), and **not** consensus-reduced trust for the unshielded/dust paths — those need a node change or remain Tier-F by design. A design that quietly implies "fully verified, no trust in the feed" would be wrong in exactly the way brief 06 §2.4 / brief 07 §3.1 / brief 09 §10 warn, and would mislead users into financial decisions against a possibly-under-counted balance. Second-order risk, unchanged: L3-a's hand-written, compiler-un-attested IR + pinned vk is a new trust surface that must be audited before v1.1, or it "verifies" nothing useful (brief 07 §6.3). Third-order risk, new in v2: a compromised or careless client-software update that changes the §3.5 pin is now a named, auditable event rather than an implicit possibility — the mitigation is process (software-update review), not cryptography, and this document does not claim otherwise. Fourth-order risk, new in v3: this round's fix pattern — a prose claim getting ahead of the governing equation that's supposed to enforce it — is exactly what produced the round-2 defect in the first place; future revisions should diff every "the root covers X" prose claim against §2.5.2's actual equation before publishing, not trust that a prior correction of the prose was itself sufficient. **Fifth-order risk, new in v4, and the sharpest version of the same pattern yet:** v3 fixed the *equation* (§2.5.2) and its own §2.5.5 prose *asserted* the restore *predicate* enforced it — but the predicate (§7.1(b)) still didn't, for a full additional round, because nobody diffed the pseudocode itself against the prose describing it. The lesson generalizes past "check the equation": **every claim that code X enforces property Y must be checked against X's actual body, not against a nearby paragraph asserting it does** — a design document's own internal cross-references are not evidence, only a pointer to where the evidence should be verified. v4's fixes were re-verified by tracing the exact exploit each defect enabled through the corrected pseudocode line-by-line (see the accompanying report); future rounds should hold new claims to the same bar rather than trusting this document's own prior self-corrections. **Sixth-order risk, new in v5, one level more subtle still:** v4's own fix for the round-3 defect was itself correct in isolation — recomputing `snapshotRoot` from `sections` and building the wallet from that same object really does block the owned-notes-substitution exploit — but v4 never asked whether anything *else* in the same function, added in the same rewrite, mutated the object in between the two reads. A fix can be locally correct and still break the property it was building on, if a *different* line elsewhere in the same function touches the same shared state first. The lesson generalizes past "diff the pseudocode against the prose" (v4's own fifth-order lesson) to: **when a fix introduces or relies on a specific, shared, mutable object flowing through multiple steps, trace every step that touches that object, in execution order, not just the step the fix itself was about** — v5's §7.1(b) trace-through was written specifically to hold itself to this bar, and future rounds should demand the same trace for any fix touching shared mutable state, not just this document's own self-assessment that it did. **Seventh-order risk, new in v6, a category this document had not yet made explicit: a *quantitative* claim's arithmetic can be independently correct and its conclusion still be wrong, if the comparison the arithmetic feeds is stated backwards.** v5's nonce-collision probability (`4.66×10⁻⁸`) was computed correctly — re-verified independently this round — but the sentence built on top of it ("comfortably clears NIST's ≤2⁻³² guidance") inverted the comparison: the number was ~200× *larger* than the bound, not under it. This is a distinct failure mode from the fifth/sixth-order risks above (which were about code not matching the prose describing it): here the prose and the number agreed with each other, and were both wrong together, because nobody re-derived the ratio between them independently of the sentence asserting what that ratio meant. The lesson: **any claim of the form "X clears/meets/satisfies threshold Y" is itself a separate, checkable arithmetic statement (X compared to Y) and must be verified as its own step — computing X correctly does not make a claim about X's relationship to Y correct, and a future round should not trust this document's own comparison language any more than it trusts its own code/prose consistency claims.** This round's math (§7.3.1) states both the raw values and the explicit ratio against the bound, in both directions, specifically so a future reviewer can check the comparison itself rather than re-deriving it from a qualitative sentence. **Eighth-order risk, new in v7, one level more subtle than the seventh: a fix's own self-description can pass every check the fix's author thought to run, and still fail the one concrete counterexample an independent reviewer constructs.** v6's beacon fix was reviewed and (partially) accepted in its own round — Opus judged it sound-with-minor-gaps — while the SAME mechanism, examined by two other reviewers who each independently built a concrete before/after trace rather than evaluating the mechanism's stated properties in the abstract, was found structurally broken. The lesson: **a mechanism's own design rationale ("compares an identity token, so it detects identity mismatches") can be locally true and still not answer the question that matters ("does it detect the specific scenario in the threat model") — every fix claiming to close a named attack scenario should be checked by tracing that exact scenario through the fix step-by-step, not by confirming the fix does what its own description says it does.** This is precisely why this round's report (and this document's own text, above) traces the round-6 counterexample through the v7 mechanism explicitly, rather than describing the new mechanism's properties and leaving the trace as an exercise for the next round.

---

*Grounding: briefs 01–11 in `design/research/2026-07-21-snapshot-root-of-trust/`; UmbraDB `src/interfaces/checkpoint-store.ts`, `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts` (encryption-status claim verified directly against this file for v2 — item 10; sequence-allocation ordering re-verified directly against `src/postgres/checkpoint-store.ts:139-173` for v3 — item 7, and re-confirmed again for v4 — Priority 3), `src/interfaces/wallet-state-envelope.ts`, `src/postgres/wallet-state-envelope.ts` (real `envelopeVersion`/`ENVELOPE_VERSION` shape verified directly against this file for v4 — Priority 8, via `git grep -n "envelopeVersion" origin/main -- src/`; `PgWalletStateEnvelopeStore.load()`'s discarding of `record.sequence` verified directly against this file for v5 — Priority 4), `Formal/STORAGE_ALGEBRA.md` §6, `design/design.md` (`getOrCreateSalt`/`PgPrivateStateProvider` cross-check for v2); Midnight source cited inline. No Midnight source modified; nothing committed to Midnight. v2 revision responds to a 3-reviewer design-council audit (Claude Fable 5 / Claude Opus / GPT-5.6 Sol via Codex); v3 revision responds to a round-2 audit by the same three reviewers (Fable 5 and GPT-5.6 Sol independently converged on the core owned-notes-binding defect; Opus's no-round-3 verdict included one folded-in item); v4 revision responds to a round-3 audit that came back **unanimous 3/3 NEEDS-ROUND-4** (Fable 5, Opus, and GPT-5.6 Sol all independently re-found the owned-notes-binding defect for a third time; GPT-5.6 Sol additionally found the AES-GCM nonce-reuse vulnerability, the unimplementable seq-allocation timing, the unspecified absence-proof mechanism, the L1 tail-check gaps, and the vk-hash/legacy-version integration bugs fixed above); v5 revision responds to a round-4 audit that came back **2-of-3** (Fable 5 confirmed the core owned-notes defect closed but flagged the v4 nonce fix; Opus judged v4 fully closed; GPT-5.6 Sol found the sections-mutation defect, the sharper honest-Postgres nonce-reuse counterexample, the AAD circular dependency, and the seq/record.seq reconciliation gap fixed above — this branch was also rebased onto current `origin/main` as part of this round, confirmed clean with no conflicts since `origin/main`'s 23 new commits never touch this design document).*
